Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Four Categories of What is Established by Ta'lil
Classifying what can be proven by juridical causation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the four categories of what can be established by ta'lil and identify which category is correctly established by textual indication rather than qiyas.

Core Idea
Causes and conditions of rulings are established by textual indication, not by analogical reasoning.

In usul al-fiqh, we distinguish between what can be established by qiyas and what must be derived directly from texts. The author of Noor al-Anwar introduces a key classification that clarifies this distinction: there are four categories of rulings that can be established by juridical causation (ta'lil), but only one of them – the actual ruling – can be validated through qiyas. The other three – the cause (mu'jib), its attributes, the condition, and its attributes – must be found in the text itself.

Guided Path
1
Understand the legal context of the Quranic verse
The verse commands bringing proof (burhan) for any claim, including in legal reasoning. This establishes the principle that causes and conditions must be textually supported, not mere opinion (ra'y).
The verse is used to reject pure rationalism without textual basis.
2
Identify the four categories mentioned
List the four categories: (1) establishing the mu'jib (cause) or its description, (2) establishing the condition or its description, (3) establishing the ruling or its description, and (4) the fourth category (which is the correct one according to the author).
The fourth category is stated to be the correct one; it will be clarified later in the passage.
3
Recognize that the first two categories are not established by qiyas
The author emphasizes that the cause and condition of a ruling – such as genus being the cause for riba al-nasi'ah – cannot be derived by analogical reasoning. They are established by indication of the text (isharat al-nass).
This is a key Hanafi position: the effective cause must be textually indicated, not inferred by reason alone.
4
Note the example of genus for riba al-nasi'ah
The author explains that genus alone is the cause for the prohibition of credit sales (nasi'ah) because it is derived by textual indication from the rule of riba al-fadl, which combines quantity and genus. The resemblance of excess (shubhat al-fadl) in credit sales triggers the same prohibition via the textual hint.
This example is used to illustrate the first category: establishing the mu'jib.
5
Contrast with the third category which can be established by qiyas
The actual ruling (hukm) can be extended to new cases via qiyas, provided the cause is known from the text. The passage implies that the third category is the legitimate domain of analogical reasoning.
This distinction is crucial for usul: qiyas applies to rulings, not to the discovery of causes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
بيان أقسام ما ثبت بالتعليل
لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَالُوا لَنْ يَدْخُلَ الْجَنَّةَ إِلَّا مَنْ كَانَ هُوداً أَوْ نَصَارَى تِلْكَ أَمَانِيُّهُمْ قُلْ هَاتُوا بُرْهَانَكُمْ إِنْ كُنتُمْ صَادِقِينَ﴾ أمر النبي عليه بطلب الحجة والبرهان على النفي والإثبات جميعًا، هذا ما عندي في حلّ هذا المقام. ولما فرغ عن بيان التعليلات الصحيحة والفاسدة شرع في بيان ما يُؤتى التعليل لأجله صحيحًا وفاسدًا، فقال: بيان أقسام ما ثبت بالتعليل] وجملة ما يُعلل له أربعة إلا أن الصحيح عندنا هو الرابع على ما سيأتي، وقال بعض الشارحين إنه بيان لحكم القياس بعد الفراغ من شرطه وركنه، وهو خطأ فاحش، بل بيان حكمه. الأول: إثبات الموجب أو وصفه أي إثبات أن الموجب للحرمة أو وصفه هذا. والثاني: إثبات الشرط أو وصفه أي إثبات أن شرط الحكم أو وصفه هذا. والثالث إثبات الحكم أو وصفه، أي إثبات أن هذا حكم مشروع أو وصفه. فلا بد ههنا من أمثلة ست، وقد بينها بالترتيب، فقال: كالجنسية لحرمة النسأ، مثال لإثبات الموجب فإثبات أن الجنسية وحدها موجبة لحرمة النَّسأ ممّا لا ينبغي أن يثبت بالرأي والتعليل، وإنما أثبتناه بإشارة النص؛ لأن ربا الفضل لمّا حرم بمجموع القدر والجنس فشبهة الفضل وهي النسيئة ينبغي أن تحرم بشبهة العلّة، أعني الجنس وحده أو القدر وحده. وصفة السوم في زكاة الأنعام مثال لإثبات وصف الموجب، فإن الأنعام موجبة للزكاة، ووصفها وهو السوم مما لا ينبغي أن يُتكلّم فيه ويُثبت بالتعليل، وإنما أثبتناه بقوله عليه: " في خمس من الإبل السائمة شاة"، وعند مالك له: لا تشترط الإسامة لإطلاق لحرمة النساء: فيحرم بيع ثوب هروي بثوب هروي نسيئة. لحرمة النسأ إلخ: فبتعليل القدر والجنس الحرمة ربا الفضل في المنصوص عليه ثبت إثبات الموجب هو الجنس وحده أو القدر وحده لحرمة النَّسأ، وأيضا تعدية حكم النص إلى ما لا نص فيه مما لا ينبغي إلخ لأنه لم يوجد أصل نقيسه عليه. وإنما أثبتناه بإشارة النص والثابت بإشارة النص كالثابت بالنص صراحةً، وقال الإمام الشافعي له: إن الجنس بانفراده ليس بسبب لحرمة النّسأ؛ لأن بالنقدية وعدم النقدية لا يثبت إلا شبهة الفضل، وحقيقة الفضل غير مانعة للبيع وإن اتحد الجنس، حتى جاز بيع ثوب هروي بثوبين هرويين، فَلَأَن لا يمنع شبهة الفضل بالطريق الأولى . فشبهة الفضل أي شبهة الربا، وهو الفضل الخالي عن العوض، فإن في النسيئة شبهة الفضل، وهي الحلول في أحد الجانبين؛ لأن النقد خير من النسيئة. أعني الجنس إلخ فإن الجنس وحده أو القدر وحده شطر العلة ففيه شبهة العلية. مما لا ينبغي إلخ لعدم وجود أصل يقاس عليه. لا تشترط إلخ فيجب الزكاة في الإبل العلوفة. ر تخريجه .
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of the categories of what is established by ta'lil. For His saying: 'And they say none shall enter paradise except one who is Jew or Christian. That is their wishful thinking. Say: bring your proof if you are truthful.' The Prophet commanded to demand proof and evidence for negation and affirmation both. This is what I have in solving this place. When he finished explaining correct and corrupt ta'lils, he began explaining what ta'lil is brought for, correct and corrupt, saying: Explanation of the categories of what is established by ta'lil. The total of what is caused is four except that the correct with us is the fourth as will come. And some commentators said it is an explanation of the ruling of qiyas after finishing its condition and pillar, and that is a manifest error; rather it is an explanation of its ruling. First: establishing the mu'jib or its description, i.e. establishing that the cause of prohibition or its description is this. Second: establishing the condition or its description, i.e. establishing that the condition of the ruling or its description is this. Third: establishing the ruling or its description, i.e. establishing that this is a legislated ruling or its description. There must be six examples here, and he explained them in order, saying: Like jinsiyyah for the prohibition of nasi'ah, example for establishing the mu'jib. So establishing that jins alone is the cause of prohibition of nasi'ah is not proper to be established by opinion and ta'lil; rather we establish it by indication of the text, because when riba al-fadl was prohibited by the combination of quantity and genus, the resemblance of excess which is nasi'ah should be prohibited by the resemblance of the cause, i.e. genus alone or quantity alone. And the description of sa'ima (grazing) in zakat of cattle is an example for establishing the description of the mu'jib. For cattle are cause for zakat, and their description which is sa'ima is not to be spoken about and established by ta'lil; rather we establish it by his saying: 'In five grazing camels, a sheep.' And according to Malik it is not required to be grazing because of the absolute nature of the prohibition of women: thus it is prohibited to sell a Harawi cloth for a Harawi cloth on credit. For the prohibition of nasi'ah etc.: So by the ta'lil of quantity and genus for the prohibition of riba al-fadl in the stated case, the establishment of the mu'jib which is genus alone or quantity alone for the prohibition of nasi'ah is established. Also extending the ruling of the text to what is not stated in the text is not proper etc. because there is no original to which it is analogized. Rather we establish it by indication of the text, and what is established by indication of the text is like what is established by the text explicitly. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: genus alone is not a cause for the prohibition of nasi'ah; because by cash and credit only the resemblance of excess is established, and actual excess does not prevent sale even if genus is one, so that it is permissible to sell one Harawi cloth for two Harawi cloths; so even more should the resemblance of excess not prevent. The resemblance of excess means resemblance of riba, which is excess without compensation, for in nasi'ah there is a resemblance of excess, which is immediate payment in one side; because cash is better than credit. I mean genus etc., for genus alone or quantity alone is half of the cause, so it has a resemblance of causality. Not proper etc. because there is no original to be analogized from. Not required etc., so zakat is due on non-grazing camels? r takhrijuhu.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on the classification of what is established by juridical causation (ta'lil). The author begins by citing the Quranic verse 2:111 to highlight the imperative to bring proof (burhan) for claims. He then notes that after discussing valid and invalid ta'lils, the text turns to the categories of rulings that can be established via ta'lil. He refutes a mistaken view that this section deals with the ruling of qiyas itself; rather, it concerns the subject matter of ta'lil. The primary classification divides into three rejected categories and one accepted category. The first is establishing the cause (mu'jib) or its attribute—this cannot be done by personal opinion but only by textual indication. The example given is the prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah based on genus alone; the text argues that the cause for prohibition is genus, but this is not derived by qiyas but from the explicit texts on riba. The second is establishing the condition of a ruling or its attribute, such as the condition of grazing (sa'ima) for zakat on cattle—this too is established by hadith, not by ra'y. The third is establishing the ruling itself or its attribute, which is the legitimate domain of qiyas. The passage then delves into a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i who denies that genus alone can be a cause for riba al-nasi'ah, arguing that genre alone does not prevent sale unless there is actual excess; the Hanafi response counters by pointing to the implicit 'illa of genus.

Key Terms
التعليل (al-ta'lil): Attribution of a legal ruling to a cause ('illa) via juridical reasoning.
الموجب (al-mu'jib): The direct cause that necessitates a ruling, e.g., the cause of prohibition.
شبهة الفضل (shubhat al-fadl): A resemblance of riba, i.e., an excess in one side of a transaction without compensation, such as in credit sales.
إشارة النص (isharat al-nass): A type of textual indication that implies a ruling without explicit statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, how is the cause (mu'jib) for the prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah established?
A) By qiyas analogy from riba al-fadl
B) By indication of the text (isharat al-nass)
C) By consensus of the Companions
D) By the principle of istihsan

Key Takeaway
Only rulings (the third category) can be extended via qiyas; causes and conditions must come from the text.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
Dispute on Genus as a Cause for Riba al-Nasi'ah
Analyzing the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over the cause of riba al-nasi'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that genus alone is a cause for prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Genus alone is a cause for riba al-nasi'ah by textual indication, not by qiyas, despite the Shafi'i objection.

This lesson delves into a famous dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on the role of genus in riba prohibitions. The Hanafi school holds that genus alone is a sufficient cause to prohibit credit sales (nasi'ah) based on an implicit textual indication (isharat al-nass) from the prohibition of riba al-fadl. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that genus alone does not create prohibition unless actual excess is present. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how each school handles textual indications and the limits of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Review the Hanafi claim
The Hanafi position is that genus (jins) alone is a cause (mu'jib) for the prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah (credit sales). This cause is established by textual indication, not by analogical reasoning.
The cause is not derived from qiyas but from isharat al-nass in the text about riba al-fadl.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that genus alone cannot be a cause because actual excess (haqiqat al-fadl) is not prohibited when genus is the same (e.g., selling one Harawi cloth for two). Therefore, the mere resemblance of excess (shubhat al-fadl) should not prohibit.
The Shafi'i reasoning is based on a comparison: if the greater (actual excess) is not prohibited, the lesser (resemblance) should not be prohibited.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah is based on shubhat al-fadl, not actual excess. The text indicates that genus alone triggers this resemblance, and this indication is from the text (isharat al-nass), not from qiyas. The Hanafi principle: 'What is established by isharat al-nass is like what is established by explicit text.'
The Hanafis rely on the implicit textual indication, not on a strict qiyas from actual excess to resemblance.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: If genus alone is a cause, then selling an item of the same genus on credit (e.g., one Harawi cloth for one Harawi cloth with delayed payment) is prohibited. The Shafi'i view would allow such a sale because without actual excess, it is permissible.
This difference affects real transactions in the marketplace.
5
Appreciate the tarjih within the Hanafi school
The Hanafi school relies on the principle that textual indication (isharat al-nass) is valid and binding. The tarjih is based on the authority of the text itself, as clarified by later Hanafi scholars like al-Marghinani.
The tarjih is not arbitrary; it is based on the method of deriving laws from the Quran and Sunnah.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on the classification of what is established by juridical causation (ta'lil). The author begins by citing the Quranic verse 2:111 to highlight the imperative to bring proof (burhan) for claims. He then notes that after discussing valid and invalid ta'lils, the text turns to the categories of rulings that can be established via ta'lil. He refutes a mistaken view that this section deals with the ruling of qiyas itself; rather, it concerns the subject matter of ta'lil. The primary classification divides into three rejected categories and one accepted category. The first is establishing the cause (mu'jib) or its attribute—this cannot be done by personal opinion but only by textual indication. The example given is the prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah based on genus alone; the text argues that the cause for prohibition is genus, but this is not derived by qiyas but from the explicit texts on riba. The second is establishing the condition of a ruling or its attribute, such as the condition of grazing (sa'ima) for zakat on cattle—this too is established by hadith, not by ra'y. The third is establishing the ruling itself or its attribute, which is the legitimate domain of qiyas. The passage then delves into a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i who denies that genus alone can be a cause for riba al-nasi'ah, arguing that genre alone does not prevent sale unless there is actual excess; the Hanafi response counters by pointing to the implicit 'illa of genus.

Key Terms
التعليل (al-ta'lil): Attribution of a legal ruling to a cause ('illa) via juridical reasoning.
الموجب (al-mu'jib): The direct cause that necessitates a ruling, e.g., the cause of prohibition.
شبهة الفضل (shubhat al-fadl): A resemblance of riba, i.e., an excess in one side of a transaction without compensation, such as in credit sales.
إشارة النص (isharat al-nass): A type of textual indication that implies a ruling without explicit statement.

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute over genus as a cause for riba al-nasi'ah?
A) Hanafis prohibit credit sales of identical items; Shafi'is permit them.
B) Hanafis permit credit sales of identical items; Shafi'is prohibit them.
C) Both schools prohibit credit sales of identical items.
D) Both schools permit credit sales of identical items.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on textual indication (isharat al-nass) to establish causes, a method distinct from qiyas and often contested by other schools.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
15 min
Six Categories of What is Established by Legal Reasoning
Explaining six categories of law established by reasoning with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six categories of rulings established by ta'lil and distinguish which require textual indication versus pure analogy.

Core Idea
Cause, condition, and ruling must be grounded in textual indication, not mere reasoning.

This passage from Noorul Anwar lays a foundational principle in Hanafi usul: while legal reasoning (ta'lil) extends rulings, the core elements—cause, condition, ruling—cannot be invented by opinion. Using six categories and concrete examples, the author shows how each element must be traced back to a textual origin. This lesson will help you navigate the boundary between text-based derivation and analogical extension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six categories
The passage divides into three pairs: proving the cause itself and its description; proving the condition itself and its description; proving the ruling itself and its description. List them from the text.
Categories are: 1) al-mujib (cause), 2) sifat al-mujib (description of cause), 3) al-shart (condition), 4) sifat al-shart (description of condition), 5) al-hukm (ruling), 6) sifat al-hukm (description of ruling).
2
Match each category to its example
The text gives examples: genus for riba (cause), pasturing for zakat (description of cause), witnesses for marriage (condition), uprightness of witnesses (description of condition), odd-numbered prayer (ruling). Confirm each example's category.
The last example (al-batira') is for the ruling itself, not its description, though the passage mentions proving the ruling.
3
Locate the textual basis for each
For each example, find the Quranic verse or hadith cited as the proof. Note that some proofs are explicit (qat'i) and some are indicative (dalala).
Examples: hadith on pasturing, hadith on witnesses, indication from riba text.
4
Recognize madhhab disputes
The passage notes differences with Malik and Shafi'i. Identify the points of disagreement: pasturing condition, witness requirement, uprightness/ masculinity. Understand how each school uses different texts or interpretations.
Malik does not require pasturing; Malik accepts announcement; Shafi'i requires uprightness.
5
Understand the limit of qiyas
The author stresses that these foundational elements cannot be established by ra'y or qiyas; they require textual referral. This is a key Hanafi usul principle.
Analogy can extend rulings but cannot create causes or conditions ex nihilo.

Chapter on Analogy - Explanation of the categories of what is established by reasoning - That which will come later in his statement: 'And its ruling is correctness by predominant opinion,' and this is the explanation of what is established by reasoning. First: Proving the effective cause (mujib) or its description, i.e. proving that this is the cause of prohibition or its description. Second: Proving the condition or its description, i.e. proving that this is the condition of the ruling or its description. Third: Proving the ruling or its description, i.e. proving that this is a legislated ruling or its description. Therefore six examples are necessary here, and he has listed them in order, saying: Like jinsiyyah (genus) for the prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah, an example of proving the cause. So proving that the genus alone is a cause for the prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah is not something that should be established by opinion and reasoning; rather we established it by an indication of the text, because when riba al-fadl was prohibited due to the combination of quantity and genus, the semblance of excess (i.e., credit sale) should be prohibited due to the semblance of the cause, namely the genus alone or quantity alone. And the description of pasturing (sawm) in the zakat of grazing animals is an example of proving the description of the cause. For grazing animals are subject to zakat, and their description (pasturing) is not something that should be discussed and established by reasoning; rather we established it by his statement: 'For five camels pasturing, one sheep.' And according to Malik: the condition of pasturing is not required because of the absolute [text]. And witnesses in marriage are an example of the condition; for witnesses are a condition in marriage, and it is not appropriate to discuss establishing this condition by opinion and reasoning; rather we establish it by his statement: 'No marriage except with witnesses.' And Malik said: witnessing is not required; rather public announcement is required because of his statement: 'Announce the marriage, even with the duff.' And the condition of uprightness and masculinity in them (i.e., the witnesses) is an example of proving the description of the condition. For witnesses are a condition, and uprightness and masculinity are their description, and it is not appropriate to discuss it by reasoning. Rather we say: the absolute statement of his: 'No marriage except with witnesses' indicates the non-requirement of uprightness and masculinity. And al-Shafi'i requires them, i.e. uprightness and masculinity, because of his statement: 'No marriage except with a guardian and two upright witnesses,' and because it is not property as we mentioned earlier. And al-batira', the diminutive of batra', which is the feminine of abtar, meaning a prayer of a single rak'ah, is an example of the ruling, i.e. proving whether this prayer is legislated or not. And it is not appropriate to discuss it by opinion and reasoning.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar explains the six categories of rulings that are established by legal reasoning (ta'lil) but whose basis must ultimately be textual. The author divides them into: (1) proving the effective cause (mujib) itself, (2) proving its description, (3) proving the condition (shart) itself, (4) proving its description, (5) proving the ruling (hukm) itself, (6) proving its description. He gives one example for each. For the cause, he uses jinsiyyah (genus) for riba al-nasi'ah—the Hanafi position is that genus alone creates a semblance of riba, so credit sales of same items are prohibited; this is established by indication of text, not mere analogy. For the description of the cause, he uses the condition of pasturing for zakat on animals, citing the hadith 'five pasturing camels...' to show that only pasturing animals require zakat, not stall-fed. For the condition itself, he uses witnesses in marriage, established by the hadith 'No marriage except with witnesses.' He notes Malik holds announcement sufficient. For the description of the condition, he uses uprightness and masculinity of witnesses—Hanafis do not require them for validity (only for enforcement) based on the absolute text, while Shafi'i requires them based on another hadith and reasoning of analogy to property. For the ruling, he uses the odd-numbered prayer (al-batira', one rak'ah), questioning whether it is legislated—this cannot be decided by opinion but must come from text. The passage thus reinforces that foundational legal elements (cause, condition, ruling) are derived from revelation, not mere reasoning.

Key Terms
الموجب (al-mujib): The effective cause (illah) that necessitates a ruling, e.g., genus for riba.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition external to the ruling that must be present for the ruling to apply.
الحكم (al-hukm): The legal ruling itself, e.g., obligation or prohibition.
التعليل (al-ta'lil): Legal reasoning to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case based on common effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the condition of pasturing (sawm) required for zakat on grazing animals?
A) Because of logical reasoning that pasturing animals are more valuable.
B) Because the hadith specifies 'in five pasturing camels a sheep' as an indication.
C) Because Imam Malik required it.
D) Because it is established by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The six categories of ta'lil—cause, its description, condition, its description, ruling, its description—must each be grounded in textual indication, not mere analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

The Fourth Category: Extending Rulings via Qiyas (Ta'diyah)
Defining the fourth category of ta'lil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the fourth category of ta'lil (ta'diyah) and apply it by distinguishing between the ruling itself and its description, recognizing that qiyas extends rulings by predominant opinion.

Core Idea
Qiyas extends a ruling to new cases by predominant opinion, not certainty.

In this passage, the author continues the discussion of categories of things that can be established by ta'lil (causal reasoning). The fourth category is ta'diyah – extending a ruling from an explicitly textually established case to a new case that has no direct text. This is the proper domain of qiyas. The passage uses the example of witr prayer to illustrate that while the ruling of witr's obligation is fixed by nass, the description (wasf) of that ruling – whether it is wajib or sunnah – is also text-based and not open to qiyas. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth category of ta'lil
Locate the phrase 'الرابع من جملة علة' which introduces the fourth category. The passage states that it is 'تعدية حكم النص إلى ما لا نص فيه' – extending the ruling of the text to what has no text.
This is the technical definition of qiyas in Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the example of witr
The passage discusses witr prayer: the ruling (hukm) that witr is legislated is established by the hadith 'Allah has added a prayer for you…'. The description (wasf) – whether it is wajib or sunnah – is also textually determined. The Hanafi position is that it is wajib based on this hadith, while al-Shafi'i holds it is sunnah based on a different hadith.
Note that the disagreement is about the description, not the ruling's existence.
3
Understand the epistemological basis of ta'diyah
The passage emphasizes that ta'diyah operates by 'ghalab al-ra'y' (predominant opinion), not certainty. It explicitly states: 'دون القطع واليقين' because a mujtahid may err or hit the correct ruling.
This distinguishes qiyas from definitive textual evidences.
4
Contrast with the definition of description (wasf)
The author clarifies that the description of a ruling (e.g., whether witr is wajib or sunnah) is not subject to qiyas; it is fixed by nass. This illustrates the boundary of ta'diyah: it extends the ruling itself to new cases, not the descriptive attribute.
This prevents overextension of qiyas into matters of pure textual determination.

Chapter of Analogy. 49. Extending the ruling of the text to what has no text [in it]. i.e., the prayer of one rak'ah. And we established its non-permissibility by what was narrated that the Prophet forbade al-batira'. And al-Shafi'i permits it, acting upon his saying: 'If one of you fears the dawn, then let him pray witr with one rak'ah.' * And the description of witr is an example of establishing the description of a ruling. For witr is a legislated ruling, and its description is whether it is obligatory or sunnah. And it is not spoken about by opinion. So we established its obligation by his saying: 'Allah has added a prayer for you, and it is witr.' *** And al-Shafi'i says that it is sunnah, due to his saying: 'No except that you offer supererogatory prayer' when the Bedouin asked him: 'Are there other prayers upon me?' **** Extending the ruling of the text to what has no text. And the fourth [category] from the totality of cause is that for which causal reasoning is used: extending the ruling of the text to what has no text in it to establish in it, i.e., the ruling in what has no text by predominant opinion without certainty and assurance. 'Then let him pray witr with one rak'ah' etc. And we say: Its meaning is that he should add to the prayer he prayed one rak'ah to make it witr, for example, if he prayed two, they become three. (Al-Sunbuli) Without certainty, for a mujtahid errs and hits. (Al-Qamar) Narrated by Ibn 'Abd Allah 'Uthman ... from ... from ... Ibn Muhammad ibn Rabi'ah ibn 'Abd al-Rahman from 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Darawandi from 'Amr ibn Yahya from his father from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Messenger of Allah forbade al-batira', that a man pray one rak'ah as witr. And Ibn 'Abd al-Haqq al-Muhaddith mentioned it in al-Ahkam, likewise in al-Burhan. [Ishraq al-Absar: 30-31] ** Al-Bukhari narrated no. 946, chapter on witr, and Muslim no. 749, chapter on night prayer two by two and witr one rak'ah at the end of the night, from Ibn 'Umar. *** Know that this hadith is narrated from 'Amr ibn al-'As, 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir, Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn 'Umar, Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather, Kharija ibn Hudhafa, and Abu Basra al-Ghifari. As for the hadith of 'Amr and 'Uqbah, they were narrated by Ishaq ibn Rahawayh in his Musnad. As for the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas, it was narrated by al-Daraqutni. [Ishraq al-Absar: 31] Al-Bukhari narrated no. 46, chapter on zakat in Islam, and Muslim no. 11, chapter on explanation of prayers that are one of the pillars of Islam, from Talhah ibn 'Ubayd Allah.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the categories of what is established by ta'lil. It introduces the fourth category: ta'diyat hukm al-nass ila ma la nass fih (extending the ruling of the text to what has no text). This is the proper domain of qiyas. The author first uses the example of witr prayer: the ruling (hukm) of witr's obligation is established by nass (the hadith 'Allah has added a prayer for you, and it is witr'), not by ra'y. However, the description of the ruling (wasf al-hukm)—whether witr is wajib or sunnah—is something that can be derived via qiyas? Actually, here the Hanafi position is that witr is wajib based on nass, but the Shafi'i position that it is sunnah is based on another hadith. The key point is that the fourth category is about using 'illah (cause) to analogically extend a ruling from an original case to a new case. The passage emphasizes that this extension is based on 'ghalab al-ra'y' (predominant opinion), not certainty, because a mujtahid may err. This distinguishes qiyas from the first three categories which require definitive texts. The passage also includes a rebuttal to the Shafi'i argument on witr, explaining that the hadith about praying witr with one rak'ah before dawn actually implies combining with previous prayers, not praying a single rak'ah alone. This demonstrates how Hanafi usul validates qiyas for extending rulings while maintaining that foundational elements remain text-based.

Key Terms
تعدية (ta'diyah): Extending the ruling of a text to a new case that has no explicit text, using qiyas based on a common 'illah.
وصف الحكم (wasf al-hukm): A description or attribute of a ruling, such as whether witr is wajib or sunnah; it is established by nass, not qiyas.
غالب الرأي (ghalab al-ra'y): Predominant opinion without certainty, which is the basis for qiyas rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the epistemological basis of the fourth category of ta'lil (ta'diyah)?
A) Certainty (qat') from the Qur'an and Sunnah.
B) Consensus (ijma') of the Companions.
C) Predominant opinion (ghalab al-ra'y) without certainty.
D) Intuition (hadath) of the mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
Ta'diyah (extending rulings via qiyas) is the fourth category of ta'lil, operates by predominant opinion, and is used to analogically extend a ruling to new cases, but it cannot establish the description (wasf) of a ruling which is fixed by nass.

Ta'diyat al-Hukm: Transmitting Rulings via 'Illah
Defining ta'diyat al-hukm with witr prayer as example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ta'diyat al-hukm and apply it to the dispute over the status of witr prayer.

Core Idea
Ta'diyat al-hukm extends a textual ruling to new cases via the 'illah — the witr debate shows how.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar introduces the concept of ta'diyat al-hukm (transmission of the ruling) within the chapter on Qiyas. Using the example of witr prayer, the author illustrates how the Hanafis and Shafi'is derive different rulings from the same textual sources, demonstrating the mechanics of ta'diyat.

Guided Path
1
Define ta'diyat al-hukm
From the passage, ta'diyat means transmitting the ruling of a text (nass) to a case not explicitly mentioned in the text, via the common effective cause ('illah).
This is the essence of qiyas.
2
Identify the two disputes in the passage
The first dispute is about praying witr with a single rak'ah (al-batira'). The second is about the legal status of witr (wajib vs sunnah).
Both illustrate ta'diyat from different texts.
3
Analyze the Hanafi position on al-batira'
The Hanafis use the hadith prohibiting al-batira' to invalidate a single-rak'ah witr. They interpret the permissive hadith ('pray witr with one rak'ah') as adding to a previous prayer.
This shows ta'diyat: the prohibition is extended to any single-rak'ah witr.
4
Analyze the dispute on witr's status
The Hanafis derive wujub from the hadith 'Allah has increased you a prayer, which is witr,' applying the usal principle that the Prophet's declaration of a prayer as 'increased' indicates obligation. The Shafi'is derive sunnah from the hadith 'None except that you volunteer.'
Both schools perform ta'diyat but to different results due to differing usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس. تعدية حكم النص إلى ما لا نص فيه. أي الصلاة بركعة. وإنما أثبتنا عدم مشروعيتها بما روي أنه عليه السلام نهى عن البتيراء، والشافعي رحمه الله يجوزها عملاً بقوله عليه السلام: "إذا خشي أحدكم الصبح فليوتر بركعة". ونحن نقول: معناه فليضم مع الصلاة التي صلى ركعة لتكون وتراً مثلاً إن صلى اثنتين فتصيران ثلاثة. وصفة الوتر، مثال لإثبات صفة الحكم، فإن الوتر حكم مشروع، وصفته كونه واجباً أو سنة، ولا يُتكلّم فيه بالرأي، فأثبتنا وجوبه بقوله عليه السلام: "إن الله تعالى زادكم صلاة ألا وهي الوتر"، والشافعي رحمه الله يقول: إنها سنة؛ لقوله عليه السلام: "لا إلا أن تطوع" حين سأله الأعرابي بقوله: "هل على غيرهن؟".
Chapter of Qiyas. Transmitting the ruling of the text to that which has no text: meaning prayer with one rak'ah. We established its lack of validity by what was narrated that he (peace be upon him) forbade al-batira', and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) permits it acting upon his (peace be upon him) saying: 'If one of you fears the dawn, he should pray witr with one rak'ah.' And we say: Its meaning is that he should add to the prayer he performed one rak'ah to make it witr, for example, if he prayed two, they become three. And the description of witr is an example for establishing the description of the ruling, for witr is a legislated ruling, and its description is being obligatory or sunnah, and no opinion is spoken in it. So we established its obligation by his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Indeed Allah has increased you a prayer, which is witr.' And al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) says it is sunnah, due to his saying: 'None except that you volunteer' when the Bedouin asked him: 'Is there any other (obligatory prayer) besides them?'
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Qiyas and defines the concept of ta'diyat al-hukm (transmission of the ruling). The author uses the example of praying witr with a single rak'ah. The Hanafi position is that such a prayer is invalid because the Prophet forbade 'al-batira'' – praying one rak'ah alone as witr. Al-Shafi'i, however, permits it based on another hadith: 'If one of you fears the dawn, he should pray witr with one rak'ah.' The Hanafi response interprets that hadith to mean adding one rak'ah to a previous prayer (e.g., two rak'ahs already prayed) to make it three. Then the passage addresses the description (sifah) of witr – whether it is wajib or sunnah. The Hanafis prove it is wajib by the hadith 'Allah has increased you a prayer, which is witr.' Al-Shafi'i argues it is sunnah, citing the Prophet's response to the Bedouin: 'None except that you volunteer.' This illustrates how ta'diyat al-hukm works: the ruling from the text (prohibition or obligation) is extended to new cases via the 'illah.

Key Terms
تعدية (ta'diyat): Transmitting the ruling of a textual case to a new case via the 'illah.
البتيراء (al-batira'): A prayer consisting of a single rak'ah prayed as witr without being preceded by other rak'ahs.
الوتر (al-witr): A prayer performed after the night prayer, consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs; its status (wajib or sunnah) is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do Hanafis argue that witr is wajib?
A) Because it is a prayer with odd rak'ahs
B) Because the Prophet said 'Allah has increased you a prayer, which is witr'
C) Because it is similar to fajr prayer
D) Because the Prophet forbade al-batira'

Key Takeaway
Ta'diyat al-hukm is the core of qiyas: extending a textual ruling to new cases that share the same 'illah, as seen in the witr example.

Required Transitivity of the 'Illah: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on necessity of ta'diya for ta'lil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis require ta'diya for qiyas and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the example of thumaniyya in gold and silver.

Core Idea
Without transitivity, qiyas cannot exist—ta'lil and qiyas are one in Hanafi usul.

This passage confronts a foundational usul difference: is an 'illah valid only if it extends the ruling to new cases? The Hanafi school insists on transitivity (ta'diya) as essential for qiyas, while al-Shafi'i permits non-transitive 'illahs that merely explain the wisdom behind the ruling. We will unpack the arguments and the response to the circularity objection.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on ta'lil and ta'diya
Identify that for Hanafis, ta'lil (causation) is identical to qiyas, and transitivity (ta'diya) is a necessary condition for qiyas to be valid.
The text says: 'فالتعدية حكم لازم عندنا لا يصح القياس بدونه'
2
State the Shafi'i position and their proof
Al-Shafi'i permits ta'lil with a non-transitive 'illah (qasira), such as thumaniyya for riba in gold and silver, and argues that ta'diya is not required because it would create circularity.
Example: 'التعليل بالثمنية في الذهب والفضة لحرمة الربا؛ فإنها لا تتعدى منهما'
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the circularity objection
The Hanafi response states that the 'illah's validity depends on its existence in the branch, not on the act of extending. Thus no circularity.
Text: 'أن صحتها في نفسها لا تتوقف على صحة تعديتها، بل على وجودها في الفرع'
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence: For Hanafis, without ta'diya there is no qiyas; for Shafi'is, ta'lil can exist without qiyas, allowing for purely explanatory causes.
Hanafis: 'فيكون التعليل والقياس واحداً'; Shafi'is: 'فالتعليل عنده لبيان لمية الحكم فقط'
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text clearly establishes the Hanafi view as the relied-upon position, as it states 'فالتعدية حكم لازم عندنا' and refutes the Shafi'i argument.
No explicit 'wa alayhi al-fatwa', but the structure favors Hanafi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس. تعدية حكم النص إلى ما لا نص فيه. فالتعدية حكم لازم عندنا لا يصح القياس بدونه، والتعليل يساويه في الوجود جائز عند الشافعي؛ لأنه يجوز التعليل بالعلة القاصرة كالتعليل بالثمنية في الذهب والفضة لحرمة الربا؛ فإنها لا تتعدى منهما، فالتعليل عنده لبيان لمية الحكم فقط، ولا يتوقف على التعدية؛ لأن صحة التعدية موقوفة على صحتها في نفسها، فلو توقف صحتها في نفسها على صحة تعديتها لزم الدور. والجواب: أن صحتها في نفسها لا تتوقف على صحة تعديتها، بل على وجودها في الفرع، فلا دور. والدليل لنا: أن دليل الشرع عنده صحيح. فالتعدية حكم لازم إلخ الحاصل أن التعليل عندنا ليس إلا لتعدية الحكم في محل المنصوص إلى محل آخر، فيكون التعليل والقياس واحداً، وعند الشافعي يجوز التعليل لزيادة القبول وسرعة الوصول والاطلاع على حكمة الشارع، فيوجد بدون القياس.
Chapter of Qiyas. Transmitting the ruling of the text to that which has no text. So the transmission is a necessary ruling with us, qiyas is not valid without it, and causation is equal to it in existence, permissible according to al-Shafi'i, because he permits causation with a non-transitive cause such as causation by value (thumaniyya) in gold and silver for the prohibition of riba, for it does not extend beyond them. So causation according to him is only to explain the rationale of the ruling, and it does not depend on transmission, because the validity of transmission depends on its own validity, and if its own validity depended on the validity of transmission, circularity would result. The answer: its own validity does not depend on the validity of transmission, but on its existence in the branch, so there is no circularity. And the proof for us: that the evidence of the law according to him is valid. So transmission is a necessary ruling... The gist is that causation with us is nothing but the transmission of the ruling from the textual place to another place, so causation and qiyas are one, while according to al-Shafi'i, causation is permissible for increasing acceptance, speed of access, and insight into the wisdom of the Lawgiver, so it exists without qiyas.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational usul dispute between the Hanafi school and al-Shafi'i on the nature of ta'lil (causation) and its relationship to qiyas. The Hanafi position is that for an 'illah to be valid, it must be transitive (mutta'addiya), i.e., it must extend the ruling from the original case to a new case. Without this transitivity (ta'diya), qiyas cannot be performed. Al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, permits ta'lil with a non-transitive (qasira) 'illah, such as explaining the prohibition of riba in gold and silver based on their being priced (thumaniyya), without extending that ruling to other commodities. For al-Shafi'i, ta'lil serves to reveal the wisdom (hikma) behind the ruling, not necessarily to extend it. The Hanafi objection is that if the validity of ta'diya depends on the 'illah's own validity, and that validity depends on ta'diya, a circular argument results. The response counters that the 'illah's validity depends on its existence in the branch, not on ta'diya. Ultimately, the Hanafis equate ta'lil with qiyas itself: both require ta'diya. The passage concludes that for al-Shafi'i, ta'lil is broader than qiyas and can exist without extension.

Key Terms
العلة القاصرة (al-'illah al-qasirah): A cause that does not extend beyond its original case; it explains the ruling in the original but does not apply to new cases.
التعدية (al-ta'diyah): The transitive property of the 'illah: it moves the ruling from the original to a new case.
التعليل (al-ta'lil): The act of ascribing a legal cause ('illah) to a ruling; it can be with or without extension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence of the Hanafi requirement that ta'diya is necessary for ta'lil?
A) All 'illah must be explicit in the Quran or Sunnah.
B) A non-transitive 'illah cannot support qiyas.
C) Qiyas is valid only if the 'illah is agreed upon by all schools.
D) Ta'lil can exist without qiyas.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, ta'lil and qiyas are identical, both requiring that the 'illah be transitive (mutta'addiya); a non-transitive 'illah is insufficient for deriving new rulings.

Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Qiyas and Ta'lil: The Necessity of Transference
Defining qiyas and debating the necessity of ta'diya for ta'lil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on ta'lil, identify the key point of contention regarding transference (ta'diya), and evaluate the Hanafi argument against the restricted cause.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, valid ta'lil is always transitive; without transference it is futile (عبث).

This passage presents a foundational usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the nature of ta'lil (causation) and its relationship to qiyas (analogy). The Hanafi school argues that ta'lil cannot exist independently of qiyas—every valid ta'lil must involve transference of the ruling to a new case. The Shafi'i school allows a restricted cause (al-illa al-qasira) that explains the ruling without extending it. Understanding this dispute clarifies how each school derives rulings and evaluates the role of human reasoning in law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition of qiyas
Note the opening: 'تعدية حكم النص إلى ما لا نص فيه' (transferring the ruling of the text to that which has no text). The transference (ta'diya) is a necessary attribute.
لا يصح القياس بدونه – qiyas is invalid without ta'diya.
2
Understand the Hanafi claim: ta'lil equals qiyas
The text states 'والتعليل يساويه في الوجود' (ta'lil equals qiyas in existence). Hanafis hold that any valid ta'lil must involve transference; thus ta'lil and qiyas are coterminous.
The commentary explains: عندنا ليس إلا لتعدية الحكم.
3
Recognize the Shafi'i view allowing restricted cause
Shafi'is permit ta'lil without transference using a cause confined to the original (al-illa al-qasira), e.g., being a price (thaman) in gold/silver for riba prohibition.
For them, ta'lil serves to explain wisdom (hikma) and increase acceptance, not necessarily to extend the ruling.
4
Analyze the Hanafi argument: futility (عبث)
Hanafis claim that ta'lil without transference is futile because it provides no new ruling (already known from text) and no action benefit. It fails to produce certain knowledge or obligation.
The text argues: لا بد أن يكون موجبًا للعلم أو العمل... فلا فائدة له إلا ثبوت الحكم في الفرع.
5
Note the exception: cause by text or ijma
Both schools agree that if the restricted cause is established by explicit text (nass) or consensus (ijma), it is valid. The benefit then is knowing the Lawgiver's designation.
النزاع إنما هو في علة مستنبطة مناسبة... وأما المنصوصة فجائزة بالاتفاق.

وأما
= الظن فبعد غلبة رأي المجتهد إلى عليتها، وترجّح عليتها عنده بأمارات معتبرة في استنباط العلل لا معنى لعدم الظن، عند عدم الرجحان فلا نزاع ، وعند تعارض الوصف القاصر والمتعدي فالعلة هو المتعدي فلا نزاع أيضًا. (القمر) لا بد أن يكون إلخ إذ لو خلا عن العلم والعمل كليهما لكان عبثًا. (القمر) والتعليل: أي بالقاصر لا يفيد العلم قطعًا فإن العلة القاصرة توجب غلبة الظن (القمر) لأنه أي لأن العمل في المنصوص عليه ثابت بالنص، أي لا بالعلة فإن النص فوق التعليل، فيضاف الثبوت إلى النص لا إلى العلة.
فلا فائدة له أي للتعليل إلا ثبوت إلخ، ولما لم يكن العلة متعدية إلى الفرع، بل تكون قاصرة فيكون التعليل بلا فائدة، فعلم أنه لا يجوز التعليل بالعلة القاصرة فإنه عبث ولقائل أن يقول: إن فائدتها زيادة الإطمينان
بالأحكام والإطلاق على حكمة الشارع في شرعيتها. (القمر) وهو أي ثبوت الحكم في الفرع (القمر) ابتداء أي لا تعدية بأن يكون مقيسًا على الأصل المنصوص. (القمر) فيه أي في إثبات السبب أو الشرط
أو الحكم بدون التعدية. (القمر) وأما في السبب والشرط بالتعليل أي ما لا نص فيه فلا يجوز إلخ. (القمر) ويجوز إلخ لأن الوصف الذي هو دال على تعيين السبب في الأصل أو على تعيين الشرط فيه لما وجد في الفرع فيعدى السببية والشرطية أيضًا إلى الفرع بأن جعلناه سببًا أو شرطًا أيضًا، ألا ترى إلى قياس أمير المؤمنين علي له شرب الخمر على القذف فقال: إنه كما أن القذف علة لإقامة الحدّ أي ثمانين جلدة كذالك شرب الخمر علة لهذا الجلد، فتعدّى العلة بالقياس وقبل الصحابة الله قوله (القمر) فخر الإسلام محيه وكذا عند القاضي أبي زيد "تنوير". (المحشي بوصف مشترك بينه: أي بين الزنا وبين اللواطة، وهو سفح ماء محرّم في محل مشتهى. (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas. Transferring the ruling of the text to what has no text, thus transference is a necessary attribute with us: Qiyas is not valid without it. And ta'lil equals it in existence. It is permissible according to al-Shafi'i because he permits ta'lil with the restricted cause, like ta'lil by being a price (thaman) in gold and silver for the prohibition of riba; for it does not transfer from them. So ta'lil according to him is only to explain the reason of the ruling, and does not depend on transference. Because the validity of transference is dependent on its validity in itself. If its validity in itself were dependent on the validity of its transference, a circularity would occur. The answer: Its validity in itself does not depend on the validity of its transference, but on its existence in the branch, so no circularity. And our proof: that the evidence of the law according to him is valid. So transference is a necessary attribute. The conclusion: ta'lil according to us is only for transferring the ruling from the place of the text to another place, so ta'lil and qiyas are one. According to al-Shafi'i, ta'lil is permissible for increasing acceptance, speed of access, and insight into the wisdom of the Lawgiver, so it exists without qiyas. The summary: ta'lil according to al-Shafi'i is more general than qiyas; because it does not require transference. Its effect is the establishment of the ruling on the original by the cause: if the cause transfers, the ruling is established in the branch and it is qiyas; if it does not transfer, the ruling remains limited to the original, and it is a proper ta'lil like the text which is specific. (al-Sanbali) It equals it i.e. qiyas: if qiyas is not valid without transference, then ta'lil is not valid without transference either, for the implicans is negated by the negation of the necessary. (al-Qamar) In existence i.e. not in concept or truth. (al-Muhashi) Permissible according to al-Shafi'i: meaning transference is not necessary for ta'lil according to him. If ta'lil provides transference of the cause to the branch, it is qiyas; if ta'lil does not provide transference but stays confined to the place of the text, it is not qiyas. So ta'lil according to him is more general than qiyas. (al-Qamar) Because he permits etc. As for the verifying scholars of the Hanafis, they do not permit this ta'lil. (al-Qamar) With the restricted cause: i.e. that which does not exist in the branch. Then know that the dispute is only about a cause derived from suitability between the ruling and the cause. As for the cause stipulated by text or consensus, it is permissible to be restricted and specific to the original by agreement, no dispute. And a benefit is also obtained: our knowledge by the Lawgiver's declaration that this cause is the effective one. And what benefit is greater than this? (al-Qamar) For it does not transfer etc., since other than the two stones (gold and silver) are not created as a price. (al-Qamar) In its validity: the pronoun refers to ta'lil, and the feminine is because originally it was 'ta'lila', or because ta'lil means the cause. al-Muhashi: And the answer: its validity i.e. the validity of the cause in itself etc. It can also be answered that this interdependence from both sides is mutual interdependence like in correlatives, so no circularity. (al-Qamar) And our proof etc. This proof is refuted by ta'lil with the restricted cause stipulated by a probable text like khabar al-wahid, for it requires that this ta'lil is also not permissible due to the running of its premises, so understand. And the author of al-Talwih said: There is no dispute in ta'lil with a restricted cause that is not stipulated. If what is meant is lack of certainty about its causality, then there is no dispute, for the Shafi'is also say there is no certainty. If what is meant is lack of probability, then after the ijtihad's overwhelming opinion on its causality and its preponderance according to him by reliable indications in deriving causes, there is no meaning to lack of probability. When there is no preponderance, then no dispute. And when the restricted and transitive descriptions conflict, the cause is the transitive one, so no dispute also. (al-Qamar) It must be that which leads to certain knowledge or action. And ta'lil (with the restricted) does not provide certain knowledge definitely, nor does it provide action in the original because it is established by the text, so it has no benefit except the establishment of the ruling in the branch, which is the meaning of transference. And ta'lil for the first three categories and negating them is invalid, meaning: establishing a cause, condition, or ruling initially by opinion, and likewise negating them, is invalid; because the servant has no choice or authority in it, it is only for the Lawgiver. As for if a cause, condition, or ruling is established by text or consensus, and we want to transfer it to another place, there is no doubt that this is permissible by agreement in the ruling; because he placed qiyas. As for the cause and condition, it is not permissible according to the generality (al-amma), but it is permissible according to Fakhr al-Islam in its place. For example, if we compare sodomy to adultery as a cause for the hadd penalty by a shared description between it and sodomy to make sodomy also a cause for the hadd, it is permissible according to him, not according to them. If the author followed Fakhr al-Islam, as appears, then the meaning of 'al-amma' in Fakhr al-Islam's view is [as above]. (al-Qamar) It must be etc., for if it were devoid of both knowledge and action, it would be futile. (al-Qamar) And ta'lil: i.e. with the restricted does not provide certain knowledge definitely, for the restricted cause gives only overwhelming opinion. (al-Qamar) Because action in the original is established by the text, i.e., not by the cause, for the text is above ta'lil, so the establishment is attributed to the text, not to the cause. So there is no benefit for it (ta'lil) except the establishment in the branch. And since the cause is not transitive to the branch but is restricted, the ta'lil would be without benefit, so it is known that ta'lil with the restricted cause is not permissible, as it is futile. One could say: Its benefit is increased tranquility in the rulings and insight into the Lawgiver’s wisdom in their legislation. (al-Qamar) And it i.e. the establishment of the ruling in the branch. (al-Qamar) Initially i.e. without transference by being measured to the original text. (al-Qamar) In it i.e. in establishing the cause, condition, or ruling without transference. (al-Qamar) As for the cause and condition by ta'lil i.e. what has no text, it is not permissible etc. (al-Qamar) And it is permissible etc., because the description that indicates the designation of the cause in the original or the designation of the condition in it, when it exists in the branch, the causality and conditionality are also transferred to the branch by making it a cause or condition as well. Do you not see the qiyas of the Commander of the Faithful Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) of drinking wine on slander (qadhf): he said: Just as slander is a cause for establishing the hadd (eighty lashes), so is drinking wine a cause for these lashes. Thus the cause was transferred by qiyas, and the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) accepted his statement. (al-Qamar) Fakhr al-Islam, may Allah have mercy on him, and likewise with Qadi Abu Zaid in al-Tanwir. (al-Muhashi) By a shared description between them: i.e. between adultery and sodomy, which is pouring prohibited fluid into a desired place. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nature of ta'lil (causation/ratio legis) and its relationship to qiyas (analogical reasoning). The text opens with the definition of qiyas: transferring a ruling from a text (original) to a case not covered by text (branch). It then states that transference (ta'diya) is a necessary attribute of qiyas; without it, qiyas is invalid. Ta'lil, according to the Hanafis, equals qiyas in existence: any valid ta'lil must involve transference. The Shafi'i school, however, permits ta'lil with a restricted cause (al-illa al-qasira), i.e., a cause that stays confined to the original case and does not transfer to other cases, as exemplified by the cause of 'being a price' (thaman) in gold and silver for the prohibition of riba. For the Shafi'is, ta'lil serves merely to explain the wisdom of the ruling, not necessarily to extend it. The Hanafis object that such ta'lil is futile because it does not produce any new ruling (the original is already established by text) and does not lead to action or knowledge in practice. The Hanafis argue that if ta'lil were valid without transference, it would be an unnecessary exercise. However, the text acknowledges that if the 'illa is established by explicit text or ijma, even the Hanafis accept it as valid, recognizing its benefit in understanding the Lawgiver's intent. The debate touches on logical issues like circularity (dawr) and the conditions for the validity of a cause. The Hanafi proof is that without the benefit of transference, ta'lil is idle. A counterexample from khabar al-wahid is briefly discussed. The passage concludes by discussing the permissibility of transferring causes and conditions by qiyas, with reference to Fakhr al-Islam and the qiyas of 'Ali concerning wine and slander. Throughout, the text follows the pattern of stating the matn, then providing commentary from various scholars (al-Sanbali, al-Qamar, al-Muhashi), clarifying terms and nuances.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): تعدية حكم النص إلى ما لا نص فيه (transferring the ruling of the text to that which has no text)
التعليل (al-ta'lil): بيان علة الحكم (explaining the ratio legis of a ruling). This passage discusses its relationship to qiyas.
العلة القاصرة (al-illa al-qasira): العلة التي لا تتعدى محل النص (the cause that does not transfer from the place of the text)
التعدية (al-ta'diya): نقل الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع (transferring the ruling from the original to the branch)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the status of a ta'lil that uses a restricted cause (al-illa al-qasira) without being established by text or ijma?
A) Valid and legitimate, as it explains wisdom
B) Invalid because it is futile (عبث)
C) Valid only if the cause is transitive
D) Permissible but not preferred

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, ta'lil must involve transference; a restricted cause without text or ijma is rejected as futile.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Conditions for Valid Ta'lil and the Dispute over Ta'diyah in Qiyas
Establishing rules for ta'lil and the dispute over ta'diyah of cause/condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between a qasira and muta'addi 'illah, and evaluate the dispute over transferring the cause/condition itself via qiyas.

Core Idea
Ta'lil is only beneficial if the 'illah transfers the ruling to a branch — a qasira 'illah is futile unless it becomes muta'addi.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar explores the conditions under which ta'lil (causation) is valid in qiyas. The author distinguishes between a deficient 'illah ('illah qasira) which remains confined to the original case, and a transgressive 'illah ('illah muta'addi) that can be extended to new cases. A key dispute arises over whether the very causality or conditionality of a textually established cause can be transferred to a new case by qiyas. The passage also provides the famous analogy of 'Ali (RA) as evidence for the permissibility of transferring causality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for valid ta'lil
Read the opening sentence: 'لا بد أن يكون موجبًا للعلم أو العمل' — ta'lil must produce either knowledge or action. If it does neither, it is frivolous. Determine what kind of 'illah meets this condition.
The 'illah qasira gives only zann (predominant speculation), not knowledge, and it does not produce action for the original (already known by text). So it fails the condition unless it transfers to a branch.
2
Understand the prohibition of establishing causes by mere opinion
The text states that establishing a cause, condition, or ruling (or negating them) by personal opinion (ra'y) is invalid. Authority rests solely with the Lawgiver. However, if a cause is already established by text or consensus, we may transfer it via qiyas.
This is the foundational principle that qiyas is not legislation but discovery of existing law.
3
Analyze the dispute over ta'diyah of cause/condition
While transferring the ruling (hukm) by qiyas is agreed upon, transferring the causality itself (sababiyyah) or conditionality (shartiyyah) is disputed. The majority (al-amma) reject it; Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi permits it. Follow the dispute: what is the proof on each side?
The practical consequence: under Fakhr al-Islam, sodomy becomes a direct cause for hadd; under the majority, it is only analogized to adultery for the ruling.
4
Examine the proof from the analogy of 'Ali (RA)
The text cites the analogy of 'Ali (RA) comparing drinking wine to slander. He said: just as slander is a cause for hadd (80 lashes), so is drinking wine. The Companions accepted this. This shows that the causality of the description (waskh/shurb) was transferred by qiyas.
The shared description is 'emission of forbidden fluid in a desired place' for the sodomy analogy, but for the wine analogy, the description is probably the causing of harm or accusation (the text mentions both).
5
Conclude the only benefit of ta'lil is ta'diyah
The passage ends by stating that nothing remains of the benefits of ta'lil except transfer to what has no text. This reinforces that the 'illah must be muta'addi; a qasira 'illah is useless unless it can be extended.
This leads naturally into the next topic: istihsan as an evidence that sometimes opposes manifest qiyas.

تعدية حكم النص إلى ما لا نص فيه
لا بد أن يكون موجبًا للعلم أو العمل، والتعليل لا يفيد العلم قطعًا، ولا يفيد العمل أيضًا في المنصوص عليه؛ لأنه ثابت بالنص، فلا فائدة له إلا ثبوت الحكم في الفرع، وهو معنى التعدية، والتعليل للأقسام الثلاثة الأول ونفيها باطل، يعني إن إثبات سبب أو شرط أو حكم ابتداءً بالرأي وكذا نفيها باطل؛ إذ لا اختيار ولا ولاية للعبد فيه، وإنما هو إلى الشارع، وأمّا لو ثبت سبب أو شرط أو حكم من نص أو إجماع، وأردنا أن نُعدّيه إلى محل آخر، فلا شك

بيان الاستحسان
كونه باطلًا أنه باطل ابتداءً لا تعديةً وإلا فالمراد به البطلان مطلقا ابتداءً وتعدية.

أي حكم النص
هذا تارةً على سبيل القياس الجلي وتارةً على سبيل الاستحسان وهو الدليل الذي أي التعدية
يعارض القياس الجلي أشار إلى بيانه بقوله:
بيان الاستحسان]
Chapter of Qiyas
51
Transferring the ruling of a text to what is not mentioned in the text.
It is necessary that it be productive of knowledge or action. And ta'lil (causation) does not produce knowledge definitively, nor does it produce action regarding the ruled-upon (the original case) because the ruling is established by the text, so it has no benefit except establishing the ruling in the branch, which is the meaning of transfer (ta'diyah). And ta'lil for the first three categories and their negation is invalid, meaning that establishing a cause, condition, or ruling initially by opinion, and likewise negating them, is invalid; for the servant has no choice or authority in it, it is only for the Lawgiver. However, if a cause, condition, or ruling is established by text or consensus, and we wish to transfer it to another locus, there is no doubt that that is permissible in the ruling by agreement, because qiyas has been established. But regarding the cause and condition, it is not permissible according to the general scholars, but it is permissible according to Fakhr al-Islam. For example, if we analogize sodomy to adultery in being a cause for the hadd punishment with a description shared between them and sodomy, to make sodomy also a cause for the hadd, it is permissible according to him, not according to them. If the author is a follower of Fakhr al-Islam as is apparent, then the meaning of 'general' is Fakhr al-Islam. And as for speculation, after the mujtahid's opinion predominates towards its effective cause, and its preferability is established with valid indicators in deriving causes, there is no meaning to lack of speculation. When there is no preponderance, there is no dispute. And when there is conflict between a deficient (qasir) and transgressive (muta'addi) description, the effective cause is the transgressive; so also no dispute. (al-Qamar) 'It is necessary' etc., because if it were devoid of both knowledge and action, it would be frivolous. (al-Qamar) And ta'lil: that is, with the deficient (cause) does not produce knowledge definitively, for the deficient cause gives rise to predominant speculation. (al-Qamar) Because the action regarding the ruled-upon is established by the text, that is, not by the cause, for the text is above ta'lil, so the establishment is attributed to the text, not to the cause. So there is no benefit to it, meaning to ta'lil, except establishing the ruling in the branch. And since the cause is not transgressive to the branch, but is deficient, the ta'lil becomes without benefit. It is thus known that ta'lil with the deficient cause is not permissible, for it is frivolous. One may object that its benefit is increasing tranquility regarding the rulings and being informed of the wisdom of the Lawgiver in their legislation. (al-Qamar) And it (i.e., establishing the ruling in the branch) (al-Qamar) initially, i.e., not as a transfer, in that it is analogized to the original text. (al-Qamar) In it (i.e., in establishing the cause or condition or ruling without transfer). (al-Qamar) And as for the cause and condition by ta'lil, i.e., what has no text, it is not permissible, etc. (al-Qamar) And it is permissible, etc., because the description that indicates the specification of the cause in the original, or the specification of the condition in it, when found in the branch, the causality and conditionality are also transferred to the branch, so that we make it a cause or a condition as well. Do you not see the analogy of the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) of drinking wine to slander? He said: Just as slander is a cause for establishing the hadd, i.e., eighty lashes, likewise drinking wine is a cause for these lashes. So the cause was transferred by qiyas, and the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) accepted his statement. (al-Qamar) Fakhr al-Islam, and similarly with Qadi Abu Zayd. (al-Muhashi) With a shared description between them, i.e., between adultery and sodomy, and it is the emission of forbidden fluid in a desired place. (al-Qamar)

Chapter of Qiyas
02
Explanation of Istihsan
That it is invalid: it is invalid initially, not as a transfer; otherwise, what is meant by it is absolute invalidity, both initially and as a transfer. So nothing remains except the fourth, meaning nothing remains of the benefits of ta'lil except transfer to what has no text. And since
(i.e., the ruling of the text)
this is sometimes on the basis of manifest qiyas and sometimes on the basis of istihsan, and it is the evidence that (i.e., the transfer) conflicts with manifest qiyas, he indicated its explanation by saying:
Explanation of Istihsan]
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is an extended ruling on the nature and conditions of ta'lil (causation) in qiyas. It opens by stating that the 'illah (legal cause) must be productive of either conclusive knowledge (ilm) or probable speculation (zann) leading to action. Ta'lil by a deficient (qasira) cause, which stays in the original, does not produce knowledge and is useless unless it serves to transfer the ruling to a branch. The author then prohibits establishing a cause, condition, or ruling by mere personal opinion, as authority lies solely with the Lawgiver. However, once a cause is textually established, transferring it to a new case via qiyas is permissible by agreement on the level of the ruling itself; but transferring the causality itself (i.e., making the new case a cause) is disputed. The majority (al-amma) reject it, while Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi permits it, provided the descriptive attribute is shared, as in analogy between sodomy and adultery. The commentary notes that even the deficient cause gives predominant speculation, but ta'lil by it is still invalid unless it transfers to a branch. The passage concludes by summarizing that the only remaining benefit of ta'lil is ta'diyah, and introduces the next topic: istihsan as an evidence that opposes manifest qiyas. The author follows the order: first defining qiyas and its conditions, then addressing istihsan.

Key Terms
العلة القاصرة (al-'illah al-qasirah): A cause that remains in the original and does not transfer to a branch; only benefits the original ruling.
العلة المتعدية (al-'illah al-muta'addiyah): A cause that can be applied to other cases beyond the original, enabling qiyas.
التعدية (al-ta'diyah): Transferring the ruling or cause from the original to a branch via qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the only remaining benefit of ta'lil after excluding knowledge and action for the original?
A) Increasing tranquility in the rulings
B) Transferring (ta'diyah) the ruling to what has no text
C) Establishing a new cause by opinion
D) Confirming the original ruling by consensus

Key Takeaway
The only valid purpose of ta'lil is to transfer the ruling (and possibly the cause/condition) to new cases; a qasira 'illah is futile unless it can be extended.
