Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Precedence of Istihsan over Qiyas by Strength of Effect
Explains rule for preferring istihsan or qiyas based on effect strength

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for preferring istihsan over qiyas jali by comparing the strength of their legal effects (athar), and explain why Hanafis reject co-extensiveness (tard) as a sufficient basis for causality.

Core Idea
Prefer the stronger legal effect, not the clearer analogy — strength of effect (athar) decides between qiyas jali and istihsan.

In Hanafi usul, there is often a conflict between a clear analogy (qiyas jali) and a hidden but more effective analogy (istihsan). The author of Noor al-Anwar lays down a simple rule: the criterion for preference is not the apparentness of the analogy but the strength of the legal effect it produces. This rule is rooted in the Hanafi view that a cause (illa) is only valid if it has a proven impact on the ruling, not merely because it co-varies with it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of the rule
The first three types of istihsan—by textual effect, by consensus, and by necessity—always take precedence over qiyas. The difficulty arises only between clear qiyas (jali) and hidden qiyas (istihsan). Focus on that pair.
2
State the decisive criterion
The rule: precedence is given to the one with the stronger legal effect (athar), regardless of whether it is apparent or hidden. Strength of effect is measured by its impact, permanence, and textual or consensual support.
The author compares this to the Hereafter outweighing this world despite being hidden.
3
Examine the underlying usul principle
This rule is built on the Hanafi position that a cause (illa) is established by its effect (athar), not by mere co-extensiveness (tard). Co-extensiveness alone does not prove causation; the cause must demonstrate its impact in producing the ruling through text or consensus.
The Shafi'i school, called 'Ahl al-Tard', accepts causes based solely on co-extensiveness.
4
Analyze the dispute with the Shafi'i school
The Hanafi response: a tard cause is insufficient because it lacks proof of actual effect. The Shafi'is defend tard causes; each school refutes the other's methodology. The practical difference appears in cases like the leftover water of predatory birds.
Hanafis use istihsan (hidden qiyas) based on strong effect, while Shafi'is may use clear qiyas based on co-extensiveness.
5
Address a common misconception
Critics claim istihsan is a fifth proof outside the four (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas). The text clarifies that istihsan is a type of qiyas—specifically a stronger hidden analogy—so it remains within the four proofs. Thus Abu Hanifa is not to be criticized.
The confirmation is: 'acting by istihsan is not outside the four proofs, but it is a stronger type of qiyas'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
بيان الاستحسان
أن الأقسام الثلاثة الأول مقدّمة على القياس، وإنما الاشتباه في تقديم القياس الجلي على الخفي ،وبالعكس، فأراد أن يبين ضابطة ليعلم بها تقديم أحدهما على الآخر، فقال: ولما صارت العلة عندنا علة بأثرها لا بدورانها كما تقوله الشافعية من أهل الطرد قدّمنا العلة على القياس والاستحسان الذي هو قياس الخفي إذا قوي أثره؛ لأن المدار على قوة التأثير وضعفه، لا على الظهور والخفاء؛ فإن الدنيا ظاهرة والعقبى باطنة، لكنها ترجّحت على الدنيا بقوة أثرها من حيث الدوام ،والصفاء وأمثلته كثيرة منها: سؤر سباع الطير المذكور آنفا، فإن الاستحسان فيه قوي الأثر؛ ولذا يقدم على القياس كما حرّرت، وفي هذا إشارة إلى أن العمل بالاستحسان ليس بخارج من الحجج الأربعة، بل هو نوع أقوى للقياس، فلا طعن على أبي حنيفة له في أنه يعمل بما سوى الأدلّة الأربعة.
وقدمنا القياس لصحة أثره الباطن على الاستحسان
الأقسام الثلاثة أي الاستحسان الذي يكون بالأثر والإجماع والضرورة. (القمر) لا بدورانها أي بدوران الحكم مع العلة وجودًا وعدما أو وجودًا . (القمر) من أهل الطرد إلخ والعلة الطردية هي الوصف الذي اعتبر فيه دوران الحكم معه وجودًا أو عدمًا عند البعض، وجودًا عند البعض الآخر من غير نظر إلى ثبوت أثره في موضع بنص أو إجماع، والاحتجاج بها غير صحيح عندنا، والشافعية يحتج بها، ونحن نحتج بالعلة المؤثرة وندفع العلل الطردية على وجه يُلجئ الشافعية إلى القول بالتأثير، والشافعية تدفع المؤثرة، ثم نجيبهم عن الدفع.(السنبلي) على القياس أي الذي ضعف أثره وإن كان جليًا. (القمر) قوي الأثر : فإن ملاقاة الطاهر بالطاهر له تأثير قوي في التطهر . (القمر) هذا أي في قول المصنف له الاستحسان الذي هو القياس الخفي. (القمر) فلا طعن إلخ كما قال طعنًا من لا رواية له: إن حجج الشرع الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والقياس، والاستحسان قسم خامس خارج عن الأربعة، فالعمل به عمل بما ليس بحجة شرعًا. (القمر) وقدمنا القياس أي القياس الجلي إلخ، وهذا معطوف على قول المصنف له: "قدمنا" إلخ، ثم اعلم أن هذا القياس أي الذي يترجّح على الاستحسان بقوة أثره الباطن قليل الوجود فإنه لم يوجد إلا في سبع مسائل، كذا في "التحقيق"، وأما القسم الأول أي تقديم الاستحسان بقوة أثره على القياس فأكثر من أن يُحصى. (القمر) لصحة أثره الباطن أي وإن كان فاسدًا بحسب الظاهر . (القمر) على الاستحسان وتسمية هذا الاستحسان استحسانًا مع أنه متروك غير مستحسن من باب التغليب لا من باب الحقيقة. (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas: Explanation of Istihsan. That the first three types [of istihsan] are given precedence over qiyas, and the confusion is only in giving precedence of clear qiyas over hidden [qiyas] and vice versa. So he wanted to explain a rule by which precedence of one over the other is known. He said: Since the cause for us is a cause by its effect, not by its co-extensiveness as the Shafi'is, the people of ṭard, say, we gave precedence to the cause [or: qiyas] over qiyas and istihsan, which is hidden qiyas, when its effect is strong, because the criterion is strength and weakness of effect, not apparentness and hiddenness. For the worldly life is apparent and the Hereafter is hidden, but it outweighs this world by the strength of its effect in terms of permanence and purity. Examples are many, among them: the leftover water of predatory birds mentioned earlier; for in it, istihsan has a strong effect, so it is given precedence over qiyas as has been set down. And in this there is an indication that acting by istihsan is not outside the four proofs, but it is a stronger type of qiyas, so Abu Hanifa is not to be criticized for acting with other than the four proofs. And we gave precedence to qiyas over istihsan due to the soundness of its hidden effect. The three types: istihsan by effect, consensus, and necessity. (al-Qamar) 'Not by its co-extensiveness': i.e., by the co-extensiveness of the ruling with the cause in existence and non-existence or in existence. (al-Qamar) 'People of ṭard': the ṭardi cause is the description in which the co-extensiveness of the ruling with it is considered, in existence or non-existence according to some, and in existence according to others, without considering the proof of its effect in a place by text or consensus. Arguing by it is not valid for us, while the Shafi'is argue by it. We argue by the effective cause and refute the ṭardi causes in a way that forces the Shafi'is to acknowledge effect, and the Shafi'is refute the effective, then we answer them regarding the refutation. (al-Sanbali) 'Over qiyas': i.e., the qiyas whose effect is weak, even if it is clear. (al-Qamar) 'Strong effect': for the contact of a pure thing with a pure thing has a strong effect in purification. (al-Qamar) 'This': i.e., in the author's statement: 'istihsan, which is hidden qiyas'. (al-Qamar) 'So no criticism': as said as a criticism by one with no narration: the proofs of the law are the Book, Sunnah, Consensus, and Qiyas, and Istihsan is a fifth category outside these four, so acting on it is acting without a legal proof. (al-Qamar) 'And we gave precedence to qiyas': i.e., clear qiyas, and this is connected to the author's statement: 'We gave precedence' etc. Then know that this qiyas, i.e., which outweighs istihsan by the strength of its hidden effect, is rare, for it is found only in seven issues, as in al-Tahqiq. As for the first category, i.e., giving precedence to istihsan over qiyas due to the strength of its effect, it is more than can be counted. (al-Qamar) 'Due to the soundness of its hidden effect': i.e., even if it is unsound outwardly. (al-Qamar) 'Over istihsan', and calling this istihsan 'istihsan' though it is abandoned and not approved is by way of predominance, not reality.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (usul rule) from the chapter on Qiyas, explaining the precedence between istihsan (hidden analogy) and qiyas jali (clear analogy). The author states that the first three types of istihsan (by textual effect, consensus, or necessity) are always given precedence over qiyas. The difficulty lies in deciding between clear qiyas and hidden qiyas (istihsan). The rule is: prefer whichever has the stronger legal effect (athar), regardless of its apparent clarity. The Hanafi approach is to consider the cause (illa) as effective by its actual impact in producing a ruling, not merely by its co-extensiveness (dawaran) with the ruling as the Shafi'is hold. Co-extensiveness alone is insufficient; the cause must demonstrate its effect in a specific case through text or consensus. The example of leftover water of predatory birds illustrates this: istihsan (deeming it pure) is preferred over qiyas (deeming it impure by analogy with wild beasts) because the effect of purity has a strong basis in original purity. This rule also refutes the criticism that istihsan is outside the four proofs; it is actually a stronger form of qiyas. The passage concludes with a note that giving precedence to qiyas over istihsan (due to its strong hidden effect) is rare, occurring only in about seven issues.

Key Terms
علة (illa): The effective cause in qiyas; the attribute that determines the ruling due to its proven effect, not merely co-extensiveness.
استحسان (istihsan): Preferring a stronger hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) over a clear analogy (qiyas jali) due to the strength of its effect.
قياس جلي (qiyas jali): Clear analogy, where the cause is apparent and directly comparable; often referred to as the weaker of the two when its effect is weak.
قياس خفي (qiyas khafi): Hidden analogy, synonymous with istihsan; a less apparent but more effective analogy.
طرد (tard): Co-extensiveness; the method of verifying a cause by checking if the ruling is present with the cause and absent without it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul rule, what is the criterion for preferring between clear qiyas (qiyas jali) and hidden qiyas (istihsan)?
A) The quantity of supporting texts
B) The strength of the effect (athar), not the apparentness
C) The chronological order of the analogies
D) The popularity among jurists

Key Takeaway
The strength of a ruling's effect (athar) determines which analogy prevails, not its apparentness.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Precedence of Qiyas over Istihsan in Sajdah Tilawah During Prayer
Istinbat: conflict resolution between qiyas and istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tarjih to resolve a conflict between qiyas and istihsan in the case of sajdat al-tilawah during prayer, and explain why qiyas is preferred despite istihsan's apparent strength.

Core Idea
Qiyas can override istihsan when a companion practice (like Ibn Mas'ud's) gives it an external preponderance, acting like a consensus.

In this passage, we examine a nuanced usul al-fiqh scenario: a conflict between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) regarding whether a person praying can combine the ruku' of the prayer with the required sajdat al-tilawah by bowing with the intention of fulfilling both. On the surface, istihsan seems stronger, but the Hanafi school gives precedence to qiyas here due to a supporting report from Companions. This lesson will guide you through the reasoning and the conditions for this tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the legal issue
Identify the conflict: a person recites an ayah of sajdah during prayer. Can he combine the ruku' of the prayer with the tilawah prostration by bowing with intention of both?
This is a case where two usul sources (qiyas and istihsan) give divergent rulings.
2
Analyze the qiyas argument
Examine the analogy between ruku' and sujud based on similarity in humility and the Quranic usage of 'raki'an' for sujud.
Qiyas here is clear (jali) but formal.
3
Analyze the istihsan argument
Understand the istihsan: sujud is a higher form of veneration; ruku' does not substitute for it in prayer, so it should not substitute here either.
Istihsan appears sound at first glance (apparent effect).
4
Identify the hidden flaw in istihsan
Realize that sajdat al-tilawah is not an independent act of worship; its purpose is humility, which is also achieved by ruku' in prayer.
This flaw weakens the istihsan's basis.
5
Apply tarjih: why qiyas is preferred
The qiyas gains preponderance due to a report from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar allowing the practice, with no contrary report, acting like a consensus.
This external support outweighs the apparent strength of istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذي ظهر أثره وخفي فساده كما إذ تُلي آية السجدة في صلاته فإنه يركع بها قياسًا، وفي الاستحسان لا يجزئه الأصل في هذا أنه إن قرأ آية السجدة يسجد لها، ثم يقوم فيقرأ ما بقي، ويركع إذا جاء أوان الركوع، وإن ركع في موضع آية السجدة وينوي التداخل بين ركوع الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة كما هو المعروف بين الحفاظ يجوز قياسًا لا استحسانًا، وجه القياس أن الركوع والسجود متشابهان في الخضوع، ولهذا أطلق الركوع على السجود في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَرَّ رَاكِعاً وَأَنَابَ﴾، وجه الاستحسان: أنا أُمرنا بالسجود وهو غاية التعظيم والركوعُ دونه، ولهذا لا ينوب عنه في الصلاة، فكذا في سجدة التلاوة، فهذا الاستحسان ظاهر أثره، ولكن خفي فساده، وهو أن السجود في التلاوة لم يشرع قربةً مقصودةً بنفسها وإنما المقصود التواضع والركوع في الصلاة يعمل هذا العمل أي التواضع. الذي ظهر أثره أي إذا نظر بأدنى نظر يُرى صحته، ثم إذا تأمل حق التأمل علم أنه فاسد (القمر) يركع بها: أي إن شاء، إلا أن الركوع يحتاج إلى النية دون السجدة كذا قال ابن الملك لله. (القمر) يجوز إلخ بشرط إن نوى أداءها، نص عليه محمد الله؛ لأن معنى التعظيم فيهما واحد، وينبغي ذلك التداخل للإمام مع كثرة القوم أو حال المخافة حتى لا يؤدّي إلى التخليط (السنبلي) لا استحسانا: لأن القياس في هذه المسألة مقدّم على الاستحسان قال محمد الله وبالقياس نأخذ وإن كان الأصل هو العمل بالاستحسان؛ لأن القياس ترجح بما روي عن ابن مسعود وابن عمر له أنهما أجاز أن يركع عن السجود في الصلاة، ولم يرد غيرهما خلافه، فكان كالإجماع، فقدّم على الاستحسان لوجود المرجّح، إلخ. من الطحطاوي.(السنبلي) متشابهان : أي صورةً، وهذا القياس الجلى فاسد ظاهرًا؛ لأن المشابهة الصورية لا تفيد حكما شرعيا . (القمر) وخرّ أي داود عليه راكعا أي ساجدًا، سمي السجود ركوعًا؛ لأنه مبدأ السجود أناب أي رجع إلى الله تعالى بالتوبة، كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) إنا أمرنا بالسجود قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْجُدُوا لِلَّهِ وَاعْبُدُوا﴾ (النجم: 62) وأيضًا ﴿وَاسْجُدْ وَاقْتَرِبْ﴾ (العلق: 19) وما في "مسير الدائر" فاسجد واقترب فليس في القرآن.(القمر) لا ينوب أي الركوع عنه أي عن السجدة. (القمر) ولكن خفي فساده فصار القياس قوي أثر الباطن. (القمر) قربةً مقصودةً ولهذا لا يلزم بالنذر كما لا يلزم الوضوء بالنذر. (القمر) التواضع ليحصل مخالفة المشركين فإنهم استكبروا و لم يتواضعوا. (القمر)
[The case] where its effect appeared and its flaw was hidden, as when an ayah of sajdah is recited in his prayer, then he bows (ruku') with it by qiyas, and in istihsan it does not suffice him. The basis is: if he recites an ayah of sajdah, he performs prostration for it, then stands and recites what remains, and bows when the time for ruku' comes. If he bows in the place of the sajdah ayah and intends overlap between the prayer's ruku' and the tilawah prostration, as is known among the memorizers, it is permissible by qiyas, not by istihsan. The face of qiyas: ruku' and sujud are similar in humility, and for this reason ruku' was used for sujud in His statement: {And he fell down bowing (raki'an) and repented}. The face of istihsan: We are commanded to perform sujud, and it is the ultimate act of veneration, while ruku' is below it; for this reason ruku' does not substitute for it in prayer, so likewise in tilawah prostration. This istihsan has apparent effect, but its flaw is hidden: the tilawah prostration was not prescribed as an independent act of worship intended for itself, rather the purpose is humility, and the ruku' in prayer achieves this purpose (i.e., humility). (Al-Qamar) 'Whose effect appeared': i.e., when looked at with the slightest consideration its correctness is seen, but when one reflects carefully, one knows it is flawed. (Al-Qamar) 'He bows with it': i.e., if he wishes, except that bowing requires intention while prostration does not, as Ibn al-Malak said. (Al-Qamar) 'Permissible': subject to the condition that he intends to perform it; Muhammad (al-Shaybani) textually stated this because the meaning of veneration is the same in both. This overlap is recommended for the imam with a large congregation or in fear, so that it does not lead to confusion. (Al-Sanbali) 'Not by istihsan': because qiyas in this issue is given precedence over istihsan. Muhammad (al-Shaybani) said: 'We take by qiyas even though the original practice is to act by istihsan because qiyas was given weight by what was reported from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) that they allowed bowing instead of prostration in prayer, and no one contradicted them, so it was like consensus, so qiyas was given precedence over istihsan due to the presence of a preponderant factor.' From al-Tahtawi. (Al-Sanbali) 'Similar in form': this clear qiyas is apparently flawed because formal similarity does not produce legal rulings. (Al-Qamar) 'And he fell down': i.e., David (peace be upon him) as bowing (raki'an), i.e., prostrating; sujud is called ruku' because it is the beginning of sujud. 'Anaba' means returned to Allah in repentance. (Al-Qamar) 'We are commanded to prostrate': Allah said {Prostrate to Allah and worship} and also {Prostrate and draw near}. (Al-Qamar) 'Does not substitute': i.e., ruku' does not substitute for prostration. (Al-Qamar) 'But its flaw was hidden': so qiyas became strong in its hidden effect. (Al-Qamar) 'Intended as an act of worship': for this reason it is not obligated by vow, as ablution is not obligated by vow. (Al-Qamar) 'Humility': to achieve opposing the polytheists, for they were arrogant and did not humble themselves.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a detailed case analysis (istinbat) of a fiqh issue: when a person recites an ayah of sajdah (prostration) during prayer, can he combine the prayer's ruku' (bowing) with the required sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation) by bowing with the intention of fulfilling both? The analysis applies the rule from the previous page: sometimes qiyas (clear analogy) is preferred over istihsan due to its strong hidden effect. Here, qiyas draws an analogy between ruku' and sujud based on their formal similarity in humility, citing the Quranic usage of 'raki'an' to mean prostrating (referring to Prophet Dawud). Qiyas allows combining them with proper intention. Istihsan, however, forbids it because sujud is a higher form of veneration and does not substitute for ruku' in prayer; analogously, it should not do so for tilawah. The istihsan appears sound (apparent effect) but is flawed because tilawah prostration is not an independent act of worship; its purpose is humility, which is also achieved by ruku'. Despite this, the text concludes that in this specific case, qiyas is given precedence over istihsan due to a report from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar permitting the practice, which, with no contrary report, acts like consensus. This is a rare case where qiyas outweighs istihsan, as noted earlier. The commentary clarifies conditions: the intention must be present, and overlapping is recommended for the imam to avoid confusion.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed when reciting certain verses of the Quran.
قياس (qiyas): Clear analogy that compares the formal similarity between ruku' and sujud.
استحسان (istihsan): Hidden analogy that forbids combining because ruku' is lesser than sujud and cannot substitute.
ظهور الأثر (zuhur al-athar): Apparent effect: the istihsan seems sound at first glance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of reciting an ayah of sajdah during prayer, why is qiyas (allowing ruku' to stand for sujud) given precedence over istihsan (prohibiting it)?
A) Because qiyas is always stronger than istihsan
B) Because of a report from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar permitting it, which acts like a consensus
C) Because the Quran explicitly allows it
D) Because istihsan is invalid in Hanafi school

Key Takeaway
Qiyas can be given precedence over istihsan when supported by an external preponderant factor, such as companion practice, which acts like a consensus.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Istiḥsān vs Qiyas: Substituting Ruku' for Sajdah Tilawah in Prayer
Analysis of istihsan vs qiyas in a specific fiqhi case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of preferring qiyas over istihsan when supported by athar (companion reports) and identify the hidden invalidity (khufi fasad) in the istihsan argument.

Core Idea
Qiyas can override istihsan when companion reports give it preponderance, even if the istihsan seems sound at first.

This passage presents a classic usul debate: when a person recites a prostration verse during prayer, may he substitute ruku' (bowing) for the sajdah tilawah? The Hanafi school resolves this by weighing qiyas against istihsan, ultimately preferring qiyas due to transmitted evidence. You will learn how the school evaluates these two sources and the conditions under which one prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two conflicting methods
A worshipper recites a sajdah verse during prayer and performs ruku', intending it to fulfill both the obligatory ruku' and the wajib sajdah tilawah. The question: is this substitution valid? By qiyas it is valid; by istihsan it is not.
2
Examine the qiyas argument
Qiyas argues that ruku' and sajdah share the quality of humility (khushu'). The Quran uses 'bowing' to mean 'prostration' in the story of Prophet Dawud (38:24/44). Thus, the same goal is achieved.
This is a qiyas in the form of shabah (similarity).
3
Examine the istihsan argument
Istihsan argues that prostration is the highest form of veneration, while bowing is lower. The Quran commands prostration explicitly (53:62, 96:19). In regular prayer, bowing does not substitute for prostration, so it should not here either.
This istihsan is based on the apparent strength of the command (amr).
4
Identify the hidden invalidity in the istihsan
Upon deeper reflection, sajdah tilawah is not an intrinsically intended act of worship (qurbah maqsudah bi nafsiha); it is a means to show humility. Ruku' in prayer achieves the same humility, so the substitution is valid.
The invalidity is hidden (khafi) because the apparent strength of the command is misleading.
5
See how companion reports tip the scale
Reports from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar permit bowing instead of prostration in prayer. No companion opposed them, making it like consensus (ijma'). This gives preponderance (tarjih) to the qiyas over istihsan.
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani explicitly adopts this qiyas.

باب القياس بيان الاستحسان الذي ظهر أثره وخفي فساده كما إذ تُلي آية السجدة في صلاته فإنه يركع بها قياسًا، وفي الاستحسان لا يجزئه الأصل في هذا أنه إن قرأ آية السجدة يسجد لها، ثم يقوم فيقرأ ما بقي، ويركع إذا جاء أوان الركوع، وإن ركع في موضع آية السجدة وينوي التداخل بين ركوع الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة كما هو المعروف بين الحفاظ يجوز قياسًا لا استحسانًا، وجه القياس أن الركوع والسجود متشابهان في الخضوع، ولهذا أطلق الركوع على السجود في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَرَّ رَاكِعاً وَأَنَابَ﴾، وجه الاستحسان: أنا أُمرنا بالسجود وهو غاية التعظيم والركوع دونه، ولهذا لا ينوب عنه في الصلاة، فكذا في سجدة التلاوة، فهذا الاستحسان ظاهر أثره، ولكن خفي فساده، وهو أن السجود في التلاوة لم يشرع قربةً مقصودةً بنفسها وإنما المقصود التواضع والركوع في الصلاة يعمل هذا العمل (التواضع) الذي ظهر أثره أي إذا نظر بأدنى نظر يُرى صحته، ثم إذا تأمل حق التأمل علم أنه فاسد (القمر) يركع بها: أي إن شاء، إلا أن الركوع يحتاج إلى النية دون السجدة كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) يجوز إلخ بشرط إن نوى أداءها، فيه نص عليه محمد؛ لأن معنى التعظيم فيهما واحد، وينبغي ذلك التداخل للإمام مع كثرة القوم أو حال المخافة حتى لا يؤدّي إلى التخليط (السنبلي) لا استحسانا: لأن القياس في هذه المسألة مقدّم على الاستحسان قال محمد وبالقياس نأخذ وإن كان الأصل هو العمل بالاستحسان؛ لأن القياس ترجح بما روي عن ابن مسعود وابن عمر أنهما أجاز أن يركع عن السجود في الصلاة، ولم يرد غيرهما خلافه، فكان كالإجماع، فقدّم على الاستحسان لوجود المرجّح، إلخ. من الطحطاوي. (السنبلي) متشابهان : أي صورةً، وهذا القياس الجلى فاسد ظاهرًا؛ لأن المشابهة الصورية لا تفيد حكما شرعيا . (القمر) وخرّ أي داود عليه راكعا أي ساجدًا، سمي السجود ركوعًا؛ لأنه مبدأ السجود أناب أي رجع إلى الله تعالى بالتوبة، كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) إنا أمرنا بالسجود قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْجُدُوا لِلَّهِ وَاعْبُدُوا﴾ (النجم: ٦٢) وأيضًا ﴿وَاسْجُدْ وَاقْتَرِبْ﴾ (العلق : ١٩) وما في "مسير الدائر" فاسجد واقترب فليس في القرآن. (القمر) لا ينوب أي الركوع عنه أي عن السجدة. (القمر) ولكن خفي فساده فصار القياس قوي أثر الباطن. (القمر) قربةً مقصودةً ولهذا لا يلزم بالنذر كما لا يلزم الوضوء بالنذر. (القمر) التواضع ليحصل مخالفة المشركين فإنهم استكبروا و لم يتواضعوا. (القمر) لا خارجها فلهذا لم نعمل به بل عملنا بالقياس المستترة صحته، وقلنا: يجوز إقامة الركوع مقام سجود التلاوة، بخلاف الصلاة فإن الركوع فيها مقصود على حدة والسجود على حدة، فلا ينوب أحدهما عن الآخر. ثم المستحسن بالقياس الخفي تصح تعديته إلى غيره؛ لأنه أحد القياسين، غايته أنه خفي يقابل الجلي، بخلاف الأقسام الأخر، يعني ما يكون بالأثر أو الإجماع أو الضرورة؛ لأنها معدولة عن القياس من كل وجه، ألا ترى أن الاختلاف في الثمن قبل قبض المبيع لا يوجب يمين البائع قياسًا، ويوجبه استحسانًا؛ فإنه إذا اختلفا في الثمن بدون قبض المبيع بأن قال البائع: بعتها بألفين وقال المشتري اشتريتها بألف فالقياس أن لا يحلف البائع؛ لأن المشتري لا يدعي عليه شيئًا حتى يكون هو منكرا، لا خارجها يعني أن الركوع خارج الصلاة لا ينوب عن سجدة التلاوة؛ لأن الركوع في غير الصلاة ليست قربةً ولا يحصل به التعظيم، فلا يتأدّى به سجدة التلاوة. (القمر) وقلنا يجوز إلخ كما يقوم الطهارة لغير الصلاة للطهارة للصلاة الحصول المقصود. (القمر) هذا تقرير عامة المشايخ، وقال محمد بن سلمة ما حاصله يرجع إلى أنه حكم بتقديم القياس على الاستحسان والقياس الظاهر ههنا صحة إقامة السجدة الصلبية مقام التلاوتية، والاستحسان عدم الصحة؛ لأن الصلبية قائمة مقام نفسها، فلا تقوم مقام غيرها، وجعل تأديتها بالركوع استحسانا والقياس يأباه؛ لأنه جعل القياس هو الظاهر، ومقابله هو الاستحسان كذا لخصته "الطحطاوي" و "المراقي" . (السنبلي) بخلاف الصلاة إلخ: دفع دخل، تقريره: أن الركوع في الصلاة لا يتأدّى به السجدة الصلاتية، فينبغي أن لا يتأدّى بالركوع سجدة التلاوة أيضًا لأنها مثلها؟ وحاصل الدفع منع المماثلة. (القمر) على حدة: لوقوع الأمر مستقلاً لكل واحد من الركوع والسجود. (القمر) ثم المستحسن إلخ: أي الحكم المستحسن بالعلة الخفية، فالمراد بالقياس العلة؛ إذ لا يجوز القياس على الفرع كما هو الصحيح، والمراد بالتعدية إثبات ذلك الحكم في محل آخر، كذا قال أعظم العلماء مولانا عبد السلام لله (القمر) من المستحسن أي الحكم الثابت بالاستحسان (المحشي) إلى غيره : أي إذا وُجد فيه تلك العلة. (القمر) بالأثر : أي النص الكتابي أو الحديث (القمر) لأنها أي لأن هذه الثلاثة صارت معارضة للقياس، فصارت هذه الثلاثة مخالفة للقياس، فلا تتعدّى إلى شيء. (القمر) أن الاختلاف أي اختلاف البائع والمشتري. (القمر) حتى يكون هو : أي البائع منكراً ، والحلف لا يكون إلا على المنكر. (القمر)
Chapter on Qiyas. Explanation of istiḥsān whose effect appears but whose invalidity is hidden: as when a verse of sajdah is recited in his prayer, then he performs ruku' with it by qiyas, and by istiḥsān it does not suffice him. The basis in this is that if he recites a verse of sajdah, he prostrates for it, then stands and recites what remains, and bows when the time for bowing comes. And if he bows in the place of the verse of sajdah and intends an overlap between the bowing of the prayer and the prostration of recitation, as is known among the memorizers, it is permissible by qiyas, not by istiḥsān. The face of qiyas: that bowing and prostrating are similar in humility, and for this bowing is applied to prostration in His saying: 'And he fell down bowing and repented.' The face of istiḥsān: we are commanded to prostrate, which is the utmost veneration, and bowing is below it; for this reason it does not substitute for it in prayer, so likewise in the prostration of recitation. So this istiḥsān has an apparent effect, but its invalidity is hidden, namely that the prostration in recitation was not legislated as an intrinsically intended act of worship; rather the intended goal is humility, and bowing in prayer performs this act (humility) which appears effective. When one looks with minimal consideration, its soundness is seen, but when one reflects thoroughly, one knows it is invalid. (Al-Qamar) 'he bows with it': meaning if he wishes, except that bowing requires intention while prostration does not, as Ibn al-Malik said. (Al-Qamar) 'it is permissible etc.' with the condition that he intends to perform it; Muhammad [al-Shaybani] explicitly stated this because the meaning of veneration is the same in both. And this overlap is recommended for the imam when the congregation is large or in a state of fear, so as not to lead to confusion. (As-Sanbalī) 'not istiḥsānan': because qiyas in this issue is given precedence over istiḥsān. Muhammad said: we adopt qiyas even though the principle is to act by istiḥsān; because qiyas is preponderated by what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they permitted bowing instead of prostration in prayer, and no one else opposed them, so it was like consensus, so it was given precedence over istiḥsān due to the existence of a preponderator, etc. from Aṭ-Ṭaḥṭāwī. (As-Sanbalī) 'similar': i.e., in form, and this obvious qiyas is apparently invalid because formal similarity does not produce a legal ruling. (Al-Qamar) 'And he fell': i.e., David, peace be upon him, 'bowing' i.e. prostrating. Prostration is called bowing because it is the beginning of prostration. 'Anaba' i.e., returned to Allah Almighty in repentance, as al-Bayḍāwī said. (Al-Qamar) 'We are commanded to prostrate': Allah said: 'So prostrate to Allah and worship' (53:62) and also 'And prostrate and draw near' (96:19). What is in "Masīr ad-Dā'ir" 'fasjud waqtarib' is not in the Qur'an. (Al-Qamar) 'does not substitute': i.e., bowing does not substitute for prostration. (Al-Qamar) 'but its invalidity is hidden' so the qiyas became strong in inner effect. (Al-Qamar) 'an intrinsically intended act of worship': for this it is not necessary by vow just as ablution is not necessary by vow. (Al-Qamar) 'humility': to achieve opposition to the polytheists who were arrogant and did not humble themselves. (Al-Qamar) 'outside it': so for this we did not act by it, but we acted by qiyas whose soundness is hidden, and we said: it is permissible to substitute bowing for the prostration of recitation, unlike the prayer, because bowing in it is intended separately and prostration separately, so one does not substitute for the other. Then the ruling preferred by hidden qiyas may be extended to another case because it is one of the two qiyases, the difference being that it is hidden as opposed to obvious. Unlike the other categories, meaning those based on transmitted text or consensus or necessity, because they are deviated from qiyas completely. Do you not see that disagreement about the price before taking possession of the sold item does not necessitate an oath from the seller by qiyas, but by istiḥsān it does? For if they disagree about the price without taking possession, the seller saying 'I sold it for two thousand' and the buyer saying 'I bought it for one thousand', by qiyas the seller is not to take an oath because the buyer does not claim anything against him such that he would be the denier. 'outside it': meaning that bowing outside prayer does not substitute for the prostration of recitation because bowing outside prayer is not an act of worship and does not achieve veneration, so the prostration of recitation is not performed by it. (Al-Qamar) 'and we said it is permissible etc.' just as purification for non-prayer substitutes for purification for prayer in achieving the intended goal. (Al-Qamar) This is the determination of the general body of shaykhs. And Muhammad ibn Salama said something summarized as: it returns to the ruling of giving precedence to qiyas over istiḥsān, and the apparent qiyas here is the soundness of substituting the structural prostration for the recitation prostration, and istiḥsān is the lack of soundness because the structural prostration stands in place of itself, so it does not stand in place of another. His making performing it by bowing istiḥsān, and qiyas rejects it, because he made qiyas the apparent and its opposite is istiḥsān. This is how I summarized from Aṭ-Ṭaḥṭāwī and Al-Marāqī. (As-Sanbalī) 'unlike the prayer etc.': repelling an objection, its summary: that bowing in prayer does not fulfill the prayer's prostration, so it should not fulfill the recitation's prostration either because it is like it? The gist of the rebuttal is the denial of similarity. (Al-Qamar) 'separately': because the command occurs independently for each of bowing and prostrating. (Al-Qamar) 'then the preferred (mustaḥsan)' etc.: i.e., the ruling preferred by a hidden cause, by 'qiyas' meaning the cause, since it is not permissible to perform qiyas on the branch, as is the correct view. By 'extension' is meant establishing that ruling in another place, as said by the greatest scholar Maulānā Abdul Salām (Al-Qamar). 'from the preferred': i.e., the ruling established by istiḥsān (the marginal) 'to another': i.e., if that cause is found. (Al-Qamar) 'by transmitted text': i.e., scriptural text or hadith. (Al-Qamar) 'because they': i.e., because these three became opposed to qiyas, so these three are contrary to qiyas, so they are not extended to anything. (Al-Qamar) 'that the disagreement': i.e., disagreement between seller and buyer. (Al-Qamar) 'so that he is': i.e., the seller is the denier, and the oath is only taken by the denier. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the foundational usul tool of istihsan (juristic preference) as compared to qiyas (analogy). The author presents a specific fiqhi case: when a person recites a verse that requires prostration (ayat al-sajdah) during prayer, may he substitute the ruku' (bowing) for the sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation)? The text states that by qiyas, this substitution is permissible because both bowing and prostration involve humility, and indeed the Quran uses 'bowing' to mean 'prostration' in the story of Prophet Dawud (peace be upon him). By istihsan, however, the substitution is not valid because prostration is a higher form of veneration than bowing and is commanded separately. The author explains that this istihsan has an apparent soundness but hidden invalidity: the sajdah tilawah is not an intrinsically intended act of worship (qurbah maqsudah bi nafsiha) but rather a means to show humility, and bowing in prayer achieves that humility. Therefore, the qiyas is valid. The Hanafi school ultimately adopts the qiyas over istihsan in this case, not because istihsan is weak, but because the qiyas is supported by transmitted reports (athar) from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) who permitted bowing instead of prostration in prayer. Since no companion opposed them, this is like consensus (ijma'), giving preponderance (tarjih) to the qiyas. The passage then broadens the discussion: a ruling established by hidden qiyas can be extended to other cases because it is still a type of qiyas, unlike rulings based on text (nass), consensus (ijma'), or necessity (darurah), which are not analogically extended. An example is given: disagreement over price before taking possession of a sold item—by qiyas the seller does not take an oath because the buyer is not claiming anything, but by istihsan he does take an oath due to other considerations. The passage concludes that this istihsan is confined to its specific context and cannot be generalized. Throughout, the text reconciles the tension between qiyas and istihsan, showing that the Hanafi school does not always prefer istihsan over qiyas; rather, the stronger evidence prevails.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical deduction: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illah).
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference: departing from the apparent qiyas in favor of a stronger evidence or a more suitable ruling based on considerations of public interest, necessity, or a deeper understanding of the Law.
السجدة (as-sajdah): Prostration; an act of worship involving placing the forehead on the ground. In this context, it refers to both the obligatory prostration in prayer (sajdah salat) and the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah) upon reciting a specific verse.
الركوع (ar-rukū'): Bowing in prayer: bending the torso so that the hands reach the knees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a person recites a verse of sajdah in prayer and performs ruku' intending both the ruku' of prayer and the sajdah tilawah, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) It is valid by qiyas but not by istihsan.
B) It is valid by istihsan but not by qiyas.
C) It is invalid by both qiyas and istihsan.
D) It is valid by ijma' (consensus).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits substituting ruku' for sajdah tilawah in prayer by qiyas, because companion reports give preponderance to qiyas over the seemingly strong istihsan.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
The Ruling on Specifying a Derived Cause in Qiyas
Explains the ruling on specifying a derived cause and the internal Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on specifying a derived cause and evaluate the counter-argument from those who allow it.

Core Idea
A derived cause cannot be specified—claiming a preventer contradicts the cause’s validity and makes every mujtahid correct.

This passage addresses an internal Hanafi debate: can a mujtahid rescue his derived cause from a counterexample (naqd) by claiming that a preventer (māniʿ) blocked the ruling? The majority says no; a minority says yes. Understanding this rule is crucial for constructing sound qiyas arguments and avoiding logical contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Define takhṣīṣ al-ʿillah (specification of the cause) and distinguish it from denying the cause's existence. Note that the cause here is a derived cause (mustanbaṭah), not a textual one.
Specification = cause is acknowledged but a preventer is claimed.
2
State the majority position and its proof
The Hanafi majority (author's view) holds that specification is not allowed. The proof is rational: if allowed, every mujtahid could claim a preventer to defend any objection, leading to taṣwīb (everyone correct).
The proof is a qiyās argument (dalīl ʿaqlī).
3
State the minority position and its reasoning
Some Hanafis (mashāyikh al-ʿIrāq, al-Karkhī, Qāḍī Abū Zayd) allow specification. Their reasoning: the derived cause is merely an indicator (amārah), not a full cause that necessitates the ruling. An indicator can be present in some cases and absent in others.
They analogize to clouds as an indicator of rain.
4
Analyze the majority's response to the minority
The majority responds that claiming a preventer leads to contradiction: first the mujtahid asserts the cause is valid, then after the objection he claims it is prevented. This inconsistency makes the claim unacceptable. In contrast, denying the cause's existence (due to a missing condition) involves no contradiction.
The counterexample of the forgetful fasting person illustrates the point.
5
Distinguish between derived and textual causes
The passage notes that specification is more accepted for textual causes (ʿillah manṣūṣah) because they are less prone to contradiction. For derived causes, the rule is stricter to preserve the integrity of ijtihād.
Zinā and theft are textual causes; they are not applied in all situations due to preventers, but this is not specification of a derived cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس

بيان تخصيص العلة المستنبطة

ولهذا أي ولأجل أن المجتهد يخطئ ويصيب قلنا: لا يجوز تخصيص العلة، وهو أن يقول: كانت علتي حقة مؤثرة لكن تخلف الحكم عنها لمانع؛ وموجودة في الفرع أي موجب ذلك الحكم لأنه يؤدي إلى تصويب كل مجتهد؛ إذ لا يعجز مجتهد ما عن هذا القول، فيكون كل منهم مصيبا في استنباط العلة خلافا للبعض كمشايخ العراق والكرخي، فإنهم جوزوا تخصيص العلة وكالقاضي أبي زيد المستنبط؛ لأن العلة أمارة على الحكم، فجاز أن يجعل أمارة في بعض المواضع دون البعض. وإنما قيدت العلة بالمستنبط؛ لأن العلة المنصوصة ذهب إلى تخصيصها كثير من الفقهاء.

لأن الزنا والسرقة علة للجلد والقطع، ومع ذلك لا يجلد ولا يقطع في بعض المواضع لمانع. وذلك أي بيان تخصيص العلة أن يقول: كانت علتي توجب ذلك لكنه لم يجب مع قيامها لمانع، فصار المحل الذي لم يثبت الحكم فيه مخصوصا من العلة بهذا الدليل. وعندنا عدم الحكم بناء على عدم العلة بأن يقول: لم توجد في محل الخلاف العلة؛ لأنها لم تصلح كونها علة مع قيام المانع.

فإن قيل: على هذا أيضًا يلزم تصويب كل مجتهد؛ إذ لا يعجز أحد عن أن يقول: لم تكن العلة موجودة ههنا، أجيب بأن في بيان المانع يلزم التناقض؛ إذ ادعى أولا صحة العلة، ثم بعد ورود النقض ادعى المانع، فلا يقبل أصلاً، بخلاف بيان عدم وجود الدليل؛ إذ لا يلزم فيه التناقض، فلهذا يقبل.

وبيان ذلك في الصائم النائم إذا صب الماء في حلقه بالإكراه أو في النوم أنه يفسد الصوم؛ لفوات ركنه وهو الإمساك. ويلزم عليه الناسي؛ فإنه لا يفسد صومه مع فوات ركنه.
Chapter of Analogy. Explanation of the specification of the derived cause. And for this, i.e., because the mujtahid errs and hits the mark, we said: It is not permissible to specify the cause, which is for him to say: My cause was true and effective, but the ruling is absent due to a preventer; and it exists in the branch, i.e., the cause of that ruling. Because it leads to deeming every mujtahid correct; since no mujtahid is incapable of this statement, so each of them would be correct in deriving the cause, contrary to some like the shaykhs of Iraq and al-Karkhī, for they permitted specifying the cause, and like Qāḍī Abū Zayd the derived (cause); because the cause is an indicator of the ruling, so it is permissible to make it an indicator in some places and not in others. And the cause is restricted to the derived one because the textual cause - many jurists have gone to specifying it. Because zinā and theft are causes for flogging and amputation, yet they are not flogged or amputated in some places due to a preventer. And that, i.e., the explanation of specifying the cause is for him to say: My cause necessitated that, but it was not necessitated with its existence due to a preventer, so the locus in which the ruling is not established becomes specified from the cause by this proof. And with us, the absence of the ruling is based on the absence of the cause, by his saying: The cause did not exist in the locus of dispute; because it was not fit to be a cause with the preventer present. If it is said: This also necessitates deeming every mujtahid correct; since no one is incapable of saying: The cause did not exist here. The answer is that in explaining the preventer there is contradiction; since he first claimed the validity of the cause, then after the objection he claimed a preventer, so it is not accepted at all. Unlike explaining the non-existence of the proof; for there is no contradiction therein, so it is accepted. And the explanation of that is in the case of a sleeping fasting person: if water is poured into his throat by force or in sleep, it breaks the fast; because its pillar, which is abstention, is lost. And the forgetful person is an objection: for his fast is not broken despite the loss of its pillar.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a dispute within the Hanafi school on whether a derived cause (ʿillah mustanbaṭah) in qiyas can be specified (takhṣīṣ). The majority of Hanafis, including the author, hold that specification is not allowed. Specification means that the mujtahid acknowledges his cause is effective in principle but claims that in a particular instance the ruling is absent due to a preventer (māniʿ) without denying the cause itself. The reasoning is that if such a claim were allowed, every mujtahid could always defend his cause against any objection by simply saying there is a preventer, thereby making every ijtihād correct (taṣwīb). This would undermine the very possibility of error. A minority among Hanafis—like the mashāyikh of Iraq, al-Karkhī, and Qāḍī Abū Zayd—allow specification. Their argument is that the derived cause is merely an indicator (amārah) of the ruling, not a complete cause that necessitates the ruling. An indicator can be present in some cases and absent in others, just as clouds are a sign of rain but rain may not come. The text then distinguishes the derived cause from a textual cause (ʿillah manṣūṣah, explicitly stated in revealed texts). Many jurists permit specification of textual causes because such texts are less prone to contradiction. The Hanafi position is further defended by noting that when a mujtahid claims a preventer, he contradicts himself: first he asserts the cause is valid, then he claims it is prevented. This contradiction makes his claim unacceptable. In contrast, when he argues that the cause is absent (due to a missing condition), there is no contradiction; he consistently holds that the cause was not actually present. The example of the fasting person illustrates this: a sleeping person who has water poured into his throat deliberately (or even while asleep) breaks his fast because the essential pillar (imṣāk) is lost. But the forgetful person (nāsī) does not break his fast despite the loss of abstention. In the Hanafi view, this is because the cause (the presence of a missing condition) is not established for the forgetful person; the ruling is absent due to the non-existence of the cause, not due to specification of the cause. Thus, the rule against specifying derived causes preserves the integrity of ijtihād and avoids granting every mujtahid automatic correctness.

Key Terms
العلة المستنبطة (al-ʿillah al-mustanbaṭah): A cause derived by ijtihad from the revealed texts, not explicitly stated.
تخصيص العلة (takhṣīṣ al-ʿillah): Claiming that a cause is effective in principle but that its ruling is absent in a particular case due to a preventer (māniʿ).
العلة المنصوصة (al-ʿillah al-manṣūṣah): A cause explicitly stated in the Quran or Sunna.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi argument against allowing specification (takhṣīṣ) of a derived cause?
A) It contradicts the Quran.
B) It leads to deeming every mujtahid correct (taṣwīb).
C) It is rejected by consensus.
D) It is only allowed for textual causes.

Key Takeaway
Specification of a derived cause is not allowed in the Hanafi school because it would make every mujtahid correct and involves contradiction; the correct response to a counterexample is to deny the cause's existence.

The Five Types of Preventers (Mawani') in Hanafi Usul
Enumeration and explanation of five types of preventers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five types of preventers (mawani') that block either the 'illa or the hukm, and distinguish them using Hanafi usul examples.

Core Idea
A preventer blocks the legal effect despite the apparent 'illa — but it may block the 'illa itself or the hukm at different stages.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar presents a five-fold classification of preventers (mawani') that can block the application of a legal ruling even when the cause ('illa) appears present. Understanding this classification is crucial for correctly analyzing khiyar options and other exceptions in mu'amalat. The passage builds on the earlier discussion of takhsis al-'illa (specifying the cause by a preventer).

Guided Path
1
State the purpose of the classification
Why are mawani' divided into five? What is the underlying principle?
The division depends on whether the preventer blocks the 'illa itself or the hukm, and at which stage.
2
Identify the first two types (preventers of the 'illa)
What blocks inception vs. completion? Give the examples from the passage.
Selling a free person blocks inception; selling another's property without permission blocks completion.
3
Identify the next three types (preventers of the hukm)
What blocks initiation, completion, and bindingness? Give the examples from the passage.
Khiyar al-shart blocks initiation; khiyar al-ru'ya blocks completion; khiyar al-'ayb blocks bindingness.
4
Analyze the subtle differences between the three preventers of hukm
How are initiation, completion, and bindingness distinct? Use the khiyar examples to illustrate.
Initiation: ownership does not start. Completion: ownership starts but can be undone without court. Bindingness: ownership is complete but contract can be rescinded via court.
5
Note the alternative classification
Some scholars reduce to two types (preventers of the 'illa); how does the text address this?
The passage follows the five-part classification of those who permit takhsis al-'illa, acknowledging the alternative view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُبنى على هذا، أي على بحث تخصيص العلة بالمانع. تقسيم الموانع وهي خمسة: مانع يمنع انعقاد العلة كبيع الحر؛ فإنه إذا باع الحر لا ينعقد البيع شرعًا وإن وُجد صورةً. ومانع يمنع تمام العلة كبيع عبد الغير بلا إذنه؛ فإنه ينعقد شرعًا لوجود المحل، ولكنه لا يتمّ ما لم يوجد رضاء المالك. ومانع يمنع ابتداء الحكم كخيار الشرط في البيع؛ فإنه وجدت العلة بتمامها، ولكن لم يبتدء الحكم، وهو الملك للخيار. ومانع يمنع تمام الحكم كخيار الرؤية؛ فإنه لا يمنع ثبوت الملك، ولكنه لم يتم معه، ولهذا يتمكن من له الخيار من فسخ العقد بدون قضاء أو رضاء. ومانع يمنع لزوم الحكم كخيار العيب؛ فإنه لا يمنع ثبوت الملك ولا تمامه حتى يتمكن المشتري من التصرف في المبيع، ولا يتمكن من الفسخ بدون قضاء أو رضاء، ولكنه يمنع لزومه؛ لأن له ولاية الردّ والفسخ، فلا يكون لازماً.
And upon this, i.e. upon the discussion of specifying the 'illa by a preventer, is built. The division of preventers: they are five: (1) A preventer that prevents the inception of the 'illa, like selling a free person; for if one sells a free person, the sale is not legally contracted even if it occurs in form. (2) A preventer that prevents the completion of the 'illa, like selling the property of another without his permission; for it is legally contracted due to the existence of the subject matter, but it is not completed until the owner's consent is obtained. (3) A preventer that prevents the initiation of the hukm, like the option of condition (khiyar al-shart) in a sale; for the 'illa has fully existed, but the hukm (ownership) has not initiated due to the option. (4) A preventer that prevents the completion of the hukm, like the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'ya); for it does not prevent the establishment of ownership, but it is not completed with it, and therefore the one with the option can rescind the contract without a court order or consent. (5) A preventer that prevents the bindingness of the hukm, like the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb); for it does not prevent the establishment of ownership nor its completion, to the extent that the buyer can dispose of the sold item, but he cannot rescind without a court order or consent, yet it prevents its bindingness because he has the authority to return and rescind, so it is not binding.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage classifies the five types of preventers that can block the application of a hukm even when the 'illa appears to exist. The first two prevent the 'illa itself: either from coming into existence (e.g., selling a free person, which is impossible as property) or from being complete (e.g., selling another's property without permission, which lacks full consent). The next three prevent the hukm at various stages: initiation (e.g., khiyar al-shart delays ownership), completion (e.g., khiyar al-ru'ya allows rescission without court), and bindingness (e.g., khiyar al-'ayb allows rescission for defects). Note that some scholars consider only the first two as genuine preventers of the 'illa, while the latter three are actually preventers of the hukm. This classification is foundational for understanding how legal causes operate in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
مانع (mani'): A preventer that blocks the legal effect of an 'illa or the hukm despite the apparent presence of the 'illa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Selling a free person
B) Selling the property of another without permission
C) Khiyar al-shart
D) Khiyar al-'ayb

Key Takeaway
The five types of preventers (mawani') systematically block either the 'illa or the hukm at different stages, with distinct examples from khiyar options in sale.

Five Impediments to the Ruling Despite the Cause
Enumeration and explanation of five types of mawani' al-hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the five types of mawani' that block a ruling at different stages, using examples from Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A ruling may be blocked at five stages: inception/completion of the cause, initiation/completion/bindingness of the ruling.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, a legal cause ('illah) does not always produce its ruling if an impediment (mani') intervenes. This lesson unpacks a refined classification by Sadr al-Shari'ah that distinguishes five distinct stages where a ruling can be prevented. Understanding these categories sharpens your ability to diagnose why a ruling does not apply, even when its cause appears present.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the basic concept of mani'
A mani' is something that prevents the ruling from occurring, initiating, completing, or becoming binding despite the existence of the cause. It is distinct from the absence of a condition.
A condition must be present for the ruling to exist; a mani' blocks a ruling even when its cause and conditions are present.
2
List the five categories from the text
Identify the five types mentioned: (1) مانع يمنع انعقاد العلة (implied), (2) مانع يمنع تمام العلة, (3) مانع يمنع ابتداء الحكم, (4) مانع يمنع تمام الحكم, (5) مانع يمنع لزوم الحكم.
The first two are about the cause itself; the next three about the ruling.
3
Understand why the first two were reclassified
Initially, the first two were considered specifications (takhsis) of the 'illah, but Sadr al-Shari'ah noted they actually prevent the 'illah from existing legally, so they are better treated as distinct impediments.
This avoids the theoretical objection that a ruling cannot follow a non-existent cause.
4
Match each category with its example
For each of the five, identify the concrete Hanafi example: selling another's property (completion of cause), option of stipulation (initiation of ruling), option of inspection (completion of ruling), option of defect (bindingness).
The first (inception of cause) is not explicitly given but understood as the case where the cause does not even begin.
5
Apply the classification to new cases
Practice identifying the stage affected in other fiqh scenarios, such as options or conditional contracts, to internalize the distinctions.
This skill is essential for correct legal analysis in mu'amalat.

Source Text

بيان أقسام موانع الحكم مع وجود العلة
ومانع يمنع تمام العلة كبيع عبد الغير بلا إذنه؛ فإنه ينعقد شرعًا لوجود المحل، ولكنه لا يتمّ ما لم يوجد رضاء المالك، وعَدّ هذين القسمين من قبيل تخصيص العلة مسامحة نشأت من فخر الإسلام الله؛ لأن التخصيص هو تخلّف الحكم مع وجود العلة، وههنا لم توجد العلة إلا أن يقال: إنها وجدت صورة وإن لم تُعتبر شرعًا، ولهذا عدل صاحب
أي للبائع
أي البيع
"التوضيح" إلى أن جملة ما يوجب عدم الحكم خمسة لئلا يرد عليه هذا الاعتراض. ومانع يمنع ابتداء الحكم كخيار الشرط في البيع؛ فإنه وجدت العلة بتمامها، ولكن لم يبتدء الحكم، وهو الملك للخيار. ومانع يمنع تمام الحكم كخيار الرؤية؛ فإنه لا يمنع ثبوت الملك، ولكنه لم يتم معه، ولهذا يتمكن من له الخيار من فسخ العقد بدون قضاء أو رضاء.

التمكن
Explanation of the divisions of impediments to the ruling with the existence of the cause. And an impediment that prevents the completion of the cause, like selling the property of another without his permission: it is contractually valid legally due to the existence of the subject matter, but it is not completed until the owner's consent is obtained. And counting these two divisions as a type of specification of the cause is a license originating from Fakhr al-Islam Lil? Because specification is the non-occurrence of the ruling despite the existence of the cause, and here the cause does not exist except if it is said that it existed in form even if not considered legally. For this reason, the author of al-Tawdih adjusted to a total of five things that necessitate the non-existence of the ruling, to avoid this objection. And an impediment that prevents the initiation of the ruling, like the option of stipulation in sale: the cause existed completely, but the ruling did not initiate, which is ownership due to the option. And an impediment that prevents the completion of the ruling, like the option of inspection: it does not prevent the affirmation of ownership, but it is not completed with it, and therefore the one with the option can rescind the contract without a court order or consent. And an impediment that prevents the bindingness of the ruling, like the option of defect: it does not prevent the affirmation of ownership nor its completion, so the buyer can dispose of the sold item, but he cannot rescind without a court order or consent, but it prevents its bindingness because he has the authority to return and rescind, so it is not binding.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the five types of impediments (mawani') that prevent the ruling (hukm) from taking effect despite the presence of its cause ('illah). The text discusses the classification by Sadr al-Shari'ah in al-Tawdih. The first two impediments mentioned in the text (those preventing the inception and completion of the cause) were initially considered as specifications of the 'illah, but Sadr al-Shari'ah reorganized them into five distinct categories to avoid confusion. The five are: (1) مانع يمنع انعقاد العلة - impediment preventing the inception of the cause (not explicitly detailed but implied), (2) مانع يمنع تمام العلة - impediment preventing the completion of the cause, e.g., selling someone else's property without permission; the contract is valid but requires owner's consent for completion, (3) مانع يمنع ابتداء الحكم - impediment preventing the initiation of the ruling, e.g., the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) in sale; ownership does not begin until the option period ends, (4) مانع يمنع تمام الحكم - impediment preventing the completion of the ruling, e.g., the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah); ownership is established but not complete so the buyer can rescind, (5) مانع يمنع لزوم الحكم - impediment preventing the bindingness of the ruling, e.g., the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb); ownership is complete but not binding because the buyer can return the item if a defect is found. The commentary from al-Qamar and others clarifies the rationale behind this classification.

Key Terms
مانع (mani'): Something that prevents the ruling from occurring, initiating, completing, or becoming binding despite the existence of the cause.
علة ('illah): The effective cause (ratio legis) that necessitates a ruling.
تخصيص العلة (takhsis al-'illah): The non-occurrence of the ruling despite the presence of the cause due to a specific exception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Selling the property of another without permission
B) The option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart)
C) The option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah)
D) The option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of mawani' into five types allows precise identification at which stage a ruling is blocked, enabling correct legal analysis.

Formal and Effective Causes and the First Rebuttal Method
Introduction to rebuttal methods for formal causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between formal (tardiyyah) and effective (mu'aththirah) causes in qiyas, and apply the first rebuttal method (al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah) in a dialectical exchange.

Core Idea
A formal cause is rebutted by conceding its logical implication while maintaining disagreement on the ruling.

In Hanafi usul, causes ('ilal) used in qiyas are divided into two types: formal (tardiyyah) and effective (mu'aththirah). The Shafi'is often rely on formal causes, which the Hanafis rebut using specific methods to force the opponent to demonstrate effectiveness. The first method, al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah, is a subtle technique: the objector accepts the logical consequence of the cause but still disputes the ruling, thereby exposing the cause's insufficiency. Understanding this method is key to mastering Hanafi dialectic.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of 'illah
Identify the key features of formal (tardiyyah) and effective (mu'aththirah) causes. Formal causes are derived by reason without textual or consensus proof of effectiveness; effective causes have such proof.
Hanafis reject formal causes as sufficient proofs; Shafi'is accept them.
2
Understand the four rebuttal methods for formal causes
The text mentions four methods; here we focus on the first: al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah. Recognize that this method involves conceding the proponent's logical implication while maintaining disagreement on the ruling.
This method does not outright reject the cause but exposes its lack of effectiveness.
3
Apply the method to the given example
Apply al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah to the Shafi'i argument that fasting requires specific intention because it is obligatory. The Hanafi objector accepts that obligatoriness would require intention, but disputes that it must be specific and at night.
The Hanafi position allows general intention before noon.
4
Analyze the dialectical exchange
See how this method forces the proponent to prove that the cause is effective in the specific ruling. If the proponent cannot, the objection stands.
This leads to the second stage: the proponent may need to refine the cause or switch to an effective cause.

ثم لما فرغ المصنف له عن بيان شرط القياس وركنه وحكمه شرع في بيان دفعه فقال: ثم العلل نوعان طردية ومؤثرة وعلى كل قسم ضروب من الدفع، فإن الطردية للشافعية، ونحن ندفعها على وجه يُلجئهم إلى القول بالتأثير، والمؤثرة لنا، وتدفعها الشافعية، ثم نجيبهم عن الدفع، وهذا البحث هو أساس المناظرة والمحاورة، وقد اقتبس علم المناظرة من هذا البحث للأصول، وجعل علمًا آخر، وتصرّف فيه بتغيير بعض القواعد وازديادها على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى.
أما الطردية فوجوه دفعها أربعة: القول بموجب العلة، أي قول المعترض بموجب علة المستدلّ، وهو التزام ما يلزمه المعلّل بتعليله مع بقاء الخلاف في الحكم المتنازع فيه كقولهم، أي قول الشافعية في صوم رمضان إنه صوم ،فرض فلا يتأدّى إلا بتعيين النية بأن يقول: بصوم غد نويت لفرض رمضان، فأوردوا العلة الطردية، وهي الفرضية للتعيين؛
بيان دفعه أي دفع قياس المعلّل . (المحشي) طردية: المراد بالطردية العلل التي استنبطت بالعقل، وما ثبت تأثيرها بنص أو إجماع في جنس الحكم المعلّل بها، بل إنما حكم بعليتها بالطرد وجودًا وعدمًا أو وجودًا فقط، والعلل المؤثرة ضدها، كذا قيل (القمر) ضروب أي أنواع من الاعتراضات (القمر) والمؤثرة لنا إلخ: مثاله التعليل بعلة التعليل بعلة الطواف في سقوط نجاسة سؤر سواكن البيوت اعتبارًا بالهرة والاحتجاج بالطرد كما يفعله الشافعية فاسد عند أهل التحقيق؛ لأنه لا بد من التمييز بين العلة والشرط، والطرد لا يصلح مميزا؛ لأنه يوجد مع الشرط كما يوجد مع العلة (السنبلي) المناظرة : هو توجّه المتخاصمين في النسبة بين الشيئين لإظهار الصواب. (القمر) فوجوه دفعها أربعة وهذا على تقدير تسليم أن العلل الطردية حجة، وإلا فلا حاجة إلى وجوه دفعها. (القمر) وهو: أي القول بموجب العلة التزام ما يلزمه إلخ أي تسليم ما يوجبه المستدل بتعليله مع بقاء الخلاف وثبوت مدعى المجيب، وهذا لا يخلو، إما أن يكون المعلّل غافلا عن مراد الخصم أو يكون الخصم غافلا عن مراد المعلل، وحينئذ لا بد للمعلّل من أن يبين مراده، فلا يكون بعد هذا البيان للخصم سبيل إلا الرجوع إلى الممانعة، كذا قيل، وقوله: "يلزمه" من الإلزام. Then, when the author finished explaining the condition of analogy, its pillar, and its ruling, he proceeded to explain its rebuttal. He said: Causes are of two types: formal (tardiyyah) and effective (mu'aththirah). For each type there are varieties of rebuttal. The formal [causes] belong to the Shafi'is, and we rebut them in a way that forces them to accept effectiveness. The effective [causes] belong to us, and the Shafi'is rebut them, then we respond to their rebuttal. This discussion is the foundation of dialectic and debate. The science of dialectic was derived from this research in usul and made into a separate science, with changes to some rules and additions, as we will explain, God willing. As for the formal [causes], their methods of rebuttal are four: (1) al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah, that is, the objector's statement according to the requirement of the proponent's cause, which is conceding what the proponent necessitates by his reasoning while maintaining disagreement on the disputed ruling. Example: the Shafi'is' statement concerning the fast of Ramadan: it is a obligatory fast, so it is not performed except with specific intention, saying: 'I intend to fast tomorrow for the obligatory Ramadan fast.' They adduced the formal cause, which is obligatoriness for specific intention.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of rebuttal (daf') in the context of qiyas. It classifies causes ('ilal) into two types: formal (tardiyyah) and effective (mu'aththirah). Formal causes are those derived by reason without textual or consensus proof of their effectiveness in the genus of the ruling; they are used by the Shafi'is. The Hanafis rebut them to compel recognition of effectiveness. Effective causes are those whose effectiveness is established; they are used by Hanafis, and the Shafi'is rebut them. The text then details the first of four methods of rebutting a formal cause: 'al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah' (accepting the logical consequence of the cause). This means the objector concedes that if the proponent's cause were valid, it would entail the claimed effect, but he maintains his disagreement on the actual ruling. An example is given: Shafi'is argue that fasting Ramadan requires specific intention because it is obligatory, so they use obligatoriness as a formal cause for the requirement of specific intention. The Hanafi rebuttal is to accept that obligatoriness would require intention in principle but dispute that it specifically requires explicit intention at night, as Hanafis allow intention before noon. The commentary from al-Qamar and al-Sanabli provides further definitions: formal causes are those whose effectiveness is not established by text or consensus; they are judged by concomitance (tard) in existence and non-existence or existence only. Effective causes are the opposite. The science of dialectic (munazarah) is based on this usul discussion.

Key Terms
العلة الطردية (al-'illah al-tardiyyah): A cause derived by rational inference whose effectiveness in the genus of the ruling is not established by text or consensus; it is judged only by concomitance (tard).
العلة المؤثرة (al-'illah al-mu'aththirah): A cause whose effectiveness in the ruling is established by text, consensus, or clear reasoning.
القول بموجب العلة (al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah): The first method of rebutting a formal cause: conceding the logical implication of the cause while maintaining disagreement on the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah' (القول بموجب العلة) mean as a method of rebuttal?
A) Rejecting the proponent's cause entirely
B) Accepting the logical consequence of the cause while maintaining disagreement on the ruling
C) Attacking the opponent's character
D) Changing the subject of debate

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a formal cause is rebutted by al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah: concede the implication, dispute the ruling, and demand proof of effectiveness.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
The Four Types of Mumana'ah in Qiyas
Classification of four types of objection in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four types of mumana'ah in qiyas and identify which type applies to a given objection.

Core Idea
Mumana'ah rejects a premise; it has four forms: denying the description, its validity, its existence, or the proof itself.

This passage from the Hanafi usul tradition defines mumana'ah (objection) and enumerates four distinct types based on what aspect of the analogical proof is contested. Understanding these types sharpens your ability to both construct and critique qiyas arguments. A critical refinement by the commentator al-Qamar clarifies the classification.

Guided Path
1
Define Mumana'ah and Its Features
Understand the definition: 'non-acceptance by the questioner of some or all premises of the proof of the one providing the cause, with specification and detail.' Identify that it requires specificity and can target any premise.
Mumana'ah is valid only when the opponent's proof is flawed. It is a dialectical tool, not mere denial.
2
Learn the Four Types by Induction
The text enumerates four types: (1) objection to the description itself (denying that the claimed description is the cause), (2) objection to its validity for the ruling while it exists (denying that the description is effective even if present), (3) objection to its existence in the original, (4) objection to the proof's premises generally. Note the distinction between types 1 and 2: type 1 denies the description is the cause; type 2 accepts it as a description but denies it can cause the ruling.
Types 3 and 4 are implied in the second part of the passage (المنع الثالث والرابع) but not fully expanded here; they concern the existence of the description and the proof's structure.
3
Study the Ramadan Fast Example as Type 1
The example: Shafi'i claims that expiation for breaking fast is tied to intercourse, so it doesn't apply to eating/drinking. Hanafi rebuttal: the cause is intentional breaking of the fast (present in eating/drinking). This is a type 1 mumana'ah – denying the claimed 'illa (intercourse) and substituting another (intentional break). Also note how the Hanafi argument uses al-qawl bi-mujib al-illa (accepting the opponent's cause but showing it doesn't apply) which is a subset of mumana'ah.
The hadith 'When Sha'ban ends, no fast except for Ramadan' is used as evidence for the unique specification of Ramadan, distinguishing it from other fasts.
4
Examine the Commentator's Critical Refinement
Al-Qamar points out that the second type (objection to validity for the ruling) might be reducible to the first (objection to causality). He notes that later scholars (al-qawm) interpreted the second type as objecting to the existence of the description in the original, making it distinct. He critiques the author's wording 'with its existence' and calls for careful consideration.
This refinement shows the dynamic nature of Hanafi usul and the importance of precise taxonomy in legal debate.

بيان أقسام الممانعة إذ أينما توجد الفرضية يوجد التعيين كصوم القضاء والكفارة والصلاة الخمس، ونحن ندفعه بموجب علته فنقول : عندنا لا يصح إلا بتعيين النية، وإنما نحوزه بإطلاق النية على أنه تعيين، وهو التعيين أي صوم رمضان أي صوم رمضان هذا الإطلاق أي سلمنا أن التعيين ضروري للفرض، ولكن التعيين نوعان: تعيين من جانب العباد قصدًا، وتعيين من جانب الشارع، وهذا الإطلاق في حكم التعيين من جانب الشارع، فإنه قال: * "إذا انسلخ شعبان فلا صوم إلا عن رمضان"، فإن قال الخصم: إن التعيين القصدي هو المعتبر عندنا كما في القضاء والكفارة دون التعيين مطلقًا، فنقول: لا نسلّم أن التعيين القصدي معتبر، ولا نسلّم أن علته التعيين القصدي في القضاء والكفارة هي مجرد الفرضية، بل كون وقته صالحا لأنواع الصيامات، بخلاف رمضان؛ فإنه متعين كالمتوحد في المكان القضاء والكفارة يصاب مطلق اسمه، ولم يذكر هذا الاعتراض أهل المناظرة؛ لأنه سطحي لا يبقى بعد الدقة أي ضعيف وتعين البحث؛ فإن استفسار المدعي عندهم وبيانه بعد الطلب واجب، فلا يقبله قط. بيان أقسام الممانعة والممانعة، وهي عدم قبول السائل مقدمات دليل المعلّل كلها أو بعضها بالتعيين والتفصيل، أي الثاني فنقول: عندنا لا يصلح إلخ: اعلم أن العلة في هذا المثال علة مؤثرة؛ لأن تأثير الفرضية في تعيين نية الفرض ثابت، فظهر أن القول باختصاص القول بالموجب بالعلة الطردية غير صحيح، كذا في "التنوير".(السنبلي) ضروري للفرض فوصف الفرضية موجب التعيين. بيان أقسام الممانعة
وهي أربعة بالاستقراء؛ لأنها إما أن تكون في نفس الوصف أي لا نسلّم أن هذا الوصف الذي تدّعيه وصفًا علة، بل العلة شيء آخر، كقول الشافعي رحمه الله في كفارة الإفطار : إنها أي في أداء رمضان عقوبة متعلّقة بالجماع، فلا تكون واجبة في الأكل والشرب، فنقول: لا نسلم أن العلة في الأصل هي الجماع، بل الإفطار عمدًا، وهو حاصل في الأكل والشرب أيضا بدليل أنه لو جامع ناسيًا لا يفسد صومه لعدم الإفطار. قصداً أو في صلاحيته للحكم مع وجوده أي لا نسلّم أن هذا الوصف صالح للحكم مع كونه موجوداً كقول الشافعي رحمه الله في إثبات الولاية على البكر: إنها باكرة جاهلة بأمر النكاح لعدم الممارسة بالرجال فيولّى عليها، فنقول: لا نسلّم أن وصف البكارة صالح لهذا الحكم؛ لأنه لم يظهر له تأثير في موضع آخر. أي إثبات الولاية أي لوصف البكارة أي سوى محل النزاع أي لا نسلّم إلخ هذا التفسير لكلام المصنف رحمه الله على رأي المصنف له، فإنه جعل المنع الأول منع علية الوصف، وحينئذٍ يرد عليه أن المنع الثاني الذي بينه المصنف رحمه الله بقوله : أو في صلاحيته للحكم مع وجوده عين المنع الأول، فإن صلاحية الوصف للحكم هو عليته للحكم، فمنع هذه الصلاحية هو منع العلية، إلا أن يُفرّق بأن المنع الأول منع نفس العلية سواء كانت عليتها طرديةً أو مؤثريةً، والمنع الثاني منع كون العلة علة مؤثرة، فحصل الفرق بين المنعين، لكنه حينئذٍ يلزم استدراك قول المصنف رحمه الله مع وجوده فإنه لا دخل لوجود الوصف في منع تأثیره للحكم، والقوم جعلوا المنع الثاني منع صلاحية الوصف للحكم أي عليّة له والمنع الأول منع نفس تحقق الوصف في الأصل المقيس عليه كأن يقول معلل : إن مسح الرأس مسح فيُسنّ تثليثه كالاستنجاء، فيدفع بالمنع بعدم تحقق العلة في المقيس عليه أي الاستنجاء، فإن الاستنجاء تطهير عن النجاسة الحقيقية وليس المسح تطهيرا لهذه النجاسة، فلو حمل كلام المصنف رحمه الله إما أن يكون في نفس الوصف أو في صلاحيته للحكم مع وجوده على هذين المنعين الذين رضي بهما القوم لكان أنسب لكنه يلزم توجيه الكلام بما لا يرضی به قائله، فتدبر.
