(القمر) لم يظهر له تأثير إلخ كالمال مثلاً، فإن في ولاية مالها ليس تأثير للبكر بل للصغر كما مر. (القمر) علة
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of the divisions of mumana'ah: For wherever obligation exists, specification exists, like the fast of make-up and expiation and the five prayers. We rebut it by acknowledging the cause, so we say: According to us, it is not valid except with specific intention, but we permit it with absolute intention as specification. This specification is the fast of Ramadan, this absolute intention. We concede that specification is necessary for obligation, but specification is of two types: specification from the side of the servants intentionally, and specification from the side of the Lawgiver. This absolute intention is in the ruling of specification from the side of the Lawgiver, for He said: "When Sha'ban ends, there is no fast except for Ramadan." If the opponent says: Intentional specification is what is considered according to us, as in make-up and expiation, not specification absolutely. We say: We do not concede that intentional specification is considered, nor do we concede that its cause in make-up and expiation is merely obligation, but rather because its time is suitable for types of fasts, unlike Ramadan; for it is specified like the unique one. The opponent did not mention this objection among the people of debate because it is superficial, not remaining after scrutiny, i.e., weak. And specification of investigation: for inquiry from the claimant among them and its explanation after request is obligatory, so it is not accepted at all. Explanation of the divisions of mumana'ah: Mumana'ah is the non-acceptance by the questioner of some or all premises of the proof of the one providing the cause, with specification and detail. As for the second: We say: According to us, it is not valid, etc. Know that the cause in this example is an effective cause, for the effect of obligation in specifying the intention of the obligation is established, so it appears that the statement that the rebuttal by accepting the cause is specific to the formal cause is incorrect, as in al-Tanwir. (al-Sunbuli) Necessary for obligation, so the description of obligation necessitates specification. (al-Qamar) And this is absolute, i.e., absolute intention for fasting Ramadan. (al-Qamar) Except for Ramadan: the days of Ramadan are not suitable except for the fast of Ramadan, no other. (al-Qamar) So we say: We do not concede, etc.: This statement is mumana'ah, so the rebuttal by accepting the cause returns to mumana'ah. (al-Qamar) Considered: i.e., according to the requirement of obligation. (al-Qamar) Suitable for types: make-up, supererogatory, vow, and others. (al-Muhashi) And this objection: i.e., the rebuttal by accepting the cause. (al-Qamar) It is his statement: 'If the opponent says'. (al-Muhashi) Because it is superficial, i.e., weak attributed to the surface. (al-Qamar) And its explanation, etc.: [i.e., explanation of the claim of the one providing the cause upon the one providing the cause after the request of the questioner is obligatory]. Non-acceptance, etc., with and without support, and support is what is mentioned to strengthen the rejection. (al-Qamar) Premises of the proof, etc., i.e., that the description is a cause, and that it is realized in the original and the branch, and others. (al-Qamar) Its derivation has passed.

Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of the divisions of mumana'ah. They are four by induction. For it is either regarding the description itself, i.e., we do not concede that this description that you claim is a description-cum-cause, but the cause is something else, like the statement of al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) regarding the expiation of breaking the fast: it is a penalty connected to intercourse, so it is not obligatory in eating and drinking. We say: We do not concede that the cause in the original is intercourse, rather it is intentional breaking of the fast, which is also present in eating and drinking, as evidence that if one forgetfully has intercourse, his fast is not invalidated due to lack of breaking the fast. Or regarding its validity for the ruling while it exists, i.e., we do not concede that this description is valid for the ruling while it exists, like the statement of al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) regarding establishing guardianship over a virgin: she is a virgin ignorant of the matter of marriage due to lack of interaction with men, so she is placed under guardianship. We say: We do not concede that the description of virginity is valid for this ruling, for it has not shown effect in another place. I.e., establishing guardianship, i.e., for the description of virginity, i.e., other than the place of dispute. I.e., we do not concede, etc. This interpretation of the statement of the author (may Allah have mercy on him) according to the opinion of the author, for he made the first rejection the rejection of the causality of the description, and then it is objected against him that the second rejection which the author (may Allah have mercy on him) explained by his statement: 'or in its validity for the ruling while it exists' is the same as the first rejection, for the validity of the description for the ruling is its causality for the ruling, so rejecting this validity is rejecting causality. However, there is a distinction: the first rejection is rejecting the very causality, whether the causality is formal or effective, and the second rejection is rejecting that the cause is an effective cause. Thus a difference between the two rejections is achieved, but then it is necessary to reconsider the author's statement 'with its existence' for the existence of the description has no role in rejecting its effect on the ruling. And the people made the second rejection the rejection of the validity of the description for the ruling, i.e., its causality, and the first rejection is the rejection of the very realization of the description in the original being measured, as when the one providing the cause says: Wiping the head is wiping, so its triple performance is Sunnah like istinja', and it is rebutted by rejection by non-realization of the cause in the original being measured, i.e., istinja', for istinja' is purification from actual impurity and wiping is not purification from this impurity. So if the author's statement is interpreted as either regarding the description itself or its validity for the ruling with its existence according to these two rejections which the people approved, it would be more appropriate, but it necessitates directing the speech in a way that its speaker would not be satisfied, so consider carefully. (al-Qamar) That after conceding the existence of the description. (al-Qamar) Rather intentional breaking of the fast, etc., i.e., rather the cause is intentional breaking of the fast. (al-Qamar) Rather intentional breaking of the fast, etc. I say: There is no benefit in this restriction, for breaking the fast forgetfully is not breaking the fast as has passed. (al-Sunbuli) His fast is not invalidated, etc., so it is known from this that intercourse is not a cause. (al-Sunbuli) Valid for the ruling: because the description only becomes for the ruling through effect, so as long as the effect is not shown, how can it be valid for establishing the ruling? (al-Qamar) It has not shown effect, etc., like wealth for example, for in the guardianship of her wealth, there is no effect of virginity, but rather of minority as has passed. (al-Qamar) Cause.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the concept of mumana'ah (objection/rejection) within the chapter on qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author begins by illustrating the Hanafi position on the necessity of specific intention (niyya) for obligatory fasts, using the example of Ramadan. The opponent (likely Shafi'i) argues that specific intention is not required because intention is automatically specified by the time. The Hanafi rebuttal accepts the opponent's cause (that specification is necessary) but distinguishes between two types of specification: from the servant and from the Lawgiver. The hadith 'When Sha'ban ends, no fast except for Ramadan' shows that the Lawgiver Himself specifies Ramadan, making absolute intention sufficient. This dispute is an application of the broader topic: mumana'ah is defined as the questioner's non-acceptance of some or all premises of the opponent's proof. The author then lists the four types of mumana'ah by induction: (1) Objection to the description itself – denying that the claimed description is the actual cause, asserting a different cause. Example: Shafi'i's claim that expiation in Ramadan is tied to intercourse, so it doesn't apply to eating/drinking; Hanafi replies that the cause is intentional breaking of the fast, present in both. (2) Objection to the validity of the description for the ruling while it exists – conceding the description but denying it is effective for the ruling. Example: Shafi'i claiming virginity justifies guardianship; Hanafi replies that virginity shows no effect elsewhere. (3) and (4) are further subtypes discussed in the gloss. The commentator (al-Qamar) critically refines the author's classification, noting that the second type might be reducible to the first, and offers an alternative interpretation preferred by later scholars (al-qawm). He highlights the difference between denying the cause's causality (type 1) and denying its efficacy (type 2), and critiques the author's phrasing 'with its existence'. The passage ends with a call for careful consideration (fata-dabbar). This is a classic debate in usul between formal and effective causation.

Key Terms
الممانعة (al-mumana'ah): The questioner's non-acceptance of all or some premises of the opponent's proof in qiyas, with specification and detail.
العلة الطردية (al-illa al-tardiyya): A cause that is formal, without effective influence; it is contrasted with 'illa mu'aththira (effective cause).
القول بالموجب (al-qawl bi-mujib al-illa): A rebuttal that accepts the opponent's cause but argues that it does not lead to the claimed ruling in this case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of the first type of mumana'ah (objection to the description itself)?
A) 'I accept that virginity is the cause, but it does not justify guardianship because it shows no effect elsewhere.'
B) 'The cause in expiation is not intercourse, but intentional breaking of the fast.'
C) 'I reject that the description exists in the original case, because istinja' is different from wiping.'
D) 'The proof's premise that the branch shares the same cause is false because the cause is not present.'

Key Takeaway
The four types of mumana'ah (objection to the description, its validity, its existence, and other premises) provide a precise taxonomy for challenging qiyas, refined by Hanafi scholars.

Fasād al-Wad': Invalidity of the Position of the 'Illa
Explains fasād al-wad' as a type of objection to the 'illa in qiyās.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a proposed 'illa suffers from fasād al-wad' and apply this objection to critique a qiyās argument.

Core Idea
When the claimed 'illa inherently contradicts the ruling, the qiyās is invalid — this is fasād al-wad', the strongest objection.

In Hanafi usul, not every analogy is valid. One powerful way to dismantle a qiyās is to show that the proposed cause ('illa) is fundamentally incompatible with the ruling it is supposed to justify. This is called fasād al-wad' (invalidity of the position of the cause). The following passage from Noor al-Anwaar explains this concept and illustrates it with the famous dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is over the effect of conversion to Islam on a non-Muslim marriage.

Guided Path
1
Define fasād al-wad'
Read the definition: the attribute claimed as 'illa inherently rejects the ruling and demands its opposite. Contrast this with munāqaḍa (inconsistency).
Focus on the idea that the 'illa must be suitable (munāsib) for the ruling.
2
Examine the Shafi'i example
The Shafi'is argue that conversion of one spouse automatically causes separation. Identify the 'illa (conversion) and the ruling (separation).
This is the concrete case that triggers the objection.
3
Apply the Hanafi objection
Understand why the Hanafis say this is fasād al-wad': Islam is known to preserve rights, not abolish them. Therefore conversion cannot be a cause for separation.
The 'illa contradicts the very purpose of the ruling.
4
Contrast with munāqaḍa
The text states that fasād al-wad' is stronger because it cannot be answered by merely showing the 'illa's effect; it completely nullifies the causality.
This highlights the severity of the objection.
5
Note the two types of fasād al-wad'
The commentator mentions that the author covered one type (the 'illa is unsuitable) but left another (the reasoning nullifies a textual ruling). Recall examples from previous lessons.
This expands the toolset for critique.

Source Text

(القمر) التقريب : هو سوق الدليل على وجه يستلزم المدعي. (القمر) بمجرد الإسلام فنفس الإسلام علة لإيجاب الفرقة. (القمر)
ولا يحتاج إلخ فلو عرض الإسلام على الآخر وأسلم يحتاج إلى تجديد نكاح (القمر) في وضعه فاسد أي ههنا فساد وضع العلة، فإن أدنى وضع العلة أن تناسب الحكم والإسلام ليس مناسبًا للفرقة، بل لضد الفرقة لأن إلخ. Chapter of Qiyās. 72. Explanation of the divisions of objection (mumāna'a): that is, invalidity of the position of the 'illa. And invalidity of position is that the attribute in itself is such that it rejects the ruling and necessitates its opposite, and the dialecticians did not mention it, and it can be included in what they said: that the taqrīb is not complete. Like their (the Shafi'is) reasoning for obligating separation due to the conversion to Islam of one of the spouses. For they said: When one of the two infidel spouses converts to Islam, separation occurs between them merely by conversion if she has not been consummated, and after three menstrual cycles if she has been consummated, and there is no need to present Islam to the other. And we say: This is invalid in its position because Islam is known to preserve rights, not to raise them. So it should be presented to the other; if he converts, the marriage remains between them, and if not, the separation is attributed to the other's refusal, which is a sound reasonable meaning. And this (invalidity of position) is among the strongest objections, for the one giving the 'illa cannot answer, unlike inconsistency (munāqaḍa), for there one resorts to saying that the 'illa is effective and clarifying the difference. The description being in itself etc.: know that the commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned here one of the two types of invalidity of position and left another, which is that the reasoning nullifies a textual ruling, and examples of which have passed previously, such as the analogy of the expiation for an oath on the expiation for killing (al-Sunbulī). (al-Qamar): taqrīb is presenting evidence in a way that necessitates the claim. (al-Qamar): by mere conversion: so conversion itself is the cause for obligating separation. (al-Qamar): and there is no need etc.: if he were to present Islam to the other and he converts, he would need to renew the marriage (al-Qamar). In its position it is invalid: that is, here is invalidity of the position of the 'illa, for the minimal condition of the position of the 'illa is that it be suitable for the ruling, and Islam is not suitable for separation, but rather for the opposite of separation because etc. (al-Qamar). The marriage remains etc.: because Islam establishes rights that were not, so it is more proper to preserve previous rights, because preservation is easier than initiation (al-Sunbulī). And it is a meaning: that is, attributing separation to the others refusal (al-Muhashshī). Preserver of rights: that is, beneficial rights, not remover of them, so Islam cannot be a cause for separation which is the removal of rights (al-Qamar). For he cannot etc.: except by moving to another cause (al-Qamar). Unlike inconsistency etc.: for inconsistency is embarrassing, and it is possible to avoid it by extricating oneself from the obligation of refuting the objection by changing the speech, for there one resorts to saying that the 'illa is effective, i.e., the effect of the 'illa on the ruling; because when the questioner does not accept what was mentioned without presenting proof, and no proof is accepted except by showing the effect, the respondent is compelled to show it to obligate the opponent. As for invalidity of position, it nullifies the causality entirely, so it cannot be repelled by changing the speech (al-Qamar). And clarifying the difference: that is, in the disputed matter and in the original (al-Qamar).
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of one type of objection (mumāna'a) to the 'illa in qiyās, known as 'fasād al-wad'' (invalidity of the position of the cause). The author explains that this occurs when the attribute claimed as the 'illa inherently repels the ruling and demands its opposite. The dialecticians (ahl al-munāẓara) did not list this as a separate category, but the author argues it can be subsumed under their principle that the 'illa fails to establish a valid taqrīb (approximation of evidence). The key example is the Shafi'i argument that mere conversion to Islam of one spouse necessitates immediate separation (in an unconsummated marriage) or after three cycles (in a consummated marriage), without offering Islam to the other spouse. The Hanafis reject this, saying that Islam is known to preserve rights, not abolish them. Therefore, it is contradictory to make Islam the cause of separation. Instead, the procedure should be: present Islam to the other spouse; if he/she converts, the marriage remains; if not, the separation is due to the other spouse's refusal, not due to Islam itself. The passage then contrasts fasād al-wad' with another objection, munāqaḍa (inconsistency), noting that fasād al-wad' is a stronger objection because it completely invalidates the causality and cannot be answered by merely clarifying the effect or making distinctions. The commentator (al-Qamar) adds that the matn author only mentioned one of two types of fasād al-wad' (the one where the 'illa is unsuitable for the ruling) and omitted the other type (where the reasoning nullifies a textual ruling), examples of which were previously given.

Key Terms
فساد الوضع (fasād al-wad'): The attribute claimed as 'illa inherently rejects the ruling and demands its opposite, making the analogy invalid.
الممانعة (al-mumāna'a): Objection to the 'illa in qiyās; includes fasād al-wad' and munāqaḍa.
التقريب (al-taqrīb): Presenting evidence in a way that necessitates the claim; a valid qiyās requires a proper taqrīb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis reject the Shafi'i ruling that conversion to Islam of one spouse causes immediate separation?
A) Because the 'illa (conversion) is not effective in the original case.
B) Because the 'illa (conversion) is unsuited to the ruling (separation) since Islam preserves rights, not abolishes them.
C) Because the analogy involves a different type of worship.
D) Because the ruling is based on a weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
Fasād al-wad' is a powerful objection that invalidates a qiyās by showing that the claimed 'illa is fundamentally unsuited to the ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Al-Munāqaḍa: The Objection of Inconsistency in Qiyās
Defines munāqaḍa and demonstrates it with an inter-madhhab example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the objection of munāqaḍa in a qiyās argument, and distinguish it from fasād al-wad'.

Core Idea
Munāqaḍa occurs when the claimed 'illa exists but the ruling is absent; it can be answered by showing the 'illa's effect.

This lesson examines the objection of munāqaḍa (inconsistency), a key tool in Hanafi dialectical argumentation against qiyās. Using the classic debate over intention in wudu between Hanafis and Shafi'is, the text illustrates how a munāqaḍa is raised and countered. By understanding this, you will sharpen your ability to critique analogical reasoning and recognize valid responses.

Guided Path
1
Define munāqaḍa
Understand that munāqaḍa is an objection where the claimed 'illa (cause) is present in a branch case but the ruling is absent, showing inconsistency in the analogy.
The term is synonymous with naqḍ and man' in this context.
2
Examine the Shafi'i analogy
Al-Shafi'i argued that since wudu and tayammum are both purifications, they should share the ruling on intention (obligatory).
His statement: 'They are both purifications' forms the basis of his qiyās.
3
Identify the Hanafi munāqaḍa
The Hanafis countered by pointing to washing clothes and body: also a purification for prayer, yet intention is not obligatory. This shows the 'illa 'purification' does not always produce the ruling.
This is the core inconsistency (munāqaḍa).
4
Analyze the Shafi'i response (ta'thīr)
The Shafi'i distinguished: wudu removes ritual impurity (non-understandable), washing removes actual impurity (understandable). Thus the 'illa is effective only in non-understandable purifications.
Ta'thīr means showing the effect of the 'illa in the original and limiting it.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi counter-response
The Hanafis argued that even ritual impurity becomes understandable because the entire body becomes impure upon excretion. Hence the distinction collapses, and the munāqaḍa stands.
The passage notes that this debate illustrates the strength of munāqaḍa relative to fasād al-wad'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان المناقضة]
والمناقضة ، وهي تخلف الحكم عن الوصف الذي ادعى كونه علة، ويُعبر عن هذا في علم أي الرابع أي مع وجود العلة
المناظرة بالنقض، وأما المناقضة فهي مرادفة عندهم للمنع كقول الشافعي الله في الوضوء
أهل المناظرة
والتيمم : إنهما طهارتان فكيف افترقا في النية؟ أي لا يفترقان في النية، فإذا كانت النية فرضًا في التيمم بالاتفاق فتكون في الوضوء كذلك.
أي الشافعي لك
فإنه يتنقض بغسل الثوب والبدن، فإنه أيضًا طهارة للصلاة، فينبغي أن تفرض النية فيه، فلا بد حينئذ أن يلجئ الخصم إلى بيان الفرق بينهما، والقول بالتأثير بأن غسل الثوب طهارة والبدن وغير ذلك حقيقة وإزالة النجس حقيقي، وهو معقول لا يحتاج إلى النية، بخلاف الوضوء؛ فإنه طهارة لنجس حكمي، وهو غير معقول، فيحتاج إلى النية كالتيمم، فنقول في جوابه: إن زوال الطهارة بعد خروج النجس أمر معقول؛ لأن البدن كله يتنجس بخروج البول والمني بسواء
ولهذا: أي لأن فساد الوضع أقوى من المناقضة قدم عليها. (القمر) إذا فسد الأداء إلخ: بأن كان الدعوى دنانير وأدّى شهادة الدار. (القمر) للمنع أي طلب الدليل على مقدمة معينة. (القمر) أن تفرض إلخ لأنه وجدت العلة أي الطهارة والحكم أي فرضية النية متخلف (القمر) بينهما: أي بين الوضوء وغسل الثوب والبدن. (القمر) بالتأثير: أي بتأثير تلك العلة في الحكم. (القمر) وهو معقول: فإن المقصود فيه إزالة عين النجاسة عن المحل. (القمر) لا يحتاج إلخ فإنه ليس فيه تعبد. (القمر)
وهو غير معقول بل هو تعبدي، فإنه ليس في محل الغسل نجاسة تزول بهذه الطهارة، فإذا كان تعبديا كالتيمم فلا بد من النية، فإن العبادة لا تتأدّى بدون النية. (القمر) جوابه أي جواب التفرقة والقول بالتأثير. (المحشي) يتنجس إلخ : فإن موضع الخروج إذا تنجس فوجب التطهير، وهو لا يتجزأ، فكان البدن كله يتنجس. (القمر) والمني بسواء إلخ وأنت قائل في المني بسواء في خروج النجس، فينبغي أن يكون سواء في زوال الطهارة. (السنبلي) فكان القياس غسل كل البدن بخروج البول والمني كليهما على السواء ولكن إلخ. (القمر)
بسواء:
Explanation of inconsistency (munāqaḍa). And inconsistency is that the ruling fails to accompany the attribute claimed as the cause, and this is expressed in the science of dialectics as 'naqḍ' (refutation). As for munāqaḍa, it is synonymous with 'man' (denial) among them, like the statement of al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) concerning wudu and tayammum: 'They are both purifications, so how can they differ regarding intention?' That is, they should not differ in intention. So if intention is obligatory in tayammum by consensus, then it is likewise in wudu. But this is refuted by the case of washing clothes and body, for that is also a purification for prayer, so intention should be obligatory therein. Therefore the opponent must clarify the difference between them and assert that the 'illa is effective: that washing clothes and body is a purification for actual impurity and removal of actual filth, which is understandable and does not require intention, unlike wudu, for it is a purification for a ritual impurity, which is not understandable, so it requires intention like tayammum. So we say in response: The removal of purity after the exit of filth is understandable, because the whole body becomes impure by the exit of urine and semen equally. For this reason: because fasād al-wad' is stronger than munāqaḍa, it was given precedence. (al-Qamar): if the performance is flawed etc.: like if the claim is for dinars but the witness testifies about a house. (al-Qamar): for 'man' i.e., demanding proof for a specific premise. (al-Qamar): that it be imposed etc. because the 'illa (purification) existed and the ruling (obligation of intention) did not follow. (al-Qamar): between them: i.e., between wudu and washing clothes/body. (al-Qamar): by effect: i.e., by the effect of that 'illa on the ruling. (al-Qamar): and it is understandable: for the purpose there is to remove the actual impurity from the place. (al-Qamar): does not need etc.: for there is no ritual element in it. (al-Qamar): and it is not understandable but rather ritualistic, for there is no impurity in the place of washing that is removed by this purification, so if it is ritualistic like tayammum, then intention is necessary, for worship is not performed without intention. (al-Qamar): his response i.e., the response of distinction and assertion of effect. (al-Muhashshī): becomes impure etc.: for the place of exit, if it becomes impure, then purification is required, and it is indivisible, so the whole body becomes impure. (al-Qamar): and semen equally etc.: and you say that semen is equal in the exit of filth, so it should be equal in the removal of purity. (al-Sunbulī): so the analogy would be washing the whole body with the exit of urine and semen both equally, but etc. (al-Qamar): equally:
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage defines munāqaḍa (inconsistency) as an objection in qiyās where the claimed 'illa is present but the ruling is absent in a branch case. The author equates it with 'naqḍ' in dialectics and says it is synonymous with 'man'' (denial). The example given is al-Shafi'i's argument that since wudu and tayammum are both purifications, they should share the same ruling regarding intention (i.e., intention should be obligatory in both). The Hanafis counter by raising a munāqaḍa: washing clothes and body is also a purification for prayer, yet intention is not obligatory there. Thus the 'illa (purification) is present in both wudu and washing clothes, but the ruling (obligation of intention) differs. To defend the claim, the opponent must show a difference (tafrīq) between the cases and assert that the 'illa is effective only in wudu because it is a ritual purification (ṭahāra ḥukmiyya) that is not rationally understandable, similar to tayammum, whereas washing clothes is a physical purification that is rationally understandable and does not require intention. The Hanafis then respond that the removal of ritual purity after impurity is also understandable because the entire body becomes impure upon the exit of urine or semen. The passage concludes by reiterating that fasād al-wad' is a stronger objection than munāqaḍa, which is why it was discussed first.

Key Terms
المناقضة (al-munāqaḍa): An objection where the claimed 'illa exists but the ruling is absent in a branch case; synonymous with naqḍ and man' in this context.
النقض (al-naqḍ): Refutation of a claim by showing a contradictory case; here used interchangeably with munāqaḍa.
التأثير (al-ta'thīr): The effect of the 'illa on the ruling; claiming that the 'illa actually causes the ruling in the original and can be effective in the branch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi counter-response to the Shafi'i distinction that wudu is a ritual purification (non-understandable) while washing clothes is actual purification (understandable)?
A) They accept the distinction and concede the argument.
B) They argue that even ritual impurity becomes understandable because the whole body becomes impure upon excretion.
C) They deny that wudu is a purification at all.
D) They change the subject to a different type of analogy.

Key Takeaway
Munāqaḍa is a powerful dialectical tool in Hanafi usul to challenge weak analogies, but it can be answered by showing the 'illa's effect or by distinguishing the cases.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Munāqaḍah in Qiyas: The Niyyah Debate
Definition and application of munāqaḍah with a fiqhi example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of munāqaḍah to evaluate a qiyas argument and explain the Hanafi method of bayan al-farq.

Core Idea
Munāqaḍah can be rebutted by showing a valid distinction between the cases.

In this passage, the author introduces a crucial objection in qiyas known as munāqaḍah (contradiction). It arises when a claimed cause ('illah) appears in a different case but produces a different ruling. The Shafi'i argument about intention (niyyah) in wudu provides a concrete example: if both wudu and tayammum are purifications, and intention is required in tayammum, it should also be required in wudu. The Hanafi response uses bayan al-farq (exposé of difference) to show that the two purifications are not analogous. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to construct and defend qiyas arguments.

Guided Path
1
Define munāqaḍah and its synonyms
Identify the definition from the text: the ruling not following the attribute claimed to be the cause. Note that it is also called naqḍ and is synonymous with manʿ in this context.
Munāqaḍah is a specific objection; manʿ is more general.
2
Recount the Shafi'i qiyas
State the Shafi'i argument: wudu and tayammum share the ‘illah of being purifications. Since intention is fard in tayammum by consensus, it must be fard in wudu. This claims a munāqaḍah against the Hanafi position that intention is not fard in wudu.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal via bayan al-farq
The Hanafi response distinguishes between real purification (ghusl of garment, removing haqiqi impurity) and legal purification (wudu, removing hukmi impurity). The former is comprehensible and does not require intention; the latter is non-comprehensible and requires intention, like tayammum. Then they address a counter: ghusl after janabah also removes hukmi impurity yet requires intention. The reply uses hardship (haraj): ghusl is rare, so no hardship if intention required; wudu is frequent, so requiring intention would cause hardship.
The distinction thus rebuts the charge of munāqaḍah by showing the two cases are not truly alike.
4
Understand the limit for mu'aththira
The text states that effective causes (mu'aththira, proven by text/ijma) do not admit munāqaḍah. After manʿ, only muʿāraḍa (opposition) is allowed. This protects certain 'ilal from being refuted by contradictions.
This is a Hanafi usul principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان المناقضة: والمناقضة وهي تخلف الحكم عن الوصف الذي ادعى كونه علة، ويعبر عن هذا في علم المناظرة بالنقض، وأما المناقضة فهي مرادفة عندهم للمنع كقول الشافعي في الوضوء والتيمم: إنهما طهارتان فكيف افترقا في النية؟ أي لا يفترقان في النية، فإذا كانت النية فرضا في التيمم بالاتفاق فتكون في الوضوء كذلك. فإنه يتنقض بغسل الثوب والبدن، فإنه أيضا طهارة للصلاة، فينبغي أن تفرض النية فيه، فلا بد حينئذ أن يلجئ الخصم إلى بيان الفرق بينهما، والقول بالتأثير بأن غسل الثوب طهارة والبدن وغير ذلك حقيقة وإزالة النجس حقيقي، وهو معقول لا يحتاج إلى النية، بخلاف الوضوء؛ فإنه طهارة لنجس حكمي، وهو غير معقول، فيحتاج إلى النية كالتيمم، فنقول في جوابه: إن زوال الطهارة بعد خروج النجس أمر معقول؛ لأن البدن كله يتنجس بخروج البول والمني بسواء. ولكن لما كان المني أقل إخراجا وجب الغسل فيه لتمام البدن بلا حرج، بخلاف البول؛ فإنه لما كان أكثر خروجا، وفي غسل كل البدن بكل مرة حرج عظيم، لا جرم يقتصر على الأعضاء الأربعة التي هي أصول البدن في الحدود، ووقوع الآثام منه دفعا للحرج، فالاقتصار على الأعضاء الأربعة غير معقول، وأما نجاسة البدن وإزالة الماء لها فأمر معقول، فلا يحتاج إلى النية، بخلاف التراب؛ لأنه ملوث في نفسه غير مطهر بطبعه؛ فلذا يحتاج إلى النية، وأما المؤثرة فليس للسائل فيها بعد الممانعة إلا المعارضة فيه إشارة إلى أنه تجري فيها الممانعة وما قبلها أعني القول بموجب العلة، ولا يجري فيها ما بعدها؛ لأنها لا تحتمل المناقضة.
Explanation of Contradiction: Contradiction is the ruling not following the attribute claimed to be the cause. This is called naqd in the science of dialectics. Contradiction is synonymous with prevention (man'), like the statement of al-Shafi'i concerning wudu and tayammum: 'Both are purifications, so how can they differ regarding intention?' That is, they should not differ. If intention is obligatory in tayammum by consensus, then it should be likewise in wudu. It is refuted by washing a garment and the body, for that too is a purification for prayer, so intention should be obligatory there. Then the opponent must explain the difference and claim effect (ta'thir): that washing a garment and body is a real purification removing real impurity, which is comprehensible and does not require intention, unlike wudu which is purification for a legal impurity, which is incomprehensible, so it requires intention like tayammum. We say in response: The removal of purity after impurity exits is comprehensible, because the whole body becomes impure with the exit of urine and semen equally. But because semen exits less frequently, washing the entire body is obligatory without hardship, unlike urine which exits more frequently and washing the whole body each time would be extremely burdensome; hence it is confined to the four limbs which are the origins of the body in the legal limits, to avoid hardship. Thus limiting to the four limbs is not comprehensible. As for bodily impurity and water removing it, that is comprehensible and does not require intention, unlike earth because it is inherently impure and not cleansing by nature; hence it requires intention. As for the effective cause (mu'aththira), after prevention (mumana'a) the questioner has only opposition (mu'arada), indicating that prevention and what precedes it (i.e., applying the cause) can be employed, but what follows it cannot, because it does not admit of contradiction.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute (ikhtilaf) about the concept of munāqaḍah (contradiction) in qiyas, exemplified by the issue of intention (niyyah) in purification acts. The text defines munāqaḍah as a situation where the ruling does not follow the attribute claimed to be the cause ('illah). It is equivalent to the dialectical concept of naqd and the method of man' (prevention/objection). The example given is from the Shafi'i school: al-Shafi'i argues that since both wudu and tayammum are purifications, and intention is required in tayammum by consensus, it should also be required in wudu. This is a munāqaḍah against the Hanafi position that wudu does not require intention (for its validity, as the Hanafis consider intention in wudu as sunnah, not fard). The Hanafi response uses the technique of bayan al-farq (explaining the difference): they distinguish between real purification (ghusl of garment/body) which is comprehensible and does not require intention, and legal purification (wudu) which deals with ritual impurity and is incomprehensible, thus requiring intention. But then they address the counter-argument: ghusl after impurity (e.g., janabah) also removes ritual impurity, yet intention is required. The Hanafi rebuttal uses the concept of hardship (haraj): ghusl after impurity (from semen) is rare, so no hardship; wudu after urine is frequent, so hardship is avoided by not requiring intention. Finally, the passage discusses the 'illah mu'aththira (effective cause) and states that after the stage of man', the opponent can only use mu'arada (opposition) not munāqaḍah, because the effective cause (proven by text/ijma) does not admit contradiction. This is a Hanafi position that protects certain 'ilal from being refuted by munāqaḍah.

Key Terms
المناقضة (al-munāqaḍah): The ruling not following the attribute claimed to be the cause in qiyas; a type of objection.
النقض (al-naqḍ): Synonymous with munāqaḍah in dialectics; the act of showing contradiction.
المنع (al-manʿ): Prevention; asking for a proof for a specific premise; here synonymous with munāqaḍah in the context of dialectics.
العلة (al-ʿillah): The effective cause in qiyas; the attribute on which the ruling is based.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if an opponent claims munāqaḍah against an 'illah that is mu'aththira (effective cause)?
A) The opponent must provide an alternative 'illah.
B) The opponent can only use muʿāraḍa (opposition), not munāqaḍah.
C) The opponent's claim automatically invalidates the qiyas.
D) The opponent must prove the 'illah is not mu'aththira.

Key Takeaway
Munāqaḍah is a valid objection but can be defused by bayan al-farq; in Hanafi usul, effective causes (mu'aththira) are immune to munāqaḍah.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Munaqadah and Fasad al-Wad' in Effective Causal Attributes
Explains that effective causal attributes proven by Quran/Sunnah/Ijma cannot be subject to contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that effective causal attributes (mu'aththirah) cannot be subject to munaqadah after their effect is proven by Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, and identify when objections are permissible.

Core Idea
An effective cause proven by definitive sources is immune to contradiction.

In Hanafi qiyas, not all objections are allowed at every stage. This lesson focuses on a central rule: once an effective causal attribute (mu'aththirah) has its effect established by the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, it cannot be challenged through munaqadah (contradiction) or fasad al-wad' (corruption of postulation). However, before that proof, these objections remain valid. Understanding this distinction is critical for correctly evaluating arguments in legal analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed illa and its type
Determine whether the attribute is claimed as mu'aththirah (effective) or merely tardiyyah (correlational). Only mu'aththirah is subject to this rule.
The source distinguishes between effective and non-effective causes.
2
Assess whether the effect (ta'thir) is proven
Check if the proponent has provided a proof from one of the three sources: Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma. If yes, the effect is considered established.
If the proof is absent, the cause is not yet mu'aththirah.
3
Apply the rule
If the effect is proven by these sources, the opponent cannot raise munaqadah or fasad al-wad'. If not proven, these objections are permissible until the effect is established.
After proof, only other objections (e.g., man', mu'arada) may be allowed.
4
Evaluate the objection's method
If the objection is raised, determine whether it falls under munaqadah or fasad al-wad'. If the effect is already proven, the objection is invalid.
The opponent must use other allowed objections until the effect is proven.
5
Test with the given examples
Work through the three examples: (1) impurities exiting the body (Quran), (2) leftover of domestic animals (Sunnah), (3) thief's hand not cut a third time (Ijma). See how the rule applies in each case.
These examples show the effect established by each source.

Exposition of Contradiction. Chapter of Analogy. But since semen is less frequent in exit, washing the whole body without hardship is obligatory, unlike urine; for it is more frequent, and washing the whole body each time is a great hardship, so without doubt it is confined to the four limbs which are the origins of the body in the boundaries, and occurrence of sins from it, to repel hardship, i.e., in the extremities of a person. So confining to the four limbs is not rational. As for impurity of the body and its removal by water, it is a rational matter, so it does not need intention, unlike earth; because it is inherently impure, not purifying by its nature; hence it needs intention. As for the influential [cause], the questioner has after prevention nothing except opposition, indicating that prevention and what precedes it, i.e., stating the requirement of the cause, apply to it, and what comes after does not apply, because it cannot be contradicted. But etc. is a correction of what preceded. [Commentary elaborates on the examples and the principle that effective causes proven by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma cannot be contradicted. Then discusses that objections can be raised before proof. Gives three examples: from Quran: impurity exiting from other than the two passages is hadath; from Sunnah: leftover of domestic animals is not impure; from Ijma: thief's hand not cut off a third time.]
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Qiyas discusses the position of effective causal attributes (al-illah al-mu'aththirah) with respect to objections like contradiction (munaqadah) and corruption of postulation (fasad al-wad'). The text explains that after an effective attribute's effect has been established by the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, it cannot be subject to munaqadah, because these sources themselves are immune to such objections. However, this immunity only applies after proof; before proof, objections are permissible. The commentary, citing al-Talwih, notes a difference of opinion: some hold that munaqadah is never allowed against effective causes since their effectiveness is based on definitive proof, but the correct view is that effectiveness may be only speculative, so contradiction can validly be raised until the effect is established. Three examples illustrate: (1) from the Quran — impurities exiting from other than the two regular passages (like blood) are considered hadath (ritual impurity) by analogy with the verse about coming from the privy; (2) from the Sunnah — the leftover water of domestic animals (e.g., mice, lizards) is ruled pure by analogy with the cat's leftover, based on the hadith that the cat is among those who go around you; (3) from Ijma — a thief's hand is not cut off for a third theft because it would destroy the whole benefit, contradicting the agreed-upon purpose of the punishment as a deterrent, not an eliminator. The text emphasizes that objections are allowed according to the claimant's claim and the opponent's assumption, not after the effect is proven by scriptural or consensus evidence.

Key Terms
المناقضة (al-munāqaḍah): An objection in qiyas where the claimed effective cause (illa) is present but the ruling is absent in another case, showing inconsistency.
المؤثرة (al-mu'aththirah): An effective causal attribute whose influence (ta'thir) on the ruling is established by text or consensus.
فساد الوضع (fasād al-waḍ‘): An objection that the claimed illa is not an appropriate attribute for the ruling because it does not suit the wisdom or purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After a scholar claims an effective causal attribute (mu'aththirah) and proves its effect by the Qur'an, Sunnah, or Ijma, can the opponent raise the objection of munaqadah (contradiction)?
A) Yes, because munaqadah is always allowed.
B) No, because these sources are immune to such objections.
C) Only if the proof is from Sunnah, not from Qur'an.
D) Yes, but only if the opponent provides a stronger counter-dalil.

Key Takeaway
The immunity of effective causes from munaqadah is conditional upon the prior establishment of their effect by scriptural or consensus proof.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Defending the Effective Cause: The Four Methods of Rebutting Contradiction
Exposition of methods to rebut objections to an effective cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a cause is mu'aththira, apply the four methods (daf' bi al-wasf, bi al-ma'na, bi al-hukm, bi al-gharad) to rebut a formal contradiction against it, and explain why fasad al-wad' is inapplicable to such a cause.

Core Idea
An effective cause is immune to corrupt placement but can be formally contradicted, requiring rebuttal via one of four methods.

In Hanafi usul, constructing an effective cause (al-illah al-mu'aththirah) is a sophisticated exercise. Once its efficacy is proven by a definitive source (Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma), a powerful objection called fasad al-wad' (corrupt placement) cannot be raised—the cause is protected. However, the objection of naqd (contradiction) can still be brought formally, not in reality, and the scholar must know how to rebut it using specific methods. This passage from Noor al-Anwar lays out those four methods and demonstrates them through a classic Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over what invalidates wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three bases that establish an effective cause
The passage states that a cause becomes mu'aththira when its effect is proven by the Book, Sunnah, or consensus. Each is illustrated with an example. Identify these three examples and the proof cited for each.
These three sources are definitive (qat'i), so the cause inherits their immunity.
2
Understand why fasad al-wad' does not apply to mu'aththira
The author asserts that fasad al-wad' (objection that the cause would entail a contradictory ruling) is impossible for a cause proven by those sources. Grasp the rationale: the sources themselves cannot be corrupt, so the cause derived from them shares that integrity.
This is a key Hanafi protection for established illahs.
3
Distinguish formal naqd from real naqd
Naqd (contradiction) can be raised formally (ṣūratan) but not in reality (ḥaqīqatan). That means an opponent can point to a case where the description (illah) appears present yet the ruling is absent, but the scholar must rebut it—not accept it as a true invalidation.
The rebuttal restores the cause's integrity.
4
List and explain the four rebuttal methods
The passage names four methods: daf' bi al-wasf (deny the description exists), daf' bi al-ma'na (deny the underlying rationale), daf' bi al-hukm (affirm the same ruling applies), and daf' bi al-gharad (affirm the purpose is fulfilled). Study the explanation and the text's illustration with the wudu case.
Not every contradiction requires all four; the scholar selects the applicable one(s).
5
Apply the four methods to the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute
The passage uses the example of impure discharge from other than the two passages. The Hanafi claim: such discharge is like urine (impure + exiting → hadath). The Shafi'i naqd: saliva is impure and exiting (from the mouth) but does not invalidate wudu. Walk through how the Hanafi rebuts using the first method (daf' bi al-wasf: saliva does not 'exit' from the body cavity in the same way).
The other methods are briefly mentioned; focus on understanding the logic of each.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
بيان المناقضة وفساد الوضع بعد ما ظهر أثرها بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع؛ لأن هؤلاء الثلاثة لا تحتمل المناقضة وفساد الوضع فكذا التأثير الثابت بها إما مثال ما ظهر أثره بالكتاب ما قلنا في الخارج من غير السبيلين: إنه نجس خارج، فكان حدثًا، فإن طُولبنا ببيان الأثر، قلنا: ظهر تأثيره مرة في السبيلين بقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِنْكُمْ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ ﴾ (النساء: 43)، ومثال ما ظهر أثره بالسنة ما قلنا في سؤر سواكن البيوت: إنه ليس بنجس قياسًا على سور الهرة بعلة الطواف، فإن طولبنا ببيان تأثيره قلنا: ثبت تأثيره بقوله عليها إنها من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات، ومثال ما ظهر أثره بالإجماع ما قلنا بأنه لا تقطع يد السارق في المرة الثالثة؛ لأن فيه تفويت جنس المنفعة على الكمال، فإن طولبنا ببيان تأثيره قلنا: إن حد السرقة شرع زاجرًا لا مُتلفًا بالإجماع. ثم إن فساد الوضع لا يتجه على العلة المؤثرة أصلاً، وأما المناقضة فإنها تتجه عليه صورة وإن لم تتجه عليها حقيقة، وإليه أشار بقوله: لكنه إذا تصوّر مناقضة يجب رفعه بطرق أربعة، وهي الدفع بالوصف، ثم بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف، ثم بالحكم، ثم بالغرض على ما يأتي، وليس معناه أنه يجب دفع كل نقض بطرق أربعة، بل يجب دفع بعض النقوض ببعض الطرق، وبعضها ببعض آخر منها، والمجموع يبلغ أربعة فالتعليل بالعلة المؤثرة وإيراد النقض الصوري عليها ودفعه كما نقول في الخارج من غير السبيلين: إنه نجس خارج من بدن الإنسان فكان حدثًا كالبول، فيورد عليه نقضاً على هذا التعليل من جانب الشافعي له ما إذا لم يسل، أي ناقضا للوضوء فإنه نجس خارج وليس بحدث، فندفعه أولاً بالوصف أي نمنع الخروج فيه، وقوله بالمعنى الثابت أي يقال: إن المعنى الذي صارت العلة علة لأجله لم يوجد ههنا نحو مسح الرأس مسح، فلا يُسنّ فيه التثليث كمسح الخفّ، ثم بالحكم أي بوجود الحكم في مادة النقض، ثم بالغرض: أي بوجود الغرض المطلوب من العلة في مادة النقض.
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of contradiction and corrupt placement after its effect has been manifested by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus; because these three do not admit contradiction and corrupt placement, so likewise the effect established by them. As for an example of what manifested its effect by the Book: what we said about the discharge from other than the two passages: that it is impure, exiting, so it is an event [invalidating wudu]. If we are asked to explain its effect, we say: its effect appeared once in the two passages by His saying: 'Or if any of you comes from the privy' (Quran 4:43). And an example of what manifested its effect by the Sunnah: what we said about the leftover water of domestic animals: that it is not impure, by analogy to the leftover of a cat due to the cause of frequent movement. If we are asked to explain its effect, we say: its effect is established by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed it is among those who go around you and go around.' And an example of what manifested its effect by consensus: what we said that the hand of the thief is not cut off in the third instance; because therein is the loss of the entire type of benefit. If we are asked to explain its effect, we say: The penalty for theft is legislated as a deterrent, not as a destroyer, by consensus. Then, corrupt placement does not apply to the effective cause at all. As for contradiction, it applies to it formally but not truly. He alluded to this by his saying: However, if a contradiction is conceived, its removal is obligatory by four methods: rebuttal by the description, then by the meaning established by the description, then by the ruling, then by the purpose, as will follow. It does not mean that every contradiction must be rebutted by all four methods; rather, some contradictions must be rebutted by some methods, and some by others, and the total amounts to four. So, reasoning by the effective cause and presenting the formal contradiction and its rebuttal, as we say about the discharge from other than the two passages: that it is impure, exiting from the human body, so it is an event like urine. Then a contradiction is brought against this reasoning from the side of al-Shafi'i: what if saliva does not flow? That is, it invalidates wudu while it is impure exiting and not an event. So we rebut it first by the description: we deny the exiting in it. And his saying: by the meaning established, i.e., it is said: the meaning for which the cause became a cause does not exist here, like wiping the head is wiping, so tathlith (three times) is not recommended for it like wiping the khuff. Then by the ruling: by the existence of the ruling in the contradictory instance. Then by the purpose: by the existence of the intended purpose of the cause in the contradictory instance.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This is an advanced usul al-fiqh passage explaining how to defend an effective cause (illah mu'aththirah) against the two key objections: corrupt placement (fasad al-wad') and contradiction (naqd). The author first establishes that once the efficacy of a cause is proven by the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, corrupt placement cannot be raised against it because these sources are immune to such corruption. However, contradiction can still be raised formally, though not in reality, and must be rebutted using one or more of four specific methods: (1) rebuttal by description (daf' bi al-wasf): denying that the description (the cause) exists in the contradictory case; (2) rebuttal by the meaning (daf' bi al-ma'na): denying that the underlying rationale of the cause exists; (3) rebuttal by the ruling (daf' bi al-hukm): affirming that the same ruling actually applies in the contradictory case; (4) rebuttal by the purpose (daf' bi al-gharad): affirming that the intended purpose of the cause is fulfilled. The author illustrates with a Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute: the Hanafi argue that any impure discharge from the body (other than the two passages) invalidates wudu by analogy to urine, because the effective cause is 'impure discharge.' The Shafi'i object that saliva is also impure discharge yet does not invalidate wudu. The Hanafi rebut this by the first method: saliva does not exit from the body in the same way (it is not a 'discharge' from within), or by other methods as explained. The four methods are not always all needed; the correct method depends on the case.

Key Terms
العلة المؤثرة (al-'illah al-mu'aththirah): A cause whose efficacy is proven by a textual proof (Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma), making it immune to corrupt placement but subject to formal contradiction.
المناقضة (al-munaqadah): The objection that the claimed cause exists but the ruling does not follow, requiring rebuttal through one of four methods.
فساد الوضع (fasad al-wad'): The objection that the claimed cause is corrupt because it would entail a contradictory ruling, but this cannot be raised against an effective cause proven by a source.
الدفع بالوصف (al-daf' bi al-wasf): Rebutting a contradiction by denying that the description (the cause) actually exists in the contradictory case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul text, how many methods are available to rebut a contradiction (naqd) against an effective cause?
A) One method: rebuttal by description.
B) Two methods: description and meaning.
C) Four methods: description, meaning, ruling, and purpose.
D) Five methods: including corrupt placement.

Key Takeaway
An effective cause proven by Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma is immune to fasad al-wad' but can be formally contradicted; the scholar must rebut the contradiction using one or more of the four methods: description, meaning, ruling, and purpose.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Four Methods to Refute a Naqd in Qiyas
Explains four methods to refute a formal contradiction against an effective cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the four Hanafi methods to refute a contradiction (naqd) against an effective cause in qiyas.

Core Idea
A formal counterexample does not break a valid cause if its description or effective meaning is absent.

In Hanafi usul, the illah mu'aththirah is immune from fasad al-wad' but can be challenged with formal contradictions (munaqadah). The commentator on Noor al-Anwar explains four refutation methods that the mujtahid uses to preserve the cause. These are not a checklist; each naqd requires the appropriate method. Understanding these tools is crucial for defending a qiyas against superficial objections.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the nature of munaqadah
Understand that munaqadah is only formal (surah) and does not affect the reality (haqiqah) of the effective cause. This sets the stage for refutation.
Corruption of position (fasad al-wad') does not apply to the illah mu'aththirah.
2
List the four refutation methods
Memorize the four: daf' bil-wasf (by description), daf' bil-ma'na al-thabit bil-wasf (by meaning established by description), daf' bil-hukm (by ruling), daf' bil-gharad (by purpose).
Not all four are used in every case; one or more methods may be sufficient.
3
Analyze the wudu' example
Examine the Hanafi example: the illah for breaking wudu' is exiting impurity (khuruj). The Shafi'i counterexample is non-flowing blood (la yasil) which exits but does not break wudu'. The Hanafi refutes by first denying the description (wasf): non-flowing blood is not 'exiting' but merely apparent (badin). Second, he denies the effective meaning (ma'na): even if exiting, the required meaning (washing that spot) is absent here.
This illustrates the first two methods.
4
Distinguish between the two repulsions
The first method (daf' bil-wasf) denies the existence of the description; the second method (daf' bil-ma'na) acknowledges the description but denies its causality. Both preserve the cause.
The difference is subtle but important for accuracy.
5
Apply the methods to new cases
When encountering a formal naqd, first check whether the description truly exists; if not, use method 1. If it does, check whether the effective meaning is present; if not, use method 2. If both exist, then consider methods 3 or 4.
This step-by-step ensures the cause remains intact.

باب القياس بيان المناقضة ثم إن فساد الوضع لا يتجه على العلة المؤثرة أصلاً، وأما المناقضة فإنها تتجه عليه صورة وإن لم تتجه عليها حقيقة، وإليه أشار بقوله : لكنه إذا تصوّر مناقضة يجب رفعه بطرق أربعة، وهي الدفع بالوصف، ثم بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف، ثم بالحكم، ثم بالغرض على ما يأتي، وليس معناه أنه يجب دفع كل نقض بطرق أربعة، بل يجب دفع بعض النقوض ببعض الطرق، وبعضها ببعض آخر منها، والمجموع يبلغ أربعة فالتعليل بالعلة المؤثرة وإيراد النقض الصوري عليها ودفعه كما نقول في الخارج من غير السبيلين: إنه نجس خارج، كالدم وغيره من بدن الإنسان فكان جدثًا كالبول، فيورد عليه نقضاً، أي على هذا التعليل من جانب الشافعي له ما إذا لم يسل، أي ناقضا للوضوء فإنه نجس خارج وليس بحدث، فندفعه أولاً بالوصف أي ندفع هذا النقض بالطريقين: الأول بعدم الوصف، وهو أنه ليس بخارج بل بادٍ؛ لأن تحت كل جلدة دما، فإذا زالت الجلدة ظهر الدم في مكانه ولم يخرج، ولم ينتقل من موضع إلى موضع بخلاف الدم السائل، فإنه كان في العروق وانتقل إلى فوق الجلد، وخرج من موضعه، ثم بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف دلالةً، أي ندفعه ثانيًا بعدم المعنى الثابت بالوصف، ونقول: لو سلّم أنه وجد وصف الخروج لكنه لم يوجد المعنى الثابت بالخروج دلالة، وهو وجوب غسل ذلك الموضع، فإنه يجب أوّلاً غسل ذلك الموضع، ثم يجب غسل البدن كله، ولكن نقتصر على الأربعة دفعًا للحرج فيه أي بسبب وجوب غسل ذلك الموضع صار الوصف حجة من حيث إن وجوب التطهير في البدن باعتبار ما يكون منه لا يتجزأ، فلما وجب غسل ذلك الموضع وجب غسل سائر البدن البتة، وهناك لم يجب غسل ذلك الموضع، فعدم الحكم لعدم العلة كأنه لم يوجد وهي الخروج ويورد عليه صاحب الجرح السائل، هو وجوب التطهير في البدن باد: أي بل هو مستقر في موضعه. (القمر) البادي ما زايله الجلد فظهر الدم الذي تحت كل جلدة.(المحشي) السائل: هو دم في العروق، وانتقل إلى فوق الجلد، وخرج من موضعه إلى موضع آخر وسال.(المحشي) المعنى الثابت أي الذي له دخل في علية الوصف . (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of contradiction (munaqadah). Then, indeed, the corruption of position (fasad al-wad') does not apply to the effective cause (illah mu'aththirah) at all. As for contradiction (al-munaqadah), it applies to it in form (surah) but not in reality (haqiqah). The author pointed to this by saying: But if a contradiction is imagined, it must be removed by four methods: repelling by the description (wasf), then by the meaning established by the description (ma'na al-thabit bi al-wasf), then by the ruling (hukm), then by the purpose (gharad) as will come. And it does not mean that every contradiction must be repelled by four methods; rather, some contradictions must be repelled by some methods, and some by others, and the total reaches four. So the reasoning by the effective cause and the presentation of formal contradiction upon it and its repulsion, as we say regarding what exits from other than the two passages (ghayr al-sabilayn): it is impure exterior like blood and other things from the human body, so it is hadath (ritual impurity) like urine. So a contradiction is presented against it, i.e., against this reasoning from the side of al-Shafi'i, for the case when it does not flow: that is a contradiction to wudu', for it is impure exterior but not hadath. So we repel it first by the description: that is we repel this contradiction by two ways: first, by absence of description, that it is not exiting but rather apparent (badin); because under every skin there is blood, so when the skin is removed, the blood appears in its place and does not exit, and does not move from place to place, unlike flowing blood, for it was in the veins and moved above the skin and exited from its place. Then by the meaning established by the description as an indication: that is we repel it second by absence of the meaning established by the description, and we say: even if it is conceded that the description of exiting exists, yet the meaning established by exiting as an indication does not exist, which is the obligation of washing that spot. For it is obligatory first to wash that spot, then to wash the entire body, but we confine ourselves to the four [limbs] for removal of hardship because due to the obligation of washing that spot, the description becomes evidence since the obligation of purification on the body due to what comes from it is indivisible. So when washing that spot became obligatory, washing the rest of the body necessarily became obligatory, but there washing that spot is not obligatory, so the absence of the ruling is due to the absence of the cause, as if it did not exist—that is, the exiting. And the case of flowing wound is brought against him: it is the obligation of purification on the body. 'Badin' means it is stable in its place. (al-Qamar) 'al-Badi' means that from which the skin is removed so the blood under each skin appears. (al-Muhashshi) 'al-Sa'il' is blood in veins that moves above the skin and exits from its place to another place and flows. (al-Muhashshi) 'al-Ma'na al-thabit' means that which has a role in the causality of the description. (al-Qamar) 'Huwa' means that meaning established by description. (al-Qamar) 'Dhalika al-mawdi'' means the spot from which the impurity exited. (al-Qamar) 'Fa-innahu yajibu awwalan...' because the exit of impurity has an effect on causing impurity. (al-Qamar) 'ala al-arba'ah' means on the four limbs: head, face, hands, feet. (al-Qamar) 'bi-i'tibari ma yakunu minhu' means due to what exits from the body, and he excludes by this statement the case of impurity from external sources, for that requires washing that spot only, not the whole body, by consensus, as in al-Tahqiq. (al-Qamar) 'Wa hunaka' means in the case of non-flowing, washing that spot is not obligatory by consensus because it is not exiting, so it is not impure. (al-Qamar) 'Fa-adamu al-hukm' which is its being hadath, the cause, because the aspect by which the cause becomes effective in the ruling, i.e., its being hadath, which is the obligation of washing that spot, is absent, even if the description itself is realized, so it is as if the description was not realized. And the difference between the two repulsions is that the first denies the essence of the description and the second denies the description of its causality. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Noor al-Anwar explains how to refute a challenge (naqd) against an effective cause (illah mu'aththirah) in qiyas. The author states that 'fasad al-wad'' (corruption of position) does not apply to a genuinely effective cause, but munaqadah (contradiction) can apply in form, not in reality. The commentator clarifies that when a formal contradiction arises, it must be resolved by one of four methods: (1) daf' bil-wasf (refutation by description) — denying that the description exists in the counterexample; (2) daf' bil-ma'na al-thabit bil-wasf (refutation by the meaning established by the description) — conceding the description but denying the effective meaning; (3) daf' bil-hukm (refutation by the ruling) — affirming that the ruling actually applies in the counterexample; (4) daf' bil-gharad (refutation by the purpose) — showing that the purpose of the cause is achieved. The passage illustrates with a Hanafi example: the cause for breaking wudu' is the exit of impurity from the body. The Shafi'i objection is that non-flowing blood (e.g., from a wound) does not break wudu' even though it is an exterior impurity. The Hanafi refutes first by description: non-flowing blood is not 'exiting' (it is bādin, merely apparent), so the description is absent. Second, by meaning: even if it exits, the effective meaning (obligation to wash that spot) is absent because washing the whole body is not required — only the four limbs. Thus the cause is not fully realized. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of preserving the illah mu'aththirah by showing the naqd is only formal.

Key Terms
المناقضة (al-munaqadah): A contradiction or counterexample brought against an effective cause where the cause appears present but the ruling is absent.
الدفع بالوصف (ad-daf' bi al-wasf): Refutation by denying that the description which is the cause truly exists in the counterexample.
المعنى الثابت بالوصف (al-ma'na al-thabit bi al-wasf): The effective meaning or rationale that is indicated by the description and gives it causality; refuting by denying this meaning in the counterexample.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the four refutation methods denies that the description (wasf) actually exists in the counterexample?
A) Daf' bil-wasf
B) Daf' bil-ma'na al-thabit bil-wasf
C) Daf' bil-hukm
D) Daf' bil-gharad

Key Takeaway
A formal naqd is refuted by showing that either the description or its effective meaning is absent in the counterexample, preserving the effective cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Refuting the Objection (Naqd) in Qiyas: The Four Defenses Against the Shafi'i
Explains four defenses against a Shafi'i objection to Hanafi analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the four Hanafi methods for refuting a naqd (counterexample) in qiyas, specifically regarding the definition of 'exit' for blood.

Core Idea
A valid qiyas stands even when counterexamples arise; Hanafis respond by denying the cause, its effect, postponing the ruling, or affirming the purpose.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi defense against a Shafi'i objection to the definition of 'exit' (khuruj) in analogical reasoning. The Shafi'i argues that blood appearing under skin after removal is exiting, which would undermine the Hanafi position that flowing blood is a hadath. The Hanafi scholars respond with four arguments: two that deny the attribute or its legal effect, and two that address continuous flow by postponing the ruling or affirming the purpose of the analogy. Mastering these defenses is key to defending qiyas in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i objection (naqd)
Understand that the Shafi'i claims the Hanafi definition of 'exit' is contradicted by blood under skin: it appears outside but does not move. This is a classic naqd (contradiction) against the cause (khuruj).
The objection targets the attribute of exit, not the ruling.
2
Analyze the first two defenses: denying the attribute and its effect
Defense 1: Deny that the attribute (exit) exists in non-flowing blood because it does not move from its place (it is 'bādin' not 'khārij'). Defense 2: Even if the attribute existed, the legal effect (obligation to wash the spot) is absent, indicating the cause is not operative.
These two defenses target the cause itself or its causal connection.
3
Analyze the next two defenses: postponement and purpose
Defense 3: For the flowing wound, the ruling (hadath) exists but is postponed during prayer time due to hardship. Defense 4: The purpose of analogizing blood to urine is achieved because both are excused during continuous flow, so the analogy holds.
These defenses apply even when the cause is present, by invoking a hindrance or affirming the goal of the analogy.
4
Distinguish between denial of attribute and denial of causality
The first defense denies the attribute itself; the second denies its causal efficacy. The text notes: 'The difference between the two refutations is that the first denies the attribute itself, and the second denies the attribute of its causality.'
Understanding this distinction is crucial for constructing solid responses.
5
Identify the condition for the third defense
The third defense (postponing the ruling) depends on the view that allows specification of the cause (takhsis al-illa) — i.e., that the cause may exist without its ruling due to a hindrance. This is a key difference among usuli schools.
If one rejects specification, this defense is not available.

الأول بعدم الوصف، وهو أنه ليس بخارج بل بادٍ؛ لأن تحت كل جلدة دما، فإذا زالت الجلدة ظهر الدم في مكانه ولم يخرج، ولم ينتقل من موضع إلى موضع بخلاف الدم السائل، فإنه كان في العروق وانتقل إلى فوق الجلد، وخرج من موضعه، ثم بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف دلالةً، أي ندفعه ثانيًا بعدم المعنى الثابت بالوصف، ونقول: لو سلّم أنه أي لا عبارة أي النقض وهو الخروج مثلاً وجد وصف الخروج لكنه لم يوجد المعنى الثابت بالخروج دلالة، وهو وجوب غسل ذلك الموضع، فإنه يجب أوّلاً غسل ذلك الموضع، ثم يجب غسل البدن كله، ولكن نقتصر على الأربعة دفعًا للحرج فيه أي بسبب وجوب غسل ذلك الموضع صار الوصف حجة من أي الخروج أي لكونه حدثاً حيث إن وجوب التطهير في البدن باعتبار ما يكون منه لا يتجزأ، فلما وجب غسل ذلك الموضع وجب غسل سائر البدن البتة، وهناك لم يجب غسل ذلك الموضع، فعدم الحكم لعدم العلة كأنه لم يوجد وهي الخروج ويورد عليه صاحب الجرح السائل، هو وجوب التطهير في البدن أي نقضا التعليل المذكور بعدم الوصف أي بعدم تحقق الوصف في مادة التخلّف. (القمر) وهو أي عدم الوصف أنه أي أن غير السائل. (القمر) بخارج الخارج الدم الذي تحت كل جلدة وخرج من موضعه إلى فوق الجلدة. (المحشي) بل باد: أي بل هو مستقر في موضعه. (القمر) البادي ما زايله الجلد فظهر الدم الذي تحت كل جلدة.(المحشي) السائل: هو دم في العروق، وانتقل إلى فوق الجلد، وخرج من موضعه إلى موضع آخر وسال.(المحشي) المعنى الثابت أي الذي له دخل في علية الوصف . (القمر) على الأربعة أي على الأعضاء الأربعة الرأس والوجه واليد والرجل. (القمر) باعتبار ما يكون منه أي بسبب ما يخرج من البدن، واحترز بهذا القول عن إصابة النجاسة من الخارج، فإنها توجب غسل ذلك الموضع، ولا توجب غسل جميع البدن ،بالإجماع كذا في "التحقيق". (القمر) وهناك: أي في غير السائل لم يجب غسل ذلك الموضع أي بالإجماع؛ لأنه ليس بخارج فليس بنجس. (القمر) فعدم الحكم: وهو كونه حدثًا العلة، فإن الجهة التي صارت بها العلة أي ذلك الوصف المؤثرة في الحكم أي كونه حدثًا، وهو وجوب غسل ذلك الموضع معدومة، وإن تحقق ذلك الوصف فكأنه لم يتحقق الوصف، والفرق بين الدفعين أن الأول منع ذات الوصف والثاني منع وصف عليته. (القمر) بعدم عطف على قوله : فيورد" عليه ما إذا لم يسل"، يعني يورد علينا من جانب الشافعي محليه في المثال المذكور بطريق النقض إيرادان: الأول: ما دفعناه بطريقين، والثاني: هو صاحب الجرح السائل، فإنه نجس خارج من البدن وليس بحدث ينقض الوضوء مادام الوقت باقيًا، فندفعه بالحكم، أي ندفعه بطريقين: الأول: بوجود الحكم وعدم تخلفه ببيان أنه حدث، موجب للتطهير بعد خروج الوقت يعني لا نسلّم أنه ليس بحدث بله لكن تأخر حكمه إلى ما بعد خروج الوقت ،وبالغرض أي ندفعه ثانيًا بوجود الغرض أي الدائم وهو القسم الثالث من العلة هو حدث وحصوله، فإن غرضنا التسوية بين الدم والبول وذلك حاصل فإن البول حدث، أي في ذاته أي في ذاته فإذا لزم صار عفوًا لقيام الوقت في صورة سلسل البول، فكذا هنا، يعني الدم كان حدثا، فإذا لزم صار عفوًا ليساوي البول المقيس عليه، فصار مجموع دفوع النقض أربعة. أي دام البول أي دام الأول: هو ما بينه المصنف بقوله : ما إذا لم يسل (القمر) بطريقين: أي دفع الوصف ودفع المعنى الثابت بالوصف. (القمر) مادام الوقت باقيًا: فإذا مضى الوقت صار حدثًا ينقض الوضوء. (القمر) بوجود الحكم: أي في مادة النقض والتخلف. (القمر) أنه : أي خروج هذا الدم السائل. (القمر) لكن تأخر حكمه أي عفوًا ودفعاً للحرج لمانع، وامتناع العمل لمانع لا يضرّ للتأثير، ثم اعلم أن هذا الدفع إنما يستقيم على قول من جوز تخصيص العلة، أي وجودها مع تخلف الحكم لمانع، وأما على قول من يأباه فلا يتأتى منه هذا الدفع، كذا قيل. (القمر) خروج الوقت إلخ : ضرورة قدرة المكلّف على الخروج عن عهدة التكليف، وهذا يلزمه الطهارة لصلاة أخرى بعد خروج الوقت بذلك الحدث لا بالخروج فإنه ليس بحدث بالإجماع، ولا يجوز له المسح على الخفين بعد خروج الوقت إذا لبسهما بعد السيلان والحكم قد يتصل بالسبب وقد يتأخر عنه لمانع كالبيع بشرط الخيار، وهذا النوع من الدفع إنما يستقيم على قول من جوز التخصيص كما بينا في "الكشف".
