باب القياس
بيان المعارضة
ولا ضير فيه والثاني: قلب الوصف شاهدًا على الخصم بعد أن كان شاهدا له، أي أي من نوعى القلب للخصم، فهو كقلب الجواب بجعل ظهره بطنًا وبطنه ظهرًا، فإن ظهر الوصف كان إليك والوجه إلى الخصم فإن قلب بعده فصار ظهره إليه ووجهه إليك، فهو معارضة من حيث إنه يدلّ على خلاف مدعى الخصم، وفيه مناقضة من حيث إن دليله لم يدلّ على مدعاه، وهذا هو الذي يسميه أهل المناظرة بالمعارضة بالقلب، ويجري في كثير من الأحيان في المغالطة العامة الورود كما بينوه في كتبهم، كقولهم في صوم رمضان: إنه أي الشافعية صوم فرض، فلا يتأدّى إلا بتعيين النية كصوم القضاء؛ فجعلت الفرضية علة للتعين، فعارضناه بالقلب، وجعلنا الفرضية دليلاً على عدم التعيّن فقلنا: لما كان صومًا فرضًا أي صوم رمضان استغني عن تعيين النية بعد تعينه كصوم القضاء إنما يحتاج إلى تعيين واحد فقط، لا زائد أي شرعًا فيه فهذا كذلك، لكنه إنما يتعين بالشروع، وهذا تعيّن قبله من جانب الشارع عليها حيث قال : إذا انسلخ شعبان فلا صوم إلا عن رمضان، فصوم رمضان وصوم القضاء الوصف: أي الذي جعله المستدل علة . (القمر) على الخصم أي على ضرر المستدل.(القمر) كان إليك فإنه كان شاهدًا عليك والوجه إلى الخصم فإنه كان شاهدا له، فإذا قلب ذلك الوصف بعده، فصار ظهره إليه أي إلى الخصم فإنه صار شاهدًا عليه ووجهه إليك، فإنه صار شاهدًا لك. في المغالطة التي عم ورودها على كل مدعي والمغالطة هو القياس الفاسد، وإن شئت تفصيل المغالطة العامة الورود مع جواباتها فارجع إلى تأليفنا المسمى بـ"معين الغائصين في ردّ المغالطين". (القمر) كصوم القضاء: فإنه لا يتأدّى بدون تعين النية (القمر) لا زائد فيه أي ليس محتاجًا إلى تعيين آخر بعد تعينه. (القمر) فهذا كذلك إلخ: أي صوم رمضان، فهما سيان في ذلك. (القمر) لكنه إلخ لما كان يتوهّم من قبله: استغنى عن تعيين النية بعد تعينه كصوم القضاء أنه لا فرق بينها فاستدرك بهذا وقال لكنه أي صوم القضاء إنما يتعين بعد الشروع في الصوم، وهذا أي صوم رمضان تعين قبله .إلخ بالشروع اي في الصوم حتى لو نوى للنفل قبل الصبح الصادق بعد نية القضاء تصح نية النفل، وذلك لعدم تحقق الشروع. وهذا أي صوم رمضان تعين قبله أي قبل الشروع.
فكذا سواء في أنه لا يحتاج إلى تعيين بعد تعيّن لكن الرمضان لما كان معينا قبل الشروع فلا يحتاج إلى تعيين العبد، وصوم القضاء لما لم يكن متعيّنا قبل الشروع احتاج إلى تعيين العبد ،مرة، وقد تقلب العلة من وجه آخر غير الوجهين المذكورين، وهو ضعيف كقولهم أي الشافعية في حق النوافل حيث لا تلزم بالشروع، ولا تقضى بالإفساد، وعندهم هذه عبادة لا يمضي في فاسدها، أي إذا فسدت بنفسها من غير إفساد بظهور الحدث من المصلي لا يجب إتمامها، وهذا بخلاف الحج فإنه إذا فسد يجب فيه المضي أي بالشروع والقضاء بعده، فلا تلزم بالشروع كالوضوء، فإنه لما لم يمض في فاسده لم يلزم بالشروع فيقال لهم: لما كان كذلك وجب أن يستوي فيه أي في النفل عمل النذر والشروع باللزوم كما استوى عملهما في الوضوء بعدم اللزوم فالوصف الذي جعله الشافعي الله دليلاً على عدم اللزوم بالشروع في النفل، وهو عدم الإمضاء في الفساد جعلناه علة لاستواء لا في الإفساد الحدث بالشروع، (السنبلي) سواء إلخ قلت وهما مفترقان من حيث إن الرمضان لما كان متعينًا من قبل الشارع لا يحتاج إلخ. (السنبلي) وقد تقلب العلة إلخ فيدل هذا القلب على حكم يلزم منه نقيض الحكم السابق. (القمر) الوجهين المذكورين أي قلب العلة حكمًا والحكم علة، وقلب الوصف شاهدًا عليه بعد أن كان شاهدا له. (القمر) وهو ضعيف أي فاسد كذا في "التحقيق" . (القمر) النوافل من الصلاة وكذا الصوم. (القمر) أي إذا فسدت أي الصلوات النوافل بنفسها إلخ، وما في "مسير" الدائر" : إذا فسد بنفسه من غير إفساد لظهور من المصلي إلخ فعجيب، فإن الصوم كيف يفسد بالحدث. (القمر) فلا تلزم بالشروع فلا يلزم القضاء بالإفساد . (القمر) لم يلزم بالشروع فلا يلزم القضاء بالإفساد . (القمر) لما كان كذلك: أي لا يمضي في فاسدها كالوضوء. (القمر) باللزوم: أي يلزم النفل بالنذر وكذا بالشروع. (القمر) عملهما في الوضوء إلخ أي كما يستوي عمل النذر والشروع في الوضوء حيث لا يلزم الوضوء كان عندكم أصلاً ومقيسًا عليه كذلك يجب أن يستوي عمل النذر والشروع في الفرع والاستواء في النوافل لا يمكن أن يكون بعدم اللزوم؛ إذ النوافل بالنذر تلزم بالإجماع، فوجب أن تلزم بالشروع أيضا ليتحقق الاستواء فيهما، فالوصف الذي جعله أصحاب الشافعي لله علة لعدم اللزوم وهو عدم الإمضاء في الفساد جعلناه علة للاستواء ويلزم منه اللزوم فكان قلبًا من هذا الوجه (السنبلي) وهو: أي ذلك الوصف الذي جعله الشافعي له دليلاً. (القمر) بالشروع،
Chapter of Qiyas: Explanation of Mu'arada (Counter-argument). And there is no harm in it. The second type: Inverting the description (wasf) to be a witness against the opponent after it was a witness for him. That is, one of the two types of qalb for the opponent. It is like turning a garment inside out, making its outer side inner and its inner side outer. So if the description's outer side was towards you and its face towards the opponent, then if it is inverted, its outer side becomes towards him and its face towards you. So it is mu'arada from the aspect that it indicates contrary to the opponent's claim, and it contains contradiction (munaqada) from the aspect that his evidence does not indicate his claim. This is what the dialecticians call mu'arada bi al-qalb. It often occurs in the common fallacy (al-mughalata al-amma al-wurud) as they explained in their books. For example, their statement concerning the fast of Ramadan: The Shafi'is say it is an obligatory fast, so it is not valid except with specification of intention (ta'yin al-niyya) like the make-up fast (qada). So they made obligation (fardiyya) the cause for specification. We countered them by qalb, and made obligation a proof for non-requirement of specification. We said: Since it is an obligatory fast (i.e., Ramadan), it is dispensed from specifying intention after its determinateness (ta'ayyun), just as the make-up fast only needs one specification (of intention) and no more—this is legally the case. So this is similar. But the make-up fast becomes determined (muta'ayyin) only upon commencement (shuru'), while this (Ramadan) is determined before that from the side of the Lawgiver as He said: 'When Sha'ban passes, there is no fasting except for Ramadan.' So the fast of Ramadan and the make-up fast... (commentary continues).
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Noor al-Anwar explains a second method of mu'arada (counter-argument) called qalb (inversion). The author first defines qalb al-wasf: taking a description that the opponent used as evidence for his claim and inverting it to argue the opposite. He illustrates this with the example of the fast of Ramadan versus the make-up fast. The Shafi'is argue that since Ramadan fast is obligatory (fard), it requires a specific intention (ta'yin al-niyya), just like a make-up fast. The Hanafi rebuttal uses qalb: the very attribute of being obligatory (fardiyya) can be inverted to argue that no specific intention is needed because the fast is already determined (mu'ayyan) by the season itself. The Hanafi position is that for Ramadan, the obligation dispenses the worshipper from specifying which fast is intended, unlike a make-up fast which requires specification because it is not predetermined. The passage also mentions a hadith: 'When Sha'ban passes, there is no fasting except for Ramadan,' which supports the determinateness of Ramadan. The commentary then discusses a third, weaker form of qalb applied to supererogatory acts of worship (nawafil). Here, the Shafi'is argue that nawafil are not binding upon commencement (shuru') because they do not require completion if invalidated, unlike Hajj. The Hanafi counter-argument uses the example of wudu, which is neither binding upon commencement, showing that the property of 'not going forward in its invalid state' does not necessarily imply non-binding; rather, it can be inverted to argue that supererogatory acts should be as binding as a vowed act (nadhr) once commenced, to achieve consistency. The passage stresses that this type of qalb is weak and often used in fallacious arguments, but it is a recognized method in Hanafi dialectics.

Key Terms
القلب (al-qalb): Inverting an opponent's evidence (wasf or illa) to support the opposite claim.
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): Presenting a counter-argument that refutes or neutralizes the opponent's evidence.
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specifying the intended fast (e.g., intending specifically Ramadan) in the intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi response using qalb argue about the necessity of specific intention (ta'yin) for the Ramadan fast?
A) It is required because it is a fard fast.
B) It is not required because the fast is already determined by the season.
C) It is required only for make-up fasts.
D) It is not required because the hadith says so.

Key Takeaway
Qalb is a powerful dialectical tool that inverts an opponent's own evidence to support the opposite claim, as exemplified in the Hanafi position on intention in Ramadan fasting.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
The Weak Qalb (Inversion) in Qiyas: The Case of Nawafil Obligation
Explaining an invalid inversion (qalb) in qiyas using the nawafil-shuru' debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the validity of a qalb (inversion) argument in qiyas by identifying whether it directly yields the opposite ruling and whether the claimed equality is consistent across original and branch.

Core Idea
A qalb must yield the explicit opposite ruling; mere equality is insufficient.

This passage examines a specific application of qalb al-illah (inversion of the legal cause) in the context of supererogatory acts (nawafil). The Shafi'is argue that nawafil are not binding upon commencement, analogizing to wudu'. The Hanafis respond by inverting the same illah to argue for binding. The text explains why this particular qalb is weak and distinguishes it from the proper 'aks (converse) used for tarjih. Understanding this critique is essential for mastering the methodology of qiyas and i'tirad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i position and its illah
The Shafi'is claim that supererogatory acts (nawafil) are not binding upon commencement and need not be made up if invalidated. Their illah is 'non-continuance in the invalid state' — the act is void upon a nullifier, analogous to wudu'.
The illah is the shared attribute that justifies the analogy.
2
State the Hanafi qalb argument
The Hanafis take the same illah (non-continuance) and use it to argue for equality (istiwā') between vow and commencement. Since a vow in nawafil is binding by consensus, equality would imply commencement also makes it binding.
This is the inversion: using the opponent's own illah to derive the opposite ruling.
3
Analyze why this qalb is weak
Two reasons: (1) It does not directly assert the opposite ruling (binding by commencement), but only equality which entails it. (2) The claimed equality is inconsistent — in wudu', both vow and commencement result in non-binding, while in nawafil both result in binding. So the illah does not produce the same relation in the original and branch (wudu' vs. nawafil).
A valid qalb must directly produce the explicit opposite, not an intermediate.
4
Distinguish from proper 'aks
Proper 'aks follows the pattern: if the illah is present, ruling present; if absent, ruling absent (ittirād wa in'ikās). This is a sign of a strong illah and is used for tarjih. The attempted inversion here is not a true 'aks but a weak qalb.
True 'aks is a preferred quality for an illah, not a method of objection.

Source Text

باب القياس
بيان المعارضة
سواء في أنه لا يحتاج إلى تعيين بعد تعيّن لكن الرمضان لما كان معينا قبل الشروع فلا يحتاج إلى تعيين العبد، وصوم القضاء لما لم يكن متعيّنا قبل الشروع احتاج إلى تعيين العبد ،مرة، وقد تقلب العلة من وجه آخر غير الوجهين المذكورين، وهو ضعيف كقولهم أي الشافعية في حق النوافل حيث لا تلزم بالشروع، ولا تقضى بالإفساد، وعندهم أي بعد الشروع هذه عبادة لا يمضي في فاسدها، أي إذا فسدت بنفسها من غير إفساد بظهور أي النوافل الحدث من المصلي لا يجب إتمامها، وهذا بخلاف الحج فإنه إذا فسد يجب فيه المضي أي بعد الشروع أي بأفعال الحج والقضاء بعده، فلا تلزم بالشروع كالوضوء، فإنه لما لم يمض في فاسده لم يلزم بالشروع أي في العام القابل فيقال لهم: لما كان كذلك وجب أن يستوي فيه أي في النفل عمل النذر والشروع باللزوم كما استوى عملهما في الوضوء بعدم اللزوم فالوصف الذي جعله الشافعي الله دليلاً عمل النذر والشروع على عدم اللزوم بالشروع في النفل، وهو عدم الإمضاء في الفساد جعلناه علة لاستواء لا في الإفساد الحدث سواء إلخ قلت وهما مفترقان من حيث إن الرمضان لما كان متعينًا من قبل الشارع لا يحتاج إلخ. (السنبلي) وقد تقلب العلة إلخ فيدل هذا القلب على حكم يلزم منه نقيض الحكم السابق. (القمر) الوجهين المذكورين أي قلب العلة حكمًا والحكم علة، وقلب الوصف شاهدًا عليه بعد أن كان شاهدا له. (القمر) وهو ضعيف أي فاسد كذا في "التحقيق" . (القمر) النوافل من الصلاة وكذا الصوم. (القمر) أي إذا فسدت أي الصلوات النوافل بنفسها إلخ، وما في "مسير" الدائر" : إذا فسد بنفسه من غير إفساد لظهور من المصلي إلخ فعجيب، فإن الصوم كيف يفسد بالحدث. (القمر) فلا تلزم بالشروع فلا يلزم القضاء بالإفساد . (القمر) لم يلزم بالشروع فلا يلزم القضاء بالإفساد . (القمر) لما كان كذلك: أي لا يمضي في فاسدها كالوضوء. (القمر) باللزوم: أي يلزم النفل بالنذر وكذا بالشروع. (القمر) عملهما في الوضوء إلخ أي كما يستوي عمل النذر والشروع في الوضوء حيث لا يلزم الوضوء كان عندكم أصلاً ومقيسًا عليه كذلك يجب أن يستوي عمل النذر والشروع في الفرع والاستواء في النوافل لا يمكن أن يكون بعدم اللزوم؛ إذ النوافل بالنذر تلزم بالإجماع، فوجب أن تلزم بالشروع أيضا ليتحقق الاستواء فيهما، فالوصف الذي جعله أصحاب الشافعي لله علة لعدم اللزوم وهو عدم الإمضاء في الفساد جعلناه علة للاستواء ويلزم منه اللزوم فكان قلبًا من هذا الوجه (السنبلي) وهو: أي ذلك الوصف الذي جعله الشافعي له دليلاً. (القمر) بالشروع، النذر ،والشروع، ويلزم منه اللزوم بالشروع فكان قلبًا من هذه الحيثية، وإنما كان هذا القلب ضعيفًا؛ لأنه ما أتى بصريح نقيض الخصم أعني اللزوم بالشروع، بل أتى بالاستواء الملزوم له؛ ولأن الاستواء مختلف ثبوتًا وزوالاً ، ففى الوضوء من حيث كونه لنقيض الخصم أي استواء النذر والشروع أي في الأصل والفرع أي هذا القلب الأول غير لازم بالشروع والنذر ، وفي النفل من حيث كونه لازما بهما، وسمي هذا عكساً، أي شبيهًا بالعكس، لا عكسا حقيقيًا؛ لأن العكس الحقيقي هو ردّ الشيء على سننه كما يقال في قولنا ما يلزم بالنذر يلزم بالشروع كالحج وما لا يلزم بالنذر لا يلزم بالشروع كالوضوء، وهو يصلح للترجيح على ما سيأتي؛ لأن ما يطرد وينعكس أولى مما يطرد ولا ينعكس. وهذا لما كان ردّ الشيء على خلاف سننه الأوّل كان داخلاً اللزوم بالشروع وهذا نقيض حكم المعلل فإنه عدم اللزوم بالشروع (القمر) لأنه ما أتى إلخ: فإن العاكس أثبت التسوية والمستدل لا ينفيها، فلم يثبت القلب، فلذا كان هذا القلب فاسدًا غير مقبول. (القمر) بالاستواء: أي باستواء الشروع النذر . (المحشي) ثبوتًا : لأن استواء النذر والشروع في النوافل باللزوم.(المحشي) وزوالا: دون استواء النذر والشروع في الوضوء لعدم اللزوم. (المحشي) ففي الوضوء إلخ: يعني أن النذر والشروع مستويان في الوضوء الذي هو الأصل بطريق العدم، فإنه لا يلزم بهما إجماعا، وهما مستويان في الفرع، أي النفل بطريق الوجود فإنه يلزم بهما، فالاستواء صار مختلفًا في الأصل والفرع ثبوتًا وزوالاً فكيف يصح القياس للنفل على الوضوء، فإن القياس إبانة مثل حكم أحد المذكورين بمثل علته في الآخر وهو لم يوجد.(القمر) وهو ردّ الشيء إلخ: أي رجعه من ورائه على طريقه الأول والسنن (القمر) بالنذر إلخ: هذا عكس على سنة الأول، فإن في الأول كان الوجود علة للوجود ، وفي الثاني صار العدم علة للعدم. (القمر) وهو يصلح إلخ : أي هذا العكس الحقيقي ليس بقدح في العلة، بل هو مرجّح للعلة على غيرها، فإن العلة التي تطرد وتنعكس أولى من العلة التي تطرد ولا تنعكس فإن الانعكاس يدل على أن للحكم زيادة تعلّق بالوصف، فيوجب هذا زيادة قوة في كون الوصف علة . (القمر) وهو يصلح إلخ: جواب سؤال مقدر، وهو: أن هذا القلب لما كان فاسدا فما الفائدة في ذكره في هذا المقام. فأجاب بما حاصله ظاهر . (السنبلي) على ما سيأتي: أي في مبحث ما يقع به الترجيح. (القمر) ما يطرد وينعكس إلخ الاطراد هو الوجود عند الوجود، والانعكاس هو العدم عند العدم. (القمر) لما كان بيان أن هذا ليس بعكس بل شبيه بالعكس. ردّ الشيء إلخ : فإن المعلل جعل الوصف المذكور أي عدم الإمضاء في الفاسد علة لعدم اللزوم بالشروع، والعاكس جعل ذلك الوصف المذكور علة للاستواء بين النذر والشروع فيلزم اللزوم بالشروع ضرورة لزومه بالنذر إجماعًا، كذا قيل. (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of Opposition. Equality in that it does not need specification after being determined, but Ramadan, since it is determined before commencement, does not need specification of the slave, and the fast of make-up, since it was not determined before commencement, needed specification of the slave once. And the illah may be inverted from another aspect other than the two mentioned aspects, and it is weak, like their statement (i.e., the Shafi'is) regarding supererogatory acts (nawafil) where they do not become binding by commencement, nor are they made up if invalidated. And according to them, after commencement, this worship does not continue in its invalid state, i.e., if it becomes invalid by itself without invalidation due to the appearance of an event (hadath) from the pray-er, its completion is not obligatory. And this is unlike Hajj, for if it becomes invalid, continuation (with actions of Hajj) is obligatory after commencement, and make-up later. So it does not become binding by commencement like wudu', for since wudu' does not continue in its invalid state, it did not become binding by commencement. So it is said to them: When it is so, then it must be that in supererogatory acts, the action of vow and commencement are equal in binding, just as their action in wudu' is equal in non-binding. So the description which al-Shafi'i made a proof for non-binding by commencement in supererogatory acts, namely non-continuance in invalidity, we made it an illah for equality. They said: And they are different in that Ramadan, since it is determined by the Lawgiver, does not need specification. (al-Sanbali) And the illah may be inverted, etc., so this inversion indicates a ruling that necessitates the opposite of the previous ruling. (al-Qamar) The two mentioned aspects: inverting the illah into a ruling and the ruling into an illah, and inverting the description from a witness for it to a witness against it. (al-Qamar) And it is weak, i.e., invalid, as in al-Tahqiq. (al-Qamar) The nawafil are from prayer and likewise fasting. (al-Qamar) Then they do not become binding by commencement, so make-up is not required by invalidation. (al-Qamar) When it is so: i.e., it does not continue in its invalid state like wudu'. (al-Qamar) By binding: i.e., the supererogatory act becomes binding by vow and likewise by commencement. (al-Qamar) Their action in wudu' etc., i.e., just as the action of vow and commencement in wudu' are equal where wudu' is not binding according to you as an original and measured upon, so must the action of vow and commencement be equal in the branch, and equality in nawafil cannot be by non-binding; for nawafil by vow are binding by consensus, so they must be binding by commencement also to achieve equality in them. So the description which the Shafi'is made an illah for non-binding, namely non-continuance in invalidity, we made it an illah for equality, and from it binding follows, so it was an inversion from this aspect. (al-Sanbali) And it is: i.e., that description which al-Shafi'i made a proof. (al-Qamar) By commencement, vow, and commencement, and from it follows binding by commencement, so it was an inversion from this perspective. And this inversion was weak only because it did not bring the explicit opposite of the opponent, namely binding by commencement, but brought equality which necessitates it; and because equality differs in affirmation and negation: in wudu', being not binding by commencement and vow, and in the supererogatory act, being binding by both. And this was called 'aks, i.e., similar to the converse, not a true converse; because the true converse is returning the thing on its path, as is said: Whatever is binding by vow is binding by commencement like Hajj, and whatever is not binding by vow is not binding by commencement like wudu'. And it is suitable for tarjih as will come; because what is consistent (mutṭarid) and converse (mun'akis) is preferable to what is consistent but not converse. And this, since it was returning the thing contrary to its first path, was included. Binding by commencement is the opposite of the mu'allil's ruling, for his ruling is non-binding by commencement. (al-Qamar) Because it did not bring etc.: for the one doing inversion affirmed equality, and the one adducing proof does not negate it, so inversion was not established, hence this inversion was invalid and unacceptable. (al-Qamar) By equality: i.e., by equality of commencement and vow. (al-Muhashi) Affirmation: because equality of vow and commencement in nawafil is by binding. (al-Muhashi) Negation: unlike equality of vow and commencement in wudu' due to non-binding. (al-Muhashi) So in wudu' etc.: meaning that vow and commencement are equal in wudu', which is the original, by way of non-existence, for it is not binding by either by consensus, and they are equal in the branch, i.e., supererogatory, by way of existence, for it is binding by both. So equality became different in original and branch in affirmation and negation, so how can qiyas of supererogatory upon wudu' be valid? For qiyas is showing the likeness of the ruling of one of the mentioned to the likeness of its illah in the other, and it was not found. (al-Qamar) And it is returning the thing etc.: i.e., returning it from behind on its first path and way. (al-Qamar) By vow etc.: this is a converse on the first path, for in the first the existence was the illah for existence, and in the second the non-existence became the illah for non-existence. (al-Qamar) And it is suitable etc.: i.e., this true converse is not a defect in the illah, but rather a preponderator of the illah over others, for the illah that is both consistent and converse is preferable to the illah that is consistent but not converse, because the converse indicates that the ruling has increased connection with the description, so this necessitates increased strength in the description being an illah. (al-Qamar) And it is suitable etc.: answer to an implied question: Since this inversion is invalid, what is the benefit of mentioning it in this context? He answered with what is apparently clear. (al-Sanbali) As will come: i.e., in the section on what constitutes tarjih. (al-Qamar) What is consistent and converse etc.: al-ittirād is existence upon existence, and al-in'ikās is non-existence upon non-existence. (al-Qamar) Since it was an explanation that this is not a converse but similar to a converse. Returning the thing etc.: for the mu'allil made the mentioned description, i.e., non-continuance in the invalid, the illah for non-binding by commencement, and the one doing inversion made that same description the illah for equality between vow and commencement, so binding by commencement follows necessarily due to its binding by vow by consensus, as it is said. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of a specific type of 'qalb al-illah' (inversion of the legal cause) in qiyas, used in a Hanafi counter-argument against the Shafi'i position that supererogatory acts (nawafil) are not binding upon commencement and are not required to be made up if invalidated. The Shafi'is argue based on an attribute: that the act does not continue in its invalid state (i.e., it becomes void at the appearance of a nullifier, like hadath). They analogize this to wudu', which also does not continue in an invalid state and is not binding upon commencement. The Hanafis respond by employing a qalb: they take the same attribute (non-continuance in invalidity) and use it as the cause (illah) for the equality between vow and commencement in terms of binding. Since a vow in nawafil is binding by consensus, this equality would imply that commencement also makes it binding. Thus the Hanafis attempt to invert the Shafi'i's own proof to derive the opposite ruling. However, the text explains that this particular qalb is weak (da'if) for two reasons. First, it does not directly produce the explicit opposite of the opponent's ruling (i.e., binding by commencement); instead it only produces equality (istiwā'), which would necessitate binding but is not the direct opposite. Second, the equality itself is inconsistent across the original (wudu') and the branch (nawafil): in wudu', both vow and commencement result in non-binding, while in nawafil both result in binding. So the claimed equality does not hold uniformly. The text then distinguishes this weak qalb from the proper 'aks (converse), which is a valid method of reasoning. The proper 'aks follows the pattern: if the illah is present, the ruling is present; if the illah is absent, the ruling is absent. This is called 'ittirād wa in'ikās' (consistency and converse). Such a well-behaved illah is considered stronger and can be used for tarjih (preference) between conflicting analogies. The passage concludes that this discussion of qalb is beneficial for understanding how to evaluate the strength of an illah, even if the specific inversion here is rejected. The Hanafi position, implicit in the critique, adheres to the principle that for a valid qalb, the inverted illah must directly yield the opposite of the opponent's ruling without intermediate steps.

Key Terms
قلب العلة (qalb al-illah): Inverting the legal cause (illah) in a qiyas argument by taking the opponent's illah and using it to derive the opposite ruling or a contradictory conclusion.
عكس ('aks): A proper converse in qiyas where the illah co-extends with the ruling: if the illah is present the ruling is present, and if absent the ruling is absent.
اطراد (ittirād): Consistency of the illah: whenever the illah is found, the ruling is found.
انعكاس (in'ikās): The converse of the illah: whenever the illah is absent, the ruling is absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the Hanafi qalb regarding nawafil considered weak according to the text?
A) Because the Shafi'is do not accept the illah of non-continuance.
B) Because it does not directly state binding by commencement but only equality, and the equality is inconsistent across wudu' and nawafil.
C) Because the Hanafis later abandoned this argument.
D) Because the qalb relies on an analogical inference to Hajj, which is not permissible.

Key Takeaway
A valid qalb must directly yield the opposite ruling, and the equality it relies on must be consistent across cases; otherwise it is weak and does not refute the opponent.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

8 min
The Weak Inverse (Shabih bi al-'Aks) in Qiyas
Explaining the weak inverse and its distinction from real inverse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the weak inverse (shabih bi al-'aks) and the real inverse (al-'aks al-haqiqi) in Hanafi qiyas, and explain why the weak inverse is considered corrupt.

Core Idea
A weak inverse fails because it does not directly negate the opponent's claim—it only shows equality, not the opposite ruling.

In this passage from a classical usul text, the author explains a type of argument used in mu'arada (opposition) called the weak inverse. Using the example of obligations by vow (nadhr) and commencement (shuru') in wudu' and supererogatory acts, he shows why this inverse is not a valid refutation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly evaluating qiyas arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the example of wudu' and supererogatory acts
The passage uses two acts: wudu' (ablution) and supererogatory prayers (nafl). In wudu', both vow and commencement (shuru') do not create an obligation (it is not wajib by consensus). In supererogatory, both create an obligation.
This sets up the original (asl) and branch (far') for qiyas.
2
Identify the mu'alil's claim and the weak inverse's attempt
The mu'alil (original proponent) claims that non-validity of the corrupt act is the 'illa causing non-obligation by commencement. The weak inverse argues that equality between vow and commencement should instead cause obligation by commencement.
The weak inverse tries to flip the reasoning but does not directly negate the mu'alil's claim.
3
See why the weak inverse is weak
It does not bring the clear opposite (narih al-nadid) of the opponent's claim. It only shows equality, which the opponent does not deny. Moreover, equality differs between the original and branch: in wudu' both are absent; in supererogatory both are present. Thus the 'illa is not consistent.
The marginal notes emphasize that the weak inverse is corrupt because it fails to establish a proper contradiction.
4
Contrast with the real inverse and its role in tarjih
A real inverse would state: 'What is obligated by vow is obligated by commencement, like Hajj; what is not obligated by vow is not obligated by commencement, like wudu'.' This shows consistency and inverse consistency (tard wa in'ikas), making the 'illa stronger for preponderance (tarjih).
The real inverse is not a criticism but a validator; it indicates that the ruling has additional attachment to the description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
بيان المعارضة
النذر ،والشروع، ويلزم منه اللزوم بالشروع فكان قلبًا من هذه الحيثية، وإنما كان هذا القلب ضعيفًا؛ لأنه ما أتى بصريح نقيض الخصم أعني اللزوم بالشروع، بل أتى بالاستواء الملزوم له؛ ولأن الاستواء مختلف ثبوتًا وزوالاً ، ففى الوضوء من حيث كونه لنقيض الخصم أي استواء النذر والشروع أي في الأصل والفرع أي هذا القلب الأول غير لازم بالشروع والنذر ، وفي النفل من حيث كونه لازما بهما، وسمي هذا عكساً، أي شبيهًا بالعكس، لا عكسا حقيقيًا؛ لأن العكس الحقيقي هو ردّ الشيء على سننه كما يقال في قولنا ما يلزم بالنذر يلزم بالشروع كالحج وما لا يلزم بالنذر لا يلزم بالشروع كالوضوء، وهو يصلح للترجيح على ما سيأتي؛ لأن ما يطرد وينعكس أولى مما يطرد ولا ينعكس. وهذا لما كان ردّ الشيء على خلاف سننه الأوّل كان داخلاً اللزوم بالشروع وهذا نقيض حكم المعلل فإنه عدم اللزوم بالشروع (القمر) لأنه ما أتى إلخ: فإن العاكس أثبت التسوية والمستدل لا ينفيها، فلم يثبت القلب، فلذا كان هذا القلب فاسدًا غير مقبول. (القمر)

بيان المعارضة
الخالصة عن معنى المناقضة, ويسمى في القلب شبيهًا بالعكس, وإنما جعله عكسا اتباعًا لفخر الإسلام له. (القمر) شبيها بالعكس: أي في تحقيق الردّ مطلقا.
Chapter of Qiyas. Statement of Opposition. The vow and the commencement (shuru'), and from it follows obligation due to commencement, so it was a reversal (qalb) from this respect. And this reversal was weak because it did not bring the clear opposite of the opponent's claim, i.e., obligation due to commencement, but rather brought the equality that implies it; and because equality differs in affirmation and negation. So in wudu' with respect to being the opposite of the opponent's claim, i.e., equality of vow and commencement in the original and the branch, this first reversal is not necessary by commencement and vow, and in supererogatory acts with respect to being necessary by them, and this is called 'aks (inverse), i.e., resembling the inverse, not a real inverse; because the real inverse is to return the thing to its proper way, as it is said: what is obligated by vow is obligated by commencement, like Hajj, and what is not obligated by vow is not obligated by commencement, like wudu', and it is valid for preponderance (tarjih) as will come; because what is consistent (tard) and inversely consistent (in'ikas) is more worthy than what is consistent but not inversely consistent. And this, because it was returning the thing contrary to its first way, was included in obligation by commencement, and this is the opposite of the mu'alil's ruling, which is non-obligation by commencement. (al-Qamar) 'because he did not bring etc.': the one who performed the inverse established equality and the claimant does not negate it, so the reversal was not established, hence this reversal is corrupt and unacceptable. (al-Qamar) 'by equality': i.e., by equality of commencement and vow. (al-Muhashi) 'affirmation': because equality of vow and commencement in supererogatory acts is by obligation. (al-Muhashi) 'and negation': without equality of vow and commencement in wudu' due to non-obligation. (al-Muhashi) 'so in wudu' etc.': meaning that vow and commencement are equal in wudu' which is the original by way of non-existence — for it is not obligated by them by consensus — and they are equal in the branch, i.e., supererogatory, by way of existence — for it is obligated by them. So equality became different in the original and branch in affirmation and negation, so how can qiyas of supererogatory upon wudu' be valid? Because qiyas is clarifying a similar ruling of one of the mentioned things by similar 'illa in the other, and it is not found. (al-Qamar) 'and it is returning the thing etc.': i.e., returning it from behind to its first way and path. (al-Qamar) 'by vow etc.': this is an inverse on the path of the first, for in the first existence was the 'illa of existence, and in the second non-existence became the 'illa of non-existence. (al-Qamar) 'and it is valid etc.': i.e., this real inverse is not a criticism of the 'illa, but rather it is a preponderator for the 'illa over others, for the 'illa that is consistent and inversely consistent is more worthy than the 'illa that is consistent but not inversely consistent, for inverse consistency indicates that the ruling has an additional attachment to the description, and this necessitates additional strength in the description being an 'illa. (al-Qamar) 'and it is valid etc.': an answer to an implied question: since this reversal was corrupt, what benefit is there in mentioning it in this context? He answered with what is apparent. (al-Sunbuli) 'as will come': i.e., in the section on what constitutes preponderance. (al-Qamar) 'what is consistent and inversely consistent etc.': consistency (tard) is existence upon existence, and inverse consistency (in'ikas) is non-existence upon non-existence. (al-Qamar) 'because it was clarifying that this is not an inverse but similar to an inverse. Returning the thing etc.': for the mu'alil made the mentioned description, i.e., non-validity in the corrupt, the 'illa for non-obligation by commencement, and the one performing the inverse made that mentioned description the 'illa for equality between vow and commencement, so obligation by commencement necessarily follows obligation by vow by consensus, as is said. (al-Qamar)

Statement of Opposition. The pure one without the meaning of contradiction, and it is called in reversal similar to the inverse, and he only made it an inverse following Fakhr al-Islam. (al-Qamar) 'similar to the inverse': i.e., in effecting the refutation absolutely.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage belongs to the chapter on Qiyas, specifically the section on Mu'arada (opposition). The author explains a type of weak 'aks (inverse argument) used in qiyas. The example involves comparing obligations by vow (nadhr) and obligations by commencement (shuru') in acts of worship like wudu' (ablution) and supererogatory acts (nafl). The weak inverse attempts to show equality between the two, but fails because it does not directly negate the opponent's claim (the mu'alil's ruling that commencement does not obligate in wudu'). The author distinguishes between a real inverse (which shows the opposite ruling when the 'illa is absent) and a weak inverse (which only shows equality without directly contradicting). The real inverse is valid for preponderance because it demonstrates that the 'illa is both consistent (tard) and inversely consistent (in'ikas). The marginal notes, particularly from al-Qamar, clarify that this weak inverse is corrupt because the 'illa is not properly established, and the equality differs between the original and branch. The passage concludes by noting that this type of argument is called similar to the inverse ('aks) following the terminology of Fakhr al-Islam.

Key Terms
عكس (aks): An inverse argument in qiyas that shows the opposite ruling when the 'illa is absent; can be real (haqiqi) or weak (shabih)
قلب (qalb): Reversal; an argument that attempts to flip the opponent's 'illa to produce a contradictory ruling
اطراد وانعكاس (tard wa in'ikas): Consistency and inverse consistency; criteria for a valid 'illa

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the weak inverse (shabih bi al-'aks) considered corrupt in Hanafi usul?
A) It uses a false 'illa that cannot be verified.
B) It does not bring the clear opposite of the opponent's claim.
C) It relies on consensus which is not binding in qiyas.
D) It contradicts the principle of istihsan.

Key Takeaway
The weak inverse (shabih bi al-'aks) is not a valid refutation because it does not produce the clear opposite of the opponent's ruling.

Types of Mu'arada in the Ruling of the Branch
Explaining the two sections of mu'arada in the ruling of the branch

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two types of mu'arada in the ruling of the branch (without increase and with explanatory increase) and apply the principle of tarjih to resolve conflict between competing 'illas.

Core Idea
Mu'arada in the branch ruling is resolved by tarjih — preponderance of one 'illa over another.

In Hanafi usul, when a claimant presents a proof based on a valid 'illa, the opponent may respond with mu'arada, i.e., a counter-proof that yields the opposite ruling. This passage from Noor al-Anwar explains two forms of mu'arada in the ruling of the branch (far'): one is pure opposition without any added qualification, and the other includes an explanatory increase. Understanding this distinction is crucial for navigating conflicts of 'illas and applying tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of mu'arada
Understand that mu'arada is opposition by presenting a competing 'illa without attempting to nullify the opponent's 'illa. It is a standard technique in munazarah (disputation).
Mu'arada differs from ibtal (nullification); it simply offers a counter-'illa.
2
Recognize the first type: without increase
This is pure opposition (mahd al-muqabala). The objector presents an 'illa that directly yields the opposite ruling of the mu'alil, with no added qualifications.
Example: wiping on the head is like wiping on khuff, so triple repetition is not recommended.
3
Recognize the second type: with explanatory increase
Here, the objector includes an additional phrase that clarifies the intended meaning. This addition does not change the ruling but explains its scope.
Example: 'after its completion' specifies when triple repetition is not recommended.
4
Understand the need for tarjih
When two valid 'illas conflict, neither can be acted upon simultaneously. Tarjih (preponderance) is necessary to determine which 'illa is stronger.
The first type is considered stronger because it stands without extra explanation.
5
Analyze the example of wiping on the head
The Shafi'i argues that wiping is a rukn, so triple repetition is recommended (by qiyas with washing). The Hanafi responds with mu'arada: wiping is just wiping, so triple repetition is not recommended (by qiyas with wiping on khuff). This illustrates the first type.
The Hanafi objection is pure opposition without additional explanation.

And the second: Mu'arada. This, in the terminology of disputation, is opposition by something else, and it is of two types: one of them is opposition in the ruling of the branch (far'), such that the objector says: we have a proof indicating contrary to your ruling in the analogized thing. It has five sections, all of which are valid and used in usul al-fiqh as he said, and it is valid whether he opposes it by the opposite of that ruling without increase — this is the first section thereof, such as by mentioning an 'illa indicating the opposite of the mu'alil's ruling explicitly without increase or decrease, like when al-Shafi'i says: wiping is a pillar (rukn) in wudu', so its triple repetition is recommended (yusann), like washing (ghusl). We say: wiping on the head — i.e., in pure opposition — is wiping, so its triple repetition is not recommended, like wiping on the khuff. Or with an increase that is an explanation (tafsir) — this is the second section thereof, and its example is that we say in the mentioned example at the time of opposition: indeed wiping is a pillar in wudu', so its triple repetition is not recommended after its completion. Our saying 'after its completion' is an increase over the measure of opposition, but it is an explanation of the intended meaning. However, it is problematic that this example is not for pure opposition, i.e., by comprehensiveness, similar to the inverse, i.e., in effecting the refutation absolutely. (al-Qamar) 'and for it' meaning for opposition in the ruling of the branch. (al-Qamar) 'and it is valid etc.' the reason for validity is that it involves establishing a ruling contrary to the first ruling by establishing another 'illa in that very place. (al-Sunbuli) 'by the opposite etc.' i.e., it establishes the opposite of the ruling that the mu'alil established in the analogized thing. (al-Qamar) 'without increase' i.e., in the first ruling that the mu'alil stated, and without change therein. (al-Qamar) 'from it' i.e., from opposition in the ruling of the branch by mentioning an 'illa etc., i.e., without attempting to nullify the opponent's 'illa. (al-Qamar) 'without increase and decrease etc.' so there occurs pure opposition without attempting to nullify the opponent's 'illa, so acting upon both is prevented because each one opposes the other, and the way of action is blocked except by preponderance of one 'illa over the other. So when one is preponderant, acting by the preponderant becomes obligatory at that time. (al-Sunbuli) 'or with increase etc.' i.e., that he mentions an 'illa indicating the opposite of the mu'alil's ruling with an increase that is an explanation, and it is also a valid opposition, but it is inferior to the first because the first is valid without increase, whereas this is not valid without it. (al-Sunbuli) 'it is explanation and affirmation of the first ruling.' (al-Qamar) 'indeed wiping is a rukn etc.' for his statement 'its triple repetition is not recommended' is the opposite of the mu'alil's ruling. (al-Qamar) 'for the intended meaning' i.e., the completion after the obligation, and triple repetition is only recommended because it is completion after performing the obligation (farad).
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on Mu'arada (opposition) in qiyas. The author introduces the second type of mu'arada: opposition by something else (mu'arada bi al-ghayr). This is divided into two types: (1) opposition in the ruling of the branch (far'), and (2) opposition in the 'illa (not detailed here). The text focuses on opposition in the ruling of the branch, which has five sections (only two are mentioned here). The first section is opposition without any increase — the objector presents an 'illa that directly produces the opposite ruling without adding any qualification. The example given involves the ruling on wiping the head in wudu': the Shafi'i argues that since wiping is a rukn, triple repetition is recommended (by analogy with washing). The Hanafi opponent counters by stating that wiping is just wiping, and its triple repetition is not recommended (by analogy with wiping on khuff). This is pure opposition. The second section is opposition with an increase that explains the ruling, such as adding 'after its completion' to clarify that the recommended triple repetition is after the obligatory wipe, not during it. The marginal notes clarify that the first type is superior because it stands without extra explanation, while the second requires the increase to be valid. Ultimately, when both sides present conflicting 'illas, the disputation is resolved by preponderance (tarjih) of one 'illa over the other.

Key Terms
معارضة (mu'arada): Opposition in argumentation; presenting a proof contrary to the opponent's ruling
محض المقابلة (mahd al-muqabala): Pure opposition without attempting to nullify the opponent's 'illa
ترجيح (tarjih): Preponderance; the process of weighing conflicting 'illas to determine which is stronger

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between the first and second types of mu'arada in the ruling of the branch?
A) The first uses a different 'illa, while the second uses the same 'illa.
B) The first is without increase, the second includes an increase that explains the ruling.
C) The first is valid, the second is invalid.
D) The first is from the Hanafi school, the second from the Shafi'i school.

Key Takeaway
Mu'arada in the branch ruling requires presenting a counter-'illa; the two types are distinguished by the presence of an explanatory increase, and both are resolved through tarjih.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Third and Fourth Types of Mu'arada: Taghyir in Qiyas
Explaining mu'arada that adds a change (taghyir) with examples from fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the third and fourth types of mu'arada (taghyir) and apply the Hanafi criterion for valid mu'arada with taghyir.

Core Idea
Mu'arada with a change (taghyir) is valid only if it implicitly overturns the opponent's entire ruling.

In Hanafi usul, objections (mu'arada) in qiyas are not all of one kind. This lesson focuses on the third and fourth types, both involving a 'taghyir' (change) to the original ruling. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for constructing sound objections that truly undermine the opponent's argument rather than merely adding irrelevant details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and the opponent's objection
Start by clearly stating the original claim (al-mustadill's hukm) and then the objection (mu'arada). Note whether the objection adds an element not present in the original reasoning.
For example, the Hanafi argues for absolute guardianship over an orphan girl; the Shafi'i objects by negating the brother's guardianship specifically.
2
Determine if the objection includes an addition that is a change (taghyir)
A change occurs when the objection introduces a new specification or qualification that alters the original ruling's scope, whether by negating something the first affirmed or affirming something the first did not negate.
The addition must be more than a mere interpretation (tafsir); it must actually restrict or expand the ruling.
3
Classify the change: third division vs. fourth division
The third division negates what the first affirmed (e.g., negating brother's guardianship when first affirmed absolute guardianship). The fourth division affirms what the first did not negate (e.g., affirming equality between beginning and continuation of ownership when first only spoke of sale/purchase).
Both must 'contain an objection to the first' (tahtaha mu'arada) to be valid.
4
Verify if the change implicitly undermines the original ruling
Even if the objection introduces a new element, check whether it necessarily entails the negation of the original ruling. If it does, the mu'arada is valid despite the change.
In the brother example, negating brother's guardianship implies negating all guardianship since no one distinguishes between brother and other relatives.
5
Apply the analysis to the two provided examples
Work through the orphan girl example (third division) and the Muslim slave example (fourth division) to see how the taghyir operates and why the Hanafi school accepts these objections as valid.
Note the correction of a common error: some scholars mistakenly split 'or change' and 'or in it negation…' into separate divisions, but the correct view treats both under 'or change'.

Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of Mu'arada. Rather for the second division of inversion based on our statement in the issue of fasting Ramadan after its determination, and I have not seen an example of this division of pure mu'arada. Or 'change' as a conjunction to His words 'interpretation' i.e. an addition which is a change, i.e. to the first ruling and He explained it by His words: 'or in it a negation of what the first did not affirm, or an affirmation of what the first did not negate, but under it is a mu'arada.' The change: i.e. of the one who presents evidence, for the first, so it is a circumstance from His words 'change' and a restriction for it, so it includes the third and fourth divisions. This is the truth, and some commentators understood that His words 'or change' is a third division, and His words 'or in it i.e. the owner of the circle a negation of what the first did not affirm or an affirmation of what the first did not negate' with the word 'or' without 'waw', and each of them is a fourth division, and this is a gross error arising from changing the waw to 'or'. Then the example of the third division is our statement regarding an orphan girl: she is a minor who is given authority over her by the guardianship of marriage like one who has a father. Al-Shafi'i said to him: she is a minor incapable of managing her own affairs, so she should not be given authority over her by the guardianship of brothers by analogy to wealth, since there is no guardianship of the brother over the wealth of a minor by consensus. (al-Qamar) For this division: i.e. what the mu'arada provides a ruling with an addition which is an interpretation. (al-Qamar) Or change etc. This is a third division of mu'arada regarding the ruling of the branch, which is to oppose it with the opposite of that ruling but with a type of change. (al-Sunbuli) but connected to both negation and affirmation. (al-Qamar) Third division then the meaning of His words 'or change' is that he opposes with the opposite of that ruling with an addition on the change of the first ruling by negating what the first affirmed, or affirming what the first negated but with a type of change. And its example is the example that the commentator will mention later in his words: our statement regarding the orphan girl etc. So this example can be an example of a mu'arada in which there is an addition that is a change with negation of what the first affirmed, for the first affirmed guardianship absolutely, among which is the brother's guardianship, and the opponent negated the brother's guardianship. And it can be an example of a mu'arada in which there is an addition that is a change, and in it a negation of what the first did not affirm, for the opponent negated the brother's guardianship and the one presenting evidence did not explicitly affirm it. So contemplate. (al-Qamar) Gross error: This is not an error nor a change, for what the author of 'al-Da'ir' said agrees with what Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and the author in his 'Kashf' said, and the word 'or' is mentioned in the author's 'Kashf'. (al-Qamar) She is given authority over her due to the cause of being a minor, so the guardian is the grandfather or brother or others as known in fiqh. (al-Qamar) By consensus etc. And specifying the brother is an addition that necessitates a change of the first ruling which was the subject of dispute; because the dispute is about affirming the basis of guardianship over the orphan girl, not about specifying the guardian. So we affirmed the basis of guardianship, and the opponent in this mu'arada negated the brother's guardianship specifically, and that is not a negation of what is disputed. So this is a mu'arada with an addition that is a change, and it is our statement 'by the guardianship of brothers', and in it there is a negation of what the first did not affirm; because we did not affirm in the reasoning the guardianship of brothers but rather absolute guardianship, so that the opponent negated it, but under it is a mu'arada for the first; because if the guardianship of brothers is negated, all others are negated, since no one asserts a distinction between the brother and others. And the example of the fourth division is our statement: The disbeliever has the right to purchase a Muslim slave because he has the right to sell him, so he has the right to purchase him like the Muslim. The followers of al-Shafi'i opposed him and said: Since the disbeliever has the right to sell him, it is necessary that the beginning of ownership and its continuation be equal for him, like the Muslim. But he does not have the right to permanent possession legally, rather he is forced to remove it from his ownership. So likewise he does not have the right to begin ownership. So in this mu'arada there is an addition that is a change, which is his statement: it is necessary that it be equal, and in it there is an affirmation of what the first did not negate; because we did not negate equality between beginning and continuation in the reasoning so that the opponent could affirm it in the mu'arada; rather we affirmed equality between sale and purchase. But under it is a mu'arada for the first; because if he affirmed equality between beginning and continuation, the distinction between sale and purchase becomes apparent. So this ruling is different from the first ruling; since the specific is not the absolute. So this change necessitates a defect in the mu'arada, but it is necessarily entailing the negation of the first ruling, which is not affirming guardianship over the minor by other than the father and grandfather among the guardians. (al-Sunbali) Since no one asserts a distinction etc. For everyone who negates compulsion by the guardianship of brothers negates compulsion by the guardianship of uncles and the like. (al-Qamar) And the example of the fourth division etc. It is to oppose him in the disputed locus with what is not a negation of what the rationalizer affirmed, nor an affirmation of what he negated, but rather it is a negation of what the rationalizer affirms, or an affirmation of what he did not negate, but under it is a mu'arada for the ruling of the rationalizer, such that the ruling affirmed by it necessarily entails the negation of the ruling that the rationalizer affirmed. From this aspect, the aspect of correctness in it appears. Its example is what the commentator explained. (al-Sunbali) 'Like the Muslim' i.e. just as the Muslim has the right to sell a Muslim slave so also his purchase, so also the disbeliever. (al-Qamar) 'Equal in it' i.e. for the disbeliever the beginning of ownership, i.e. the occurrence of ownership of the Muslim slave by the disbeliever and its continuation for him, i.e. its establishment in ownership. (al-Qamar) 'Like the Muslim' i.e. just as the Muslim has the right to begin ownership of the Muslim slave and its continuation, i.e. its establishment over him. (al-Qamar) 'So likewise he does not have the right' i.e. the disbeliever does not have the right to begin ownership of the Muslim slave in realization of equality. (al-Qamar) 'We affirmed equality etc.' So it was an affirmation of what the first did not negate, so the mu'arada is not connected to the locus of dispute, so it is invalid, but its correctness is directed by saying that under it is a mu'arada etc. (al-Qamar) 'Between the beginning' i.e. beginning of ownership and its continuation. (al-Qamar) 'Between sale and purchase' i.e. sale of the Muslim slave and his purchase. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Qiyas, specifically discussing the types of mu'arada (objection/opposition) in analogical reasoning. The author explains the third and fourth divisions of mu'arada that involve a 'taghyir' (change) to the original ruling.

The third division is when the opponent brings a ruling that is opposite to the original but with a specific change. The example given is about the guardianship (wilaya) of an orphan girl for marriage. The original argument (by the Hanafi) says that the orphan girl is a minor and thus can be given in marriage by a guardian (like the grandfather or brother) similar to when she has a father. The opponent (Shafi'i) objects by saying that the girl is a minor incapable of managing her affairs, so she should not be given in marriage by the brother, analogizing to wealth where the brother has no guardianship by consensus. This objection includes an addition (specifying the brother) that changes the original ruling but still implicitly negates the original claim of absolute guardianship.

The fourth division is when the opponent brings a ruling that is not a direct negation or affirmation of the original but implies a consequence that undermines the original. The example is about a disbeliever purchasing a Muslim slave. The Hanafi argues that since a disbeliever can sell a Muslim slave, he can also purchase one, like a Muslim. The Shafi'i objects by arguing that if the disbeliever can sell, then the beginning and continuation of ownership should be equal (as for a Muslim), but since he cannot have permanent possession (he is forced to sell), he also cannot begin ownership. This objection includes an addition (equality of beginning and continuation) that the original did not negate, but it implies a distinction between sale and purchase, thereby opposing the original analogy.

The author also clarifies a common mistake where some commentators misinterpreted the text, thinking that 'or change' is a third division and 'or in it negation...' is a fourth, whereas the correct understanding is that the third and fourth divisions are both included under the phrase 'or change'. The glosses by al-Qamar and al-Sunbali provide further clarification and defense of the positions of earlier Hanafi scholars like al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-muʿāraḍa): في القياس: إيراد دليل يعارض علة المستدل أو حكمه
التغيير (al-taghyīr): في المعارضة: زيادة في الحكم تغير من سعته إلى تضييق أو تقييد
الزيادة (al-ziyāda): في المعارضة: إضافة وصف أو حكم لم يذكره المستدل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
ما الفرق بين القسم الثالث والقسم الرابع من المعارضة بالتغيير عند الحنفية؟
A) القسم الثالث ينفي ما أثبته الأول، والرابع يثبت ما لم ينفه الأول
B) القسم الثالث يثبت ما لم ينفه الأول، والرابع ينفي ما أثبته الأول
C) القسم الثالث والرابع كلاهما ينفي ما أثبته الأول
D) القسم الثالث خاص بالقياس والرابع خاص بالنص

Key Takeaway
The third and fourth divisions of mu'arada both involve a change (taghyir): the third negates what the first affirmed, the fourth affirms what the first did not negate, and both are valid only if they implicitly undo the original ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Fourth Type of Mu'āraḍah: Increase that Changes Meaning
Explaining the fourth type of mu'āraḍah with the disbeliever slave example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a counter-argument that contains an increase changing the meaning (ziyādah taghyīr) and evaluate its validity under the fourth type of mu'āraḍah by checking whether it implicitly negates the original ruling.

Core Idea
An increase that changes the meaning invalidates the counter-argument unless it necessarily negates the original ruling.

This lesson examines the fourth type of mu'āraḍah, where the opponent adds a new element that alters the original cause. The classic example is the dispute over a disbeliever buying a Muslim slave. You will learn how Hanafi usul distinguishes between a valid and invalid increase based on whether it still implies the negation of the first ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original analogy
The Hanafi uses qiyas: a disbeliever can sell a Muslim slave, so he can buy him, just as a Muslim can. The cause (ʿilla) is ability to own.
This is the baseline the opponent challenges.
2
Spot the increase
The opponent adds an equality claim: initiation and continuation of ownership must be equal for a disbeliever, unlike a Muslim who can both.
This addition shifts the focus from selling/buying equality to initiation/continuation equality.
3
Determine if it changes the meaning
The original cause was absolute ability to own; the opponent introduces a condition (equality) that changes the meaning of the cause.
This is the 'increase that is a change' (ziyādah hiya taghyīr).
4
Check for implicit negation
Even though the increase changes the meaning, does it necessarily negate the original ruling? Yes, because if continuation is impossible (by consensus), then initiation must also be impossible, invalidating the original analogy.
Thus the counter-argument is valid despite the increase.

باب القياس بيان المعارضة فهذه معارضة بزيادةٍ هي تغيير وهي قولنا بولاية الإخوة، وفيه نفي لما لم يثبته الأول؛ لأنا ما أثبتنا في التعليل ولاية الإخوة بل مطلق الولاية حتى ينفي المعارض إياها، ولكن تحته معارضة للأول؛ لأنه إذا انتفت ولاية الإخوة انتفى سائرها؛ إذ لا قائل بالفصل بين الأخ وغيره من ولايات أهل القرابة ونظير القسم الرابع قولنا: إن الكافر يملك شراء العبد المسلم؛ لأنه يملك بيعه فيملك شراءه كالمسلم، فعارضه أصحاب الشافعي رضي الله عنه وقالوا: إن الكافر لمّا ملك بيعه وجب أن يستوي فيه ابتداء الملك وبقاءه كالمسلم، لكنه لا يملك القرار عليه شرعًا، بل يجبر على إخراجه عن ملكه، فكذلك لا يملك ابتداء ملكه، ففي هذه المعارضة زيادة هي تغيير، وهو قوله: وجب أن يستوي، وفيه إثبات لما لم ينفه الأول؛ لأنا ما نفينا الاستواء بين الابتداء والبقاء في التعليل حتى يثبته الخصم في المعارضة وإنما أثبتنا الاستواء بين البيع والشراء، ولكن تحته معارضة للأول؛ لأنه إذا أثبت الاستواء بين الابتداء والبقاء ظهرت المفارقة بين البيع والشراء، فهذا الحكم غير الحكم الأول؛ إذ المعين غير المطلق، فهذا التغيير يقتضي الخلل في المعارضة، لكنها مستلزمة لنفي الحكم الأول، وهو عدم إثبات الولاية على الصغيرة بغير الأب والجد من الأولياء.(السنبلي) إذ لا قائل بالفصل الخ: فإن كل من ينفي الإجبار بولاية الإخوة ينفي الإجبار بولاية العمومة ونحوها. (القمر) ونظير القسم الرابع إلخ: وهو أن يعارضه في المحل المتنازع فيه بما لم يكن نفيًا لما أثبته المعلل، أو إثباتا لما نفاه، بل يكون نفيًا لما يثبته المعلّل، أو إثباتًا لما لم ينفه، لكن يكون تحته معارضة لحكم المعلل بأن يكون حكم الثابت بها مستلزما لانتفاء الحكم الذي أثبته المعلّل، فمن هذا الوجه يظهر وجه الصحة فيها، ومثاله ما بينه الشارح (السنبلي) كالمسلم أي كما أن المسلم يملك بيع العبد المسلم فكذا شراؤه فكذا الكافر. (القمر) يستوي فيه أي في الكافر ابتداء الملك، أي حدوث ملك العبد المسلم للكافر وبقاؤه له، أي تقرره على الملك. (القمر) كالمسلم أي كما أن المسلم يملك ابتداءً ملك العبد المسلم وبقائه، أي تقرّره عليه. Chapter on Qiyas: Exposition of Counter-argument. So this is a counter-argument with an increase that is a change, like our statement concerning the guardianship of brothers. It involves negation of what the first did not establish. Because we did not establish in the legal cause the guardianship of brothers, but rather absolute guardianship, so that the opponent negates it. However, underlying it is a counter-argument to the first; because when the guardianship of brothers is negated, all other guardianships are negated, since no one distinguishes between a brother and other relatives in terms of guardianship. An example of the fourth type is our statement: the disbeliever is capable of buying a Muslim slave because he is capable of selling him, just as a Muslim can. The followers of al-Shafi'i countered saying: when the disbeliever can sell him, it is necessary that the initial acquisition and continued ownership be equal, as in the case of a Muslim; but he does not legally have permanent possession, rather he is forced to remove him from his ownership; so likewise he cannot initiate ownership. In this counter-argument there is an increase that is a change, i.e., his statement: it must be equal. It involves establishing what the first did not negate; because we did not negate equality between initiation and continuation in the legal cause, so that the opponent establishes it in the counter-argument; rather we established equality between selling and buying. However, underlying it is a counter-argument to the first; because when equality between initiation and continuation is established, the difference between selling and buying becomes apparent. So this ruling is different from the first ruling; because the specific is not the absolute, so this change necessitates a defect in the counter-argument, but it entails the negation of the first ruling, which is the non-establishment of guardianship over a minor girl by other than the father and grandfather among the guardians. (Sanbali)... (Qamar)... So the sale is valid but not the purchase; because the sale initiates ownership, so it connects to the point of dispute in this respect. Or [the counter-argument] is in a ruling other than the first, but it involves negation of the first. This is the fifth type. Its example is what Abu Hanifa said concerning a woman whose husband was reported dead: she observed the waiting period, married another, gave birth, then the first husband returned alive: the child belongs to the first husband because he is the owner of a valid marital bed (the marriage is intact). If the opponent counters that the second husband has a defective marital bed, so lineage is established through it, just as if a woman married without witnesses and gave birth, lineage is established despite the defective marriage — this counter-argument was not to negate lineage from the first, but to establish lineage for the second. So the sale is valid but not the purchase; because the disbeliever's continued ownership of a Muslim slave is prohibited by consensus, so he is ordered to remove it from his ownership by sale to a Muslim or manumission, etc. Since initiation and continuation are equal, initiation is also prevented, so his purchase of a Muslim slave is invalid because it initiates ownership. (Qamar)... (al-Muhshi)... (Sanbali)... (Qamar)...

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Qiyas discusses the fourth and fifth types of counter-arguments (mu'āraḍah) in legal analogy. The author explains that a counter-argument may contain an increase that changes the meaning (ziyādah taghyīr), which is invalid if it deviates from the original point of dispute. However, the counter-argument may still be valid if it implicitly negates the original ruling. The fourth type is exemplified by the Hanafi position that a disbeliever can buy a Muslim slave, analogous to selling. The Shafi'i opposition argues that ownership cannot be initiated if it cannot be continued, thus making the buy invalid. The Hanafi response shows that this counter-argument does not directly negate the Hanafi claim but introduces a new element (equality between initiation and continuation), which shifts the point of dispute. Yet, it still implies the negation of the original ruling. The fifth type is illustrated by the case of a woman remarrying after her husband is reported dead. Abu Hanifa rules the child belongs to the first husband due to the valid marriage contract. The opponent argues for the second husband based on a defective marriage. This counter-argument does not contradict the first ruling directly but establishes the opposite ruling, thereby negating the first. The commentary by Sanbali, Qamar, and al-Muhshi elaborates on the conditions for a valid counter-argument and the underlying reasoning.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu'āraḍah): A counter-argument in qiyas that attempts to rebut a legal analogy by offering an alternative reasoning.
زيادة هي تغيير (ziyādah hiya taghyīr): An increase in the counter-argument that changes the meaning of the original cause or ruling, making it invalid unless it implies negation.

Checkpoint
What makes the Shafi'i counter-argument in the disbeliever example valid under the fourth type of mu'āraḍah?
A) It directly contradicts the Hanafi cause.
B) It introduces an increase that changes the meaning but implies negation of the original ruling.
C) It agrees with the Hanafi position.
D) It is based on a clear Quranic text.

Key Takeaway
The fourth type of mu'āraḍah involves an increase that changes the meaning, but it is valid if the increase necessarily implies the negation of the original ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

The Fifth Type of Mu'āraḍah: Different Ruling that Negates the First
Explaining the fifth type of mu'āraḍah with the lineage example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recognize a counter-argument that establishes a different ruling (not directly contradicting the first) yet necessarily negates the first ruling, and classify it as the fifth type of mu'āraḍah.

Core Idea
A counter-argument can be valid if it establishes a new ruling that, by implication, negates the original ruling.

This lesson covers the fifth type of mu'āraḍah, where the opponent does not directly challenge the first ruling but instead proposes a different ruling for a different aspect of the case. The key is that the new ruling necessarily entails the negation of the first. The classic example involves lineage of a child when a woman remarried after her husband's reported death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling
Abu Hanifa rules that the child belongs to the first husband because of a valid marriage bed.
The original ruling is 'lineage from the first husband'.
2
Identify the opponent's counter-argument
The opponent argues that the second husband also has a marriage bed (defective) and, by analogy to marriage without witnesses, lineage should be established for him.
This is a different ruling (lineage from husband 2), not a direct denial of lineage from husband 1.
3
Check if the counter-argument implies negation
Since a child cannot have two lineages, establishing lineage from husband 2 necessarily negates lineage from husband 1.
Thus, even though the counter-argument is for a different ruling, it implies the negation of the original ruling.
4
Classify as fifth type
This is the fifth type: a counter-argument that establishes a different ruling (ḥukm ākhar) but necessarily negates the first ruling.
The validity comes from the logical impossibility of both rulings coexisting.

باب القياس بيان المعارضة فهذه معارضة بزيادةٍ هي تغيير وهي قولنا بولاية الإخوة، وفيه نفي لما لم يثبته الأول؛ لأنا ما أثبتنا في التعليل ولاية الإخوة بل مطلق الولاية حتى ينفي المعارض إياها، ولكن تحته معارضة للأول؛ لأنه إذا انتفت ولاية الإخوة انتفى سائرها؛ إذ لا قائل بالفصل بين الأخ وغيره من ولايات أهل القرابة ونظير القسم الرابع قولنا: إن الكافر يملك شراء العبد المسلم؛ لأنه يملك بيعه فيملك شراءه كالمسلم، فعارضه أصحاب الشافعي رضي الله عنه وقالوا: إن الكافر لمّا ملك بيعه وجب أن يستوي فيه ابتداء الملك وبقاءه كالمسلم، لكنه لا يملك القرار عليه شرعًا، بل يجبر على إخراجه عن ملكه، فكذلك لا يملك ابتداء ملكه، ففي هذه المعارضة زيادة هي تغيير، وهو قوله: وجب أن يستوي، وفيه إثبات لما لم ينفه الأول؛ لأنا ما نفينا الاستواء بين الابتداء والبقاء في التعليل حتى يثبته الخصم في المعارضة وإنما أثبتنا الاستواء بين البيع والشراء، ولكن تحته معارضة للأول؛ لأنه إذا أثبت الاستواء بين الابتداء والبقاء ظهرت المفارقة بين البيع والشراء، فهذا الحكم غير الحكم الأول؛ إذ المعين غير المطلق، فهذا التغيير يقتضي الخلل في المعارضة، لكنها مستلزمة لنفي الحكم الأول، وهو عدم إثبات الولاية على الصغيرة بغير الأب والجد من الأولياء.(السنبلي) إذ لا قائل بالفصل الخ: فإن كل من ينفي الإجبار بولاية الإخوة ينفي الإجبار بولاية العمومة ونحوها. (القمر) ونظير القسم الرابع إلخ: وهو أن يعارضه في المحل المتنازع فيه بما لم يكن نفيًا لما أثبته المعلل، أو إثباتا لما نفاه، بل يكون نفيًا لما يثبته المعلّل، أو إثباتًا لما لم ينفه، لكن يكون تحته معارضة لحكم المعلل بأن يكون حكم الثابت بها مستلزما لانتفاء الحكم الذي أثبته المعلّل، فمن هذا الوجه يظهر وجه الصحة فيها، ومثاله ما بينه الشارح (السنبلي) كالمسلم أي كما أن المسلم يملك بيع العبد المسلم فكذا شراؤه فكذا الكافر. (القمر) يستوي فيه أي في الكافر ابتداء الملك، أي حدوث ملك العبد المسلم للكافر وبقاؤه له، أي تقرره على الملك. (القمر) كالمسلم أي كما أن المسلم يملك ابتداءً ملك العبد المسلم وبقائه، أي تقرّره عليه. (القمر) فكذلك لا يملك: أي الكافر ابتداء ملك العبد المسلم تحقيقا للاستواء. (القمر) بين الابتداء أي ابتداء الملك وبقائه. (القمر) بين البيع والشراء: أي بيع العبد المسلم وشرائه. (القمر)  بيان المعارضة باب القياس فيصح البيع دون الشراء؛ لأنه يوجب الملك ابتداء، فيتصل بموضع النزاع من هذا الوجه. أو في حكم غير الأول لكن فيه نفي الأول، عطف على قوله: بضد ذلك الحكم" أي لم يعارضه بضد الحكم الأول، بل يعارضه في حكم آخر غير الأول، لكن فيه نفي الأول، وهذا هو القسم الخامس منها نظيره ما قال أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه في المرأة التي نُعي إليها زوجها، أي أخبرت بموته، فاعتدت وتزوجت بزوج آخر ، فجاءت بولد، ثم جاء الزوج الأول حيا أن الولد للزوج الأول؛ لأنه صاحب فراش صحيح لقيام النكاح بينهما ، فإن عارضه الخصم بأن الثاني صاحب فراش فاسد، فيستوجب به النسب كما لو تزوّجت امرأة بغير شهود وولدت منه يثبت النسب منه وإن كان الفراش فاسدًا، فهذه المعارضة لم تكن لنفي النسب عن الأول، بل لإثبات النسب للثاني، فيصح البيع: أي بيع العبد المسلم دون الشراء؛ لأن بقاء ملك الكافر في العبد المسلم ممنوع بالاتفاق، فيؤمر بإخراجه عن ملكه بالبيع من مسلم أو الإعتاق أو نحو ذلك، ولما استوى الابتداء والبقاء فيمتنع الابتداء أيضًا، فلا يصح شراؤه العبد المسلم؛ لأنه يوجب ابتداء الملك. (القمر) هذا الوجه لكن الاتصال لما يثبت إلا بعد البناء بإثبات التسوية بين الابتداء والبقاء وليس للسائل البناء رجّحت جهة الفساد. (المحشي) غير الأول: أي غير الحكم الأول الذي أثبته المعلّل، أي لا يخالف الحكم الذي أتى به السائل الحكم الذي أثبت المعلّل صورةً، بل حكمه حكم آخر في محل آخر بعلة أخرى، لكن فيه أي فيما ثبت بهذه المعارضة من الحكم الأول، أي من حيث المعنى، فإنه إذا ثبت أحدهما لم يثبت الآخر. (المحشي فراش صحيح: أقول لابد عن قيد القوي الأمة الحليلة؛ فإنها فراش صحيح ضعيف. (السنبلي) بينهما : أي بين الزوج الأول وتلك المرأة. Chapter on Qiyas: Exposition of Counter-argument. So this is a counter-argument with an increase that is a change, like our statement concerning the guardianship of brothers. It involves negation of what the first did not establish. Because we did not establish in the legal cause the guardianship of brothers, but rather absolute guardianship, so that the opponent negates it. However, underlying it is a counter-argument to the first; because when the guardianship of brothers is negated, all other guardianships are negated, since no one distinguishes between a brother and other relatives in terms of guardianship. An example of the fourth type is our statement: the disbeliever is capable of buying a Muslim slave because he is capable of selling him, just as a Muslim can. The followers of al-Shafi'i countered saying: when the disbeliever can sell him, it is necessary that the initial acquisition and continued ownership be equal, as in the case of a Muslim; but he does not legally have permanent possession, rather he is forced to remove him from his ownership; so likewise he cannot initiate ownership. In this counter-argument there is an increase that is a change, i.e., his statement: it must be equal. It involves establishing what the first did not negate; because we did not negate equality between initiation and continuation in the legal cause, so that the opponent establishes it in the counter-argument; rather we established equality between selling and buying. However, underlying it is a counter-argument to the first; because when equality between initiation and continuation is established, the difference between selling and buying becomes apparent. So this ruling is different from the first ruling; because the specific is not the absolute, so this change necessitates a defect in the counter-argument, but it entails the negation of the first ruling, which is the non-establishment of guardianship over a minor girl by other than the father and grandfather among the guardians. (Sanbali)... (Qamar)... So the sale is valid but not the purchase; because the sale initiates ownership, so it connects to the point of dispute in this respect. Or [the counter-argument] is in a ruling other than the first, but it involves negation of the first. This is the fifth type. Its example is what Abu Hanifa said concerning a woman whose husband was reported dead: she observed the waiting period, married another, gave birth, then the first husband returned alive: the child belongs to the first husband because he is the owner of a valid marital bed (the marriage is intact). If the opponent counters that the second husband has a defective marital bed, so lineage is established through it, just as if a woman married without witnesses and gave birth, lineage is established despite the defective marriage — this counter-argument was not to negate lineage from the first, but to establish lineage for the second. So the sale is valid but not the purchase; because the disbeliever's continued ownership of a Muslim slave is prohibited by consensus, so he is ordered to remove it from his ownership by sale to a Muslim or manumission, etc. Since initiation and continuation are equal, initiation is also prevented, so his purchase of a Muslim slave is invalid because it initiates ownership. (Qamar)... (al-Muhshi)... (Sanbali)... (Qamar)...
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Qiyas discusses the fourth and fifth types of counter-arguments (mu'āraḍah) in legal analogy. The author explains that a counter-argument may contain an increase that changes the meaning (ziyādah taghyīr), which is invalid if it deviates from the original point of dispute. However, the counter-argument may still be valid if it implicitly negates the original ruling. The fourth type is exemplified by the Hanafi position that a disbeliever can buy a Muslim slave, analogous to selling. The Shafi'i opposition argues that ownership cannot be initiated if it cannot be continued, thus making the buy invalid. The Hanafi response shows that this counter-argument does not directly negate the Hanafi claim but introduces a new element (equality between initiation and continuation), which shifts the point of dispute. Yet, it still implies the negation of the original ruling. The fifth type is illustrated by the case of a woman remarrying after her husband is reported dead. Abu Hanifa rules the child belongs to the first husband due to the valid marriage contract. The opponent argues for the second husband based on a defective marriage. This counter-argument does not contradict the first ruling directly but establishes the opposite ruling, thereby negating the first. The commentary by Sanbali, Qamar, and al-Muhshi elaborates on the conditions for a valid counter-argument and the underlying reasoning.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu'āraḍah): A counter-argument in qiyas that attempts to rebut a legal analogy by offering an alternative reasoning.
حكم غير الأول (ḥukm ghayr al-awwal): A ruling that is different from the one being challenged, but which logically negates the first ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the opponent's argument for the second husband's lineage considered a valid mu'āraḍah under the fifth type?
A) It directly denies that the first husband is the father.
B) It proves that the second husband's marriage is more valid.
C) It establishes a different ruling (lineage from second) that necessarily negates the first ruling.
D) It is based on a consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
The fifth type of mu'āraḍah allows a counter-argument that proposes a different ruling, as long as that ruling logically implies negation of the original ruling.
