Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Fifth Type of Mu'arada: Indirect Negation and Tarjih
Explains the fifth type of mu'arada with example from Abu Hanifa on child attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fifth type of mu'arada and apply the Hanafi tarjih rule between valid and defective marital beds to determine lineage.

Core Idea
The fifth type of mu'arada indirectly negates the original ruling by establishing a contradictory ruling elsewhere.

In this lesson, we examine the fifth type of mu'arada (opposition) in qiyas. Unlike direct contradiction, this type involves establishing another ruling that necessarily implies the negation of the original. The classical example from Imam Abu Hanifa about a woman whose first husband returns after she remarries illustrates how a valid marital bed (frash sahih) outweighs a defective one (frash fasid), even when the second husband is present. The Hanafi position is that ownership and validity (haqiqah) are stronger than mere semblance (shubha).

Guided Path
1
Identify the original qiyas and the opponent's counter
The original qiyas: the first husband's valid marriage establishes lineage. The opponent counters: the second husband, through a defective marriage, also establishes lineage by analogy to a marriage without witnesses.
The opponent does not deny the first husband's claim but presents a competing claim.
2
Distinguish the fifth type of mu'arada
This is not a direct contradiction of the hukm ('the child is not from the first'). Instead, it establishes a different hukm ('the child is from the second') which, if accepted, would negate the original hukm.
Key: the opponent's argument implies the negation of the original without explicitly stating it.
3
Apply tarjih (weighing) between the two claims
Both claims have a basis: the valid bed (first husband) and the defective bed (second husband). Tarjih is needed to decide which one takes precedence.
The opponent prioritizes presence and semen; the Hanafi prioritizes ownership and validity.
4
Recognize the Hanafi principle: haqiqah over shubha
The valid bed establishes reality (haqiqah) through a sound marriage; the defective bed only creates a semblance (shubha). In Hanafi law, reality is always preferred over semblance.
This principle is applied in many areas of fiqh, not just lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان المعارضة
باب القياس
فيصح البيع دون الشراء؛ لأنه يوجب الملك ابتداء، فيتصل بموضع النزاع من هذا الوجه. أو في حكم غير الأول لكن فيه نفي الأول، عطف على قوله: بضد ذلك الحكم" أي لم يعارضه بضد الحكم الأول، بل يعارضه في حكم آخر غير الأول، لكن فيه نفي الأول، وهذا هو القسم الخامس منها نظيره ما قال أبو حنيفة الله في المرأة التي نُعي إليها زوجها، أي أخبرت بموته، فاعتدت وتزوجت بزوج آخر ، فجاءت بولد، ثم جاء الزوج الأول حيا أن الولد للزوج الأول؛ لأنه صاحب فراش صحيح لقيام النكاح بينهما ، فإن عارضه الخصم بأن الثاني صاحب الزوج الأول أي الزوج الثاني فراش فاسد، فيستوجب به النسب كما لو تزوّجت امرأة بغير شهود وولدت منه يثبت النسب منه وإن كان الفراش فاسدًا، فهذه المعارضة لم تكن لنفي النسب عن الأول، بل لإثبات النسب من الثاني لكن فيه نفي الأول؛ لأنه إذا ثبت من الثاني ينتفي عن الأول لعدم تصور النسب من شخصين، فيحتاج حينئذ إلى الترجيح، فنقول: الأول صاحب فراش صحيح، والثاني صاحب فراش فاسد، والصحيح أولى من الفاسد فيعارضه الخصم بأن الثاني حاضر والماء ماءه، وهو أولى من الغائب، فيظهر حينئذٍ فقه المسألة، وهو أن الملك والصحة أحق بالاعتبار من الحضرة والماء، فإن الفاسد يوجب الشبهة، والصحيح يوجب الحقيقة، والحقيقة أولى من الشبهة.
والثاني في علة الأصل أي النوع الثاني من المعارضة الخالصة المعارضة في علة المقيس عليه بأن يقول: عندي دليل يدلّ على أن العلة في المقيس عليه شيء آخر لم يوجد في الفرع، ثلاثة أقسام كلها باطلة على ما قال. وذلك باطل سواء كانت بمعنى لا يتعدّى هذا هو القسم الأول كما إذا عللنا في بيع الحديد بأنه موزون قوبل بجنسه فلا يجوز بيعه متفاضلاً كالذهب والفضة، فيعارضه السائل بأن العلة عندنا في الأصل هي الثمنية، وتلك لا تتعدى إلى الحديد.
أو يتعدّى إلى فرع مجمع عليه، وهو القسم الثاني كما إذا علّلنا في حرمة بيع الجص
Statement of Opposition
Chapter of Qiyas
So the sale (of a Muslim slave) is valid without purchase; because it initiates ownership, so it connects to the point of dispute from this aspect. Or it is in a ruling other than the first, but it contains negation of the first, a conjunction to his statement: 'contrary to that ruling' – i.e., he did not oppose it with the opposite of the first ruling, but rather he opposes it in another ruling not the first, but it contains negation of the first. This is the fifth type. An example of it is what Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said regarding the woman whose husband was reported dead – i.e., she was informed of his death, so she observed ‘iddah and married another husband, then gave birth to a child, then the first husband came back alive: that the child belongs to the first husband, because he is the owner of a valid bed due to the existence of marriage between them. Then if the opponent opposes him that the second (i.e., the second husband) is the owner of a defective bed, so lineage is established by it, just as if a woman married without witnesses and gave birth from him, lineage is established from him even though the bed was defective. This opposition was not to negate lineage from the first, but to establish lineage from the second, yet it contains negation of the first; because when it is established from the second, it is negated from the first due to the impossibility (of lineage from two persons), so then a weighing (tarjih) is needed. So we say: the first is the owner of a valid bed, and the second is the owner of a defective bed, and the valid is preferable to the defective. Then the opponent opposes him that the second is present and the semen is his, so he is preferable to the absent one. Then the fiqh of the issue becomes apparent: that ownership and validity are more deserving of consideration than presence and semen, for the defective causes shubha (semblance), while the valid causes haqiqah (reality), and reality is preferable to semblance.
The second type in the ‘illa of the original: i.e., the second type of pure opposition – opposition in the ‘illa of the maqis ‘alayh by saying: I have a proof that the ‘illa in the maqis ‘alayh is something else not found in the branch. It has three types, all invalid as he said. That is invalid, whether it is in the sense of non-transitive: this is the first type, as when we give the ‘illa in the sale of iron that it is weight-based, sold in kind, so it is not permissible to sell it in disparity like gold and silver, then the opponent opposes that the ‘illa in the original in our view is thamaniyyah (monetary value), and that does not extend to iron. Or it extends to a branch agreed upon – this is the second type, as when we give the ‘illa in the prohibition of selling gypsum...
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Qiyas (analogical deduction) in Usul al-Fiqh explains the concept of mu’arada (opposition) – a technique used in debate where an opponent challenges the qiyas by presenting a counter-dalil. The text first discusses the fifth type of mu’arada, which is not a direct denial of the original ruling but an assertion of another ruling that indirectly negates the first. The example from Abu Hanifa is given: a woman whose husband was reported dead, she remarries and has a child, then the first husband returns. The child is attributed to the first husband because of the valid marriage (frash sahih). The opponent argues that the child should go to the second husband (present, with his semen) through a defective bed (frash fasid). This opposition is not directly denying the paternity of the first, but establishing the paternity of the second, which necessarily negates the first (since one child cannot have two fathers). Then a tarjih (preference) is needed: the first husband’s valid marriage (ownership and soundness) outweighs the second’s presence and semen. The Hanafi position is that validity (haqiqah) is stronger than mere semblance (shubha).

The second part covers opposition in the ‘illa of the maqis ‘alayh (the original case in qiyas). The opponent claims that the ‘illa in the original is something else not found in the branch. This type has three divisions, all considered invalid. The first is when the opponent’s ‘illa does not extend to the branch at all (e.g., in the sale of iron, the opponent says the ‘illa is monetary value, not weight). The second is when the ‘illa extends to another branch agreed upon (e.g., gypsum), which would make the analogy inconsistent. The third (implied but not fully detailed here) is also invalid. The Hanafi view is that proper mu’arada must be in the same ruling or directly negate it; opposing by claiming a different ‘illa that does not apply to the branch fails because it does not actually oppose the original qiyas.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu'aradah): A method of objection in qiyas where the opponent presents a counter-dalil that either directly negates the ruling or introduces another ruling that implies its negation.
فراش صحيح (frash sahih): A valid marital bed that establishes lineage without doubt, based on a valid marriage contract.
فراش فاسد (frash fasid): A defective marital bed (e.g., marriage without witnesses) that can still establish lineage as a semblance (shubha), but is weaker than a valid bed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of the woman with two husbands, what is the type of mu'arada used by the opponent?
A) Direct opposition of the 'illa
B) Opposition in the hukm by stating the opposite
C) Fifth type: establishing another ruling that implies negation of the first
D) Invalid opposition because the second marriage was not valid

Key Takeaway
The fifth type of mu'arada indirectly negates the original ruling by establishing a contradictory ruling elsewhere; Hanafi tarjih favors haqiqah over shubha.

Opposition in the 'Illa of the Maqis 'Alayh: Three Invalid Types
Explains the three invalid types of opposition in the 'illa of the maqis 'alayh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of opposition in the 'illa of the maqis 'alayh and explain why each is considered invalid in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Opposing by claiming a different 'illa for the original that does not apply to the branch is invalid.

This lesson covers the second type of pure opposition: opposing the 'illa of the maqis 'alayh (the original case in qiyas). The opponent claims that the effective cause in the original is something else, not the one used by the proponent. The Hanafi usul identifies three such scenarios, all invalid. We examine each: (1) the claimed 'illa does not extend to the branch (non-transitive), (2) it extends to a branch that is agreed upon, and (3) the third type (implied). Understanding why these are invalid helps sharpen the skill of correct qiyas construction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original qiyas and the opponent's objection
The proponent presents a qiyas with a specific 'illa in the original. The opponent objects that the 'illa is actually something else.
For example: in sale of iron, proponent says 'illa is weight; opponent says 'illa is monetary value (thamaniyyah).
2
Classify the type of opposition
Three types: (1) opponent's 'illa does not extend to the branch at all (non-transitive), (2) it extends to a branch that is agreed upon (e.g., gold and silver), (3) a third type implied but not detailed.
The passage explicitly says all three are invalid.
3
Understand why each type is invalid
Type 1: If the opponent's 'illa does not apply to the branch, it is irrelevant to the qiyas. Type 2: If it extends to a branch that is already agreed upon by both sides, it does not truly oppose; it just repeats a known ruling.
The third type is also invalid, likely because it also fails to properly challenge the proponent's qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان المعارضة
باب القياس
فيصح البيع دون الشراء؛ لأنه يوجب الملك ابتداء، فيتصل بموضع النزاع من هذا الوجه. أو في حكم غير الأول لكن فيه نفي الأول، عطف على قوله: بضد ذلك الحكم" أي لم يعارضه بضد الحكم الأول، بل يعارضه في حكم آخر غير الأول، لكن فيه نفي الأول، وهذا هو القسم الخامس منها نظيره ما قال أبو حنيفة الله في المرأة التي نُعي إليها زوجها، أي أخبرت بموته، فاعتدت وتزوجت بزوج آخر ، فجاءت بولد، ثم جاء الزوج الأول حيا أن الولد للزوج الأول؛ لأنه صاحب فراش صحيح لقيام النكاح بينهما ، فإن عارضه الخصم بأن الثاني صاحب الزوج الأول أي الزوج الثاني فراش فاسد، فيستوجب به النسب كما لو تزوّجت امرأة بغير شهود وولدت منه يثبت النسب منه وإن كان الفراش فاسدًا، فهذه المعارضة لم تكن لنفي النسب عن الأول، بل لإثبات النسب من الثاني لكن فيه نفي الأول؛ لأنه إذا ثبت من الثاني ينتفي عن الأول لعدم تصور النسب من شخصين، فيحتاج حينئذ إلى الترجيح، فنقول: الأول صاحب فراش صحيح، والثاني صاحب فراش فاسد، والصحيح أولى من الفاسد فيعارضه الخصم بأن الثاني حاضر والماء ماءه، وهو أولى من الغائب، فيظهر حينئذٍ فقه المسألة، وهو أن الملك والصحة أحق بالاعتبار من الحضرة والماء، فإن الفاسد يوجب الشبهة، والصحيح يوجب الحقيقة، والحقيقة أولى من الشبهة.
والثاني في علة الأصل أي النوع الثاني من المعارضة الخالصة المعارضة في علة المقيس عليه بأن يقول: عندي دليل يدلّ على أن العلة في المقيس عليه شيء آخر لم يوجد في الفرع، ثلاثة أقسام كلها باطلة على ما قال. وذلك باطل سواء كانت بمعنى لا يتعدّى هذا هو القسم الأول كما إذا عللنا في بيع الحديد بأنه موزون قوبل بجنسه فلا يجوز بيعه متفاضلاً كالذهب والفضة، فيعارضه السائل بأن العلة عندنا في الأصل هي الثمنية، وتلك لا تتعدى إلى الحديد.
أو يتعدّى إلى فرع مجمع عليه، وهو القسم الثاني كما إذا علّلنا في حرمة بيع الجص
Statement of Opposition
Chapter of Qiyas
So the sale (of a Muslim slave) is valid without purchase; because it initiates ownership, so it connects to the point of dispute from this aspect. Or it is in a ruling other than the first, but it contains negation of the first, a conjunction to his statement: 'contrary to that ruling' – i.e., he did not oppose it with the opposite of the first ruling, but rather he opposes it in another ruling not the first, but it contains negation of the first. This is the fifth type. An example of it is what Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said regarding the woman whose husband was reported dead – i.e., she was informed of his death, so she observed ‘iddah and married another husband, then gave birth to a child, then the first husband came back alive: that the child belongs to the first husband, because he is the owner of a valid bed due to the existence of marriage between them. Then if the opponent opposes him that the second (i.e., the second husband) is the owner of a defective bed, so lineage is established by it, just as if a woman married without witnesses and gave birth from him, lineage is established from him even though the bed was defective. This opposition was not to negate lineage from the first, but to establish lineage from the second, yet it contains negation of the first; because when it is established from the second, it is negated from the first due to the impossibility (of lineage from two persons), so then a weighing (tarjih) is needed. So we say: the first is the owner of a valid bed, and the second is the owner of a defective bed, and the valid is preferable to the defective. Then the opponent opposes him that the second is present and the semen is his, so he is preferable to the absent one. Then the fiqh of the issue becomes apparent: that ownership and validity are more deserving of consideration than presence and semen, for the defective causes shubha (semblance), while the valid causes haqiqah (reality), and reality is preferable to semblance.
The second type in the ‘illa of the original: i.e., the second type of pure opposition – opposition in the ‘illa of the maqis ‘alayh by saying: I have a proof that the ‘illa in the maqis ‘alayh is something else not found in the branch. It has three types, all invalid as he said. That is invalid, whether it is in the sense of non-transitive: this is the first type, as when we give the ‘illa in the sale of iron that it is weight-based, sold in kind, so it is not permissible to sell it in disparity like gold and silver, then the opponent opposes that the ‘illa in the original in our view is thamaniyyah (monetary value), and that does not extend to iron. Or it extends to a branch agreed upon – this is the second type, as when we give the ‘illa in the prohibition of selling gypsum...
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Qiyas (analogical deduction) in Usul al-Fiqh explains the concept of mu’arada (opposition) – a technique used in debate where an opponent challenges the qiyas by presenting a counter-dalil. The text first discusses the fifth type of mu’arada, which is not a direct denial of the original ruling but an assertion of another ruling that indirectly negates the first. The example from Abu Hanifa is given: a woman whose husband was reported dead, she remarries and has a child, then the first husband returns. The child is attributed to the first husband because of the valid marriage (frash sahih). The opponent argues that the child should go to the second husband (present, with his semen) through a defective bed (frash fasid). This opposition is not directly denying the paternity of the first, but establishing the paternity of the second, which necessarily negates the first (since one child cannot have two fathers). Then a tarjih (preference) is needed: the first husband’s valid marriage (ownership and soundness) outweighs the second’s presence and semen. The Hanafi position is that validity (haqiqah) is stronger than mere semblance (shubha).

The second part covers opposition in the ‘illa of the maqis ‘alayh (the original case in qiyas). The opponent claims that the ‘illa in the original is something else not found in the branch. This type has three divisions, all considered invalid. The first is when the opponent’s ‘illa does not extend to the branch at all (e.g., in the sale of iron, the opponent says the ‘illa is monetary value, not weight). The second is when the ‘illa extends to another branch agreed upon (e.g., gypsum), which would make the analogy inconsistent. The third (implied but not fully detailed here) is also invalid. The Hanafi view is that proper mu’arada must be in the same ruling or directly negate it; opposing by claiming a different ‘illa that does not apply to the branch fails because it does not actually oppose the original qiyas.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu'aradah): A method of objection in qiyas where the opponent presents a counter-dalil that either directly negates the ruling or introduces another ruling that implies its negation.
علة المقيس عليه (illat al-maqis 'alayh): The effective cause in the original case (asl) that is used to extend the ruling to the branch (far').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the first type of opposition in the 'illa (non-transitive) considered invalid?
A) Because the opponent's 'illa does not apply to the branch
B) Because the opponent's 'illa is not from the Quran
C) Because it contradicts the proponent's 'illa directly
D) Because it extends to an agreed branch

Key Takeaway
Opposition in the 'illa of the maqis 'alayh is only valid if the opponent's 'illa applies to the branch; non-transitive and agreed-upon extensions are invalid.

Three Invalid Types of Counterargument in the Illah
Explaining the three invalid types of counterargument in the illah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the three invalid types of counterargument against the illah of the original, and explain why each fails to disprove the analogy.

Core Idea
A counterargument proposing a different illah does not invalidate the analogy: a ruling can be established by multiple effective causes.

In this passage, the author explains a specific form of counterargument (muʿāraḍah) in qiyās: the objector claims that the effective cause (ʿillah) in the original case is something other than what the proponent asserts, and that this alternative cause is absent in the branch. The passage categorizes this into three types based on whether the objector's claimed ʿillah extends to other cases. Understanding why all three are invalid is crucial for defending an analogy and recognizing legitimate objections in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of counterargument
Recognize that muʿāraḍah fī ʿillat al-aṣl occurs when the objector proposes a different ʿillah for the original case and claims it is absent in the branch.
2
Distinguish the three subdivisions
Based on taʿdiyah (extensibility): (a) non-extending, (b) extending to an agreed branch, (c) extending to a disputed branch.
3
Examine the examples
For each type, trace the example from the text: iron (thamaniyyah), plaster (iqtitāt/iddikhār), plaster again (ṭuʿm) with fruits.
4
Understand the ground of invalidity
The objector's claim does not negate the proponent's ʿillah; a single ruling can be proven by multiple different ʿillahs. The absence of the objector's ʿillah does not imply absence of the ruling.
5
Recognize the purpose of ʿillah
Taʿdiyah: the ʿillah must extend to all relevant cases. Non-extending ʿillah fails this purpose, so it is invalid a fortiori.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني في علة الأصل أي النوع الثاني من المعارضة الخالصة المعارضة في علة المقيس عليه بأن يقول: عندي دليل يدلّ على أن العلة في المقيس عليه شيء آخر لم يوجد في الفرع، ثلاثة أقسام كلها باطلة على ما قال. وذلك باطل سواء كانت بمعنى لا يتعدّى هذا هو القسم الأول كما إذا عللنا في بيع الحديد بأنه موزون قوبل بجنسه فلا يجوز بيعه متفاضلاً كالذهب والفضة، فيعارضه السائل بأن العلة عندنا في الأصل هي الثمنية، وتلك لا تتعدى إلى الحديد. أو يتعدّى إلى فرع مجمع عليه، وهو القسم الثاني كما إذا علّلنا في حرمة بيع الجص بجنسه متفاضلاً بالكيل والجنس كالحنطة والشعير فيعارضه السائل بأن العلة في الأصل ليست ما قلت بل هي الاقتيات والادّخار، وهو معدوم في الجص وإن كان يتعدّى إلى فرع مجمع عليه، وهو الأرز والدخن. أو مختلف فيه، أي يتعدّى إلى فرع مختلف فيه، وهو القسم الثالث، مثاله ما لو عارض السائل في المسألة المذكورة بأن العلة في الأصل هو الطعم، ولم يوجد في الجص، وهو يتعدّى إلى فرع مختلف فيه أعني الفواكه وما دون الكيل، وهذه الأقسام كلها باطلة؛ لأن الوصف الذي يدعيه السائل لا ينافي الوصف الذي يدعيه المعلّل؛ إذ الحكم يثبت بعلل شتّى، فإن لم يكن وصفه متعدّيًا ففساده ظاهر؛ لأن المقصود بالتعليل التعدية، وإن كان متعدّيًا كانت المعارضة أيضًا فاسدة؛ لأنها لا تعلّق لها بالمتنازع فيه إلا أنها تفيد عدم تلك العلة فيه، وهو لا يوجب عدم الحكم.
And the second [type of counterargument] is in the illah of the original: that is, the second type of pure counterargument is the counterargument concerning the illah of the maqīs ʿalayh, by saying: 'I have evidence that the illah in the original is something else not found in the branch.' It has three divisions, all of which are invalid as he said. That is invalid whether it is in the sense that it does not extend [to the branch] — this is the first division, as when we give the cause in selling iron that it is weighed and sold by weight against its genus, so it is not permissible to sell it with disparity like gold and silver, and the objector counters by saying: 'The illah according to us in the original is thamaniyyah (being a currency), and that does not extend to iron.' Or it extends to a branch that is agreed upon — this is the second division, as when we give the cause in the prohibition of selling plaster by weight against its genus with the condition of capacity and genus like wheat and barley, and the objector counters by saying: 'The illah in the original is not what you said, but rather iqtitāt (being a staple food) and iddikhār (storability), and that is absent in plaster, although it extends to a branch that is agreed upon, namely rice and millet.' Or it extends to a branch that is disputed — this is the third division, an example is where the objector counters in the mentioned issue by saying: 'The illah in the original is the taste (ṭuʿm), and it is not present in plaster, and it extends to a branch that is disputed, namely fruits and what is less than the standard measure.' All these divisions are invalid because the description that the objector claims does not negate the description that the proponent of the illah claims; since the ruling is established by multiple different illahs. If his description is not extending, its invalidity is obvious because the purpose of giving an illah is extension. And if it is extending, the counterargument is also invalid because it has no connection to the matter in dispute except that it indicates the absence of that illah in the branch, and that does not necessitate the absence of the ruling.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage explains the second type of counterargument (muʿāraḍah) in the context of qiyās: the objector attacks the original case (maqīs ʿalayh) of the analogy by claiming that the effective cause (ʿillah) is something other than what the proponent of the analogy claims, and that this other ʿillah is not present in the branch (farʿ). The author divides this into three types, all of which are invalid. The first type is where the objector's claimed ʿillah does not extend to any other branch (i.e., it is specific to the original). For example, in the sale of iron, the proponent says the ʿillah is being weighed (wazn), so selling iron for iron with disparity is prohibited like gold and silver. The objector says the ʿillah is actually thamaniyyah (being a medium of exchange/currency), which does not apply to iron. The second type is where the objector's ʿillah extends to a branch that is agreed upon (by both parties) to have the same ruling. For example, in the prohibition of selling plaster (jass) with disparity, the proponent says the ʿillah is being measured by capacity (kayl) and genus (jins). The objector says the ʿillah is iqtitāt (being a staple food) and iddikhār (storability), which is absent in plaster but present in rice and millet (which are agreed to be ribawī). The third type is where the objector's ʿillah extends to a branch that is disputed (different between madhabs). For example, the same issue of plaster, the objector says the ʿillah is taste (ṭuʿm), which is absent in plaster but present in fruits and small quantities (less than the standard measure) – a dispute between Hanafis and Shāfiʿīs over whether these items are ribawī. All three are invalid because the description claimed by the objector does not negate the description claimed by the proponent; both could be valid causes, and the ruling can be established by multiple causes. If the objector's description is not extending (first type), then it is obviously invalid because the point of giving an ʿillah is to extend the ruling to all branches that share it. If it is extending (second and third types), the counterargument still fails because the absence of that particular ʿillah in the branch does not prove the absence of the ruling; the ruling could be established by another ʿillah (the proponent's). Thus, these counterarguments do not succeed in breaking the analogy.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-muʿāraḍah): A counterargument in qiyās that attacks the analogy by claiming a different ʿillah or another flaw.
العلة (al-ʿillah): The effective cause or ratio legis that justifies the extension of a ruling from the original to the branch.
التعدية (al-taʿdiyah): The property of the ʿillah that allows it to extend to other cases sharing that cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the second type of counterargument (proposing a different ʿillah that extends to an agreed branch) considered invalid?
A) Because the objector's ʿillah does not extend to any branch.
B) Because the objector's ʿillah must be the same as the proponent's.
C) Because the absence of the objector's ʿillah in the branch does not negate the proponent's ʿillah; multiple ʿillahs can coexist.
D) Because the branch is not part of the analogy.

Key Takeaway
A muʿāraḍah that proposes a different ʿillah for the original, whether extending or not, does not invalidate the analogy because multiple ʿillahs can underlie the same ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Mu'arada in Qiyas and the Rule of Valid Speech
Explains the types of mu'arada and the rule for valid objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mu'arada from mumana'a and apply the rule that every speech is valid in its origin to convert invalid objections into valid ones.

Core Idea
A mu'arada is invalid unless framed as mumana'a because rulings can have multiple causes.

In qiyas, an objector may try to invalidate an analogy by proposing a different effective cause. But simply showing a different cause does not refute the arguer's qiyas, because the ruling may have many causes. The Hanafi school teaches that such objections must be presented as a prevention (mumana'a) to be valid. This lesson unpacks the types of mu'arada and introduces a key rule: every speech is valid in its origin, so an objection can be reformulated to become sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of mu'arada
The passage lists three scenarios: the branch may be agreed upon, disputed, or the cause may be transitive but the branch disputed. All are invalid because the objector's cause does not negate the arguer's cause.
2
Understand the principle of multiple causes
The ruling can be established by various causes (علل شتّى). The absence of the objector's cause does not imply the arguer's cause is absent; the ruling may still be proven by another cause.
This is the core Hanafi argument against mu'arada.
3
Distinguish mufaraqa from mumana'a
Mufaraqa (mere distinction) is invalid because it only shows a difference without preventing the cause. Mumana'a (prevention) blocks the application of the arguer's cause and is valid.
Hanafis require objections to be framed as mumana'a.
4
Apply the rule of valid speech
The rule 'every speech is valid in its origin and use' means that even if an objection is initially flawed (mufaraqa), it can be reformulated as mumana'a to become acceptable.
The example of manumission of a mortgaged slave illustrates this.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
In the manumission example, Shafi'i argues it is invalid because it is like a sale. Hanafis respond by showing the distinction (manumission cannot be rescinded) as a mumana'a, thus preserving the validity of manumission.
This demonstrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
بيان المعارضة
بجنسه متفاضلاً بالكيل والجنس كالحنطة والشعير فيعارضه السائل بأن العلة في الأصل أي المالكي الحنطة والشعير ليست ما قلت بل هي الاقتيات والادّخار، وهو معدوم في الجص وإن كان يتعدّى إلى فرع مجمع عليه، وهو الأرز والدخن أي القدر والجنس أي الفرع أو مختلف فيه، أي يتعدّى إلى فرع مختلف فيه، وهو القسم الثالث، مثاله ما لو عارض السائل في المسألة المذكورة بأن العلة في الأصل هو الطعم، ولم يوجد في الجص، وهو أي الشافعي له لا الكيل مع الجنس أي الطعم يتعدّى إلى فرع مختلف فيه أعني الفواكه وما دون الكيل، وهذه الأقسام كلها باطلة؛ لأن الوصف الذي يدعيه السائل لا ينافي الوصف الذي يدعيه المعلّل؛ إذ الحكم يثبت بعلل شتّى، فإن لم يكن وصفه متعدّيًا ففساده ظاهر؛ لأن المقصود بالتعليل التعدية، وإن كان السائل المعارضة أي وصف السائل متعدّيًا كانت المعارضة أيضًا فاسدة؛ لأنها لا تعلّق لها بالمتنازع فيه إلا أنها تفيد عدم تلك العلة فيه، وهو لا يوجب عدم الحكم.
الفرع أي تلك المعارضة مجمع مجمع عليه أي أجمع عليه المعلّل والمعارض السائل. (القمر) أو مختلف فيه : معطوف على قول المصنف بالله : عليه (القمر) مختلف فيه : أي بين المعلّل والمعارض السائل. (القمر) أعني الفواكه إلخ فإن الفواكه وما دون الكيل الشرعي أي نصف صاع كالحفنة والحفنتين ليس فيهما الربا عندنا؛ لأنها ليست بمكيلة ولا موزونة، وعند الشافعي الله فيهما الربا. (القمر) الوصف الذي إلخ سواء كان متعديًا أو غير متعدّ.(القمر)
لا ينافي إلخ فإن معارضة العلل لا تتحقق فالعلة التي أبدعها السائل المعارض وإن لم توجد في الفرع لكن وجود العلة التي أبدعها المعلّل في الفرع كافٍ لإثبات الحكم، فيصح قياسه، وقال صاحب "التلويح": إن مقصود المعارض إبطال وصف المعلل، فإذا بين علية وصف آخر احتمل أن يكون كل من الوصفين مستقلاً بالعلية وأن يكون كل منها جزء علة فلا يصح الجزم باستقلال علة المعلّل أو المعارض، فيحصل عارضه فيحصل معارضة، فتأمل.(القمر) شتّى جمع شتيت كمريض ومرضى، وما في مسير" الدائر : جمع شتية، أي في مختلفة فمما لم يثبت. (القمر) التعدية فإذا خلا التعليل عن التعدية بطل لخلوه عن الفائدة والمقصود، وإذا بطل التعليل بطلت المعارضة، كذا قيل. (القمر) تلك العلة أي العلة التي أبدأها المعارض (القمر)
وهو: أي عدم تلك العلة في الفرع لا يوجب عدم الحكم لجواز أن يثبت الحكم في الفرع بعلة أخرى. (القمر)
عدم الحكم إلخ : إذ الحكم يثبت بعلل شتّى، فبعد فساد تلك العلة تبقى علة أخرى، وهي تكفي.(السنبلي)

صحة كل الكلام في أصل وضعه
صحة كل الكلام في أصل وضعه]
وكل كلام صحيح في الأصل، أي في أصل وضعه وجوهره ولكن يذكر سبيل المفارقة التي هي باطلة عند أهل الأصول، فأذكره على سبيل الممانعة ليخرج عن حيّز الفساد إلى حيّز أي ذلك الكلام الصحة، ويكون مقبولاً بأصله ووصفه معًا، وإنما تذكر هذه القاعدة ههنا؛ لأن المعارضة في
علة الأصل هي المسماة بالمفارقة عندهم؛ لأنه أتى السائل بعلة يقع بها الفرق بين الأصل كالشافعي مثلاً هي الثمنية كالذهب والفضة والفرع، وهو فاسد عند الأكثر، فإذا أتى السائل بكلام لطيف مقبول في ضمن هذه المفارقة كالحديد أي المفارقة من أهل الأصول الفاسدة، فلا بد أن يذكر ذلك الكلام بعينه في ضمن الممانعة ليكون ذلك الكلام مقبولاً بمادته وهيأته معا، مثاله ما قال الشافعي له في إعتاق الراهن العبد المرهون: إنه لا ينفذ إعتاقه؛ لأن الإعتاق تصرف من الراهن يلاقي حق المرتمن بالإبطال، فكان باطلاً كالبيع، فمن جوّز منا مردودا المفارقة قال في جوابه: إن الإعتاق ليس كالبيع؛ لأن البيع يحتمل الفسخ والعتق لا يحتمله،
وكل كلام إلخ لما كان المعارضة في علة المستدل فاسدًا عند الأكثر بين قاعدة بعد بيان تلك المعارضة مقبولة إذا أوردت بهذه القاعدة، فقال الماتن: وكل كلام إلخ، وحاصل معنى العبارة أن كل كلام يذكره أهل الطرد على سبيل المفارقة فأذكره على سبيل الممانعة ليخرج من حيّز الفساد إلى حيّز الصحة ويكون مقبولاً بأصله ووصفه معا. (السنبلي) أصل وضعه إلخ فإنه في الأصل والحقيقة منع للعلة المؤثرة. (القمر) ولكن يذكر إلخ أي يذكره أهل الطرد في مقام السؤال. (القمر) هي المسماة بالمفارقة إلخ فلا يرد عليه أن الكلام ههنا في المعارضة والمفارقة غيرها فلِمَ ذكرها المصنف الله ههنا؟ وتقرير الجواب غير خفي. (السنبلي) لأنه أتى إلخ: دليل لقوله: المسمّاة. (القمر) يقع بها الفرق إلخ فإنه يقول السائل: إن علة الحكم الأصل وصف كذا، وهذا الوصف موجود في الأصل ومعدوم في الفرع (القمر) وهو إلخ : أي إتيان السائل بعلة يقع بها الفرق.(السنبلي)
في إعتاق الراهن أي بدون إذن المرتمن (القمر) إنه لا ينفذ إلخ وعندنا ينفذ إعتاقه.(القمر) كالبيع أي كما أن الراهن إذا باع المرهون بدون إذن المرتمن يردّ هذا البيع، فيكون باطلاً.(القمر) يحتمل الفسخ فيظهر أثر حق المرتمن بأن يمنع النفاذ فينفسخ البيع. (القمر)
لا يحتمله إلخ فلا يظهر أثر حق المرتمن في المنع من النفاذ فينعقد العتق لازما.(القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of Mu'arada (objection). With its genus, differing in measure, like wheat and barley, so the objector objects that the effective cause in the original (i.e., the Malik’s wheat and barley) is not what you said but rather it is eatability and storability, which is absent in plaster, even if it extends to a consensual branch, i.e., rice and millet (meaning capacity and genus) i.e., the branch, or a disputed one, i.e., extends to a disputed branch, which is the third type. Example: if the objector objects in the mentioned issue that the effective cause in the original is taste, and it is not found in plaster, and he (i.e., al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him) holds that it is not measure with genus (i.e., taste) extends to a disputed branch, namely fruits and what is below the measure. And all these types are invalid because the attribute claimed by the objector does not contradict the attribute claimed by the arguer; since the ruling is established by various causes. If his attribute is not transitive (muta'addi), then its corruption is obvious because the purpose of establishing the cause is transitivity. But if the objector’s attribute (i.e., the objector's attribute) is transitive, the mu'arada is also invalid because it has no connection to the matter in dispute except that it indicates the absence of that cause in it, and that does not necessitate the absence of the ruling. The branch (i.e., that mu'arada) is consensual (i.e., agreed upon by the arguer and the objector). (Al-Qamar) 'or disputed' is coordinated with the author's saying, upon him (Al-Qamar) 'disputed' i.e., between the arguer and the objector. (Al-Qamar) 'namely fruits etc.' because fruits and what is below the shari'i measure i.e., half a sa' like a handful or two, there is no riba in them according to us because they are not measurable or weighable, but according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, there is riba in them. (Al-Qamar) 'the attribute which etc.' whether it is transitive or not. (Al-Qamar) 'does not contradict etc.' because mu'arada of causes does not materialize; the cause invented by the objecting objector, even if not found in the branch, but the existence of the cause invented by the arguer in the branch is sufficient to establish the ruling, so his qiyas is valid. And the author of al-Talwih said: The purpose of the objector is to nullify the arguer's attribute; so when he establishes the causality of another attribute, it is possible that each of the two attributes is independently a cause, or that each is a part of a cause, so one cannot be certain about the independence of the arguer's or objector's cause, thus mu'arada occurs, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'various' (shatta) is plural of shatit like mariq and marda, and in the circulating copy is the plural of shattia, i.e., different, so it is not established. (Al-Qamar) 'transitivity': if the ta'lil (causal explanation) is devoid of transitivity, it is invalid due to lack of benefit and purpose, and if the ta'lil is invalid, then the mu'arada is invalid, thus it is said. (Al-Qamar) 'that cause' i.e., the cause invented by the objector. (Al-Qamar) And it is: the absence of that cause in the branch does not necessitate the absence of the ruling because it is possible that the ruling in the branch is established by another cause. (Al-Qamar) 'absence of the ruling etc.' since the ruling is established by various causes, so after the corruption of that cause, another cause remains, and it suffices. (Al-Sanbali). [Page 92] ...
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
The passage discusses mu'arada (objection) in qiyas. It first explains types of mu'arada where the objector proposes a different cause (illa). The author lists three types of branches: (1) a branch agreed upon by both parties, (2) a disputed branch, and (3) a branch where the cause is transitive but the branch is disputed. All such mu'arada are invalid because the objector's cause does not negate the arguer's cause; the ruling can have multiple causes. The key point is that even if the objector's cause is transitive, the objection is still invalid because it only shows the absence of that cause in the branch, but the ruling could be established by another cause. Then the passage introduces a rule: 'Every speech is valid in its origin and use.' This means that when a mu'arada is presented as a mufaraqa (mere distinction) which is invalid, one should frame it as a mumana'a (prevention) to make it acceptable. An example is given: al-Shafi'i argued that a mortgagor's manumission of a mortgaged slave is invalid because it is like a sale that voids the mortgagee's right. The Hanafi response uses the rule: manumission is unlike sale because sale can be rescinded but manumission cannot. By presenting this as a mumana'a (preventing the analogy), the objection becomes valid. The passage emphasizes that the purpose of mu'arada is not just to show a difference but to block the effect of the claimed cause.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): An objection in qiyas where the objector proposes a different effective cause (illa) to invalidate the arguer's analogy.
المفارقة (al-mufaraqa): An objection that merely shows a difference between original and branch without preventing the cause; considered invalid.
الممانعة (al-mumana'a): A valid form of objection that prevents the application of the arguer's cause by showing a conflict or preventing factor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a mu'arada that proposes a different cause (e.g., taste instead of measure) invalid according to Hanafi usul?
A) Because the objector's cause is not transitive.
B) Because the ruling can be established by multiple causes, so the absence of one does not negate the ruling.
C) Because the objector must agree with the arguer's cause.
D) Because qiyas is not valid in the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
A mu'arada that merely proposes a different cause is invalid; to object validly, one must frame it as a mumana'a that prevents the claimed cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
Rule of Mufāraqa and Mumāna'a in Qiyas
Explains how to present a difference between asl and far' as a valid objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mufāraqa from mumāna'a in qiyas and apply the Hanafi rule to convert an invalid objection into a valid one.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a mufāraqa is invalid; present the same point as a mumāna'a to make it a valid objection.

This passage explains a subtle but crucial rule in countering qiyas. When an opponent points out a difference between the asl and far', simply stating that difference (mufāraqa) is not accepted. Instead, you must present it as a denial of the 'illa in the far' (mumāna'a). The example of mortgaged slave emancipation clarifies the distinction between these two forms of objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The passage states that any speech (kalam) is correct in its original meaning, but if it is presented as a mufāraqa it becomes invalid. To make it valid, present it as a mumāna'a.
The rule transforms a flawed objection into an acceptable one.
2
Understand mufāraqa vs. mumāna'a
Mufāraqa is pointing out a difference between asl and far' without denying the 'illa. Mumāna'a is denying the effectiveness of the 'illa in the far'.
The same factual difference can be framed either way.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i analogy
Shafi'i argues that emancipation of a mortgaged slave is invalid like its sale, because both nullify the mortgagee's right. This is a qiyas.
The 'illa is 'nullification of mortgagee's right'.
4
See the Hanafi response as a mumāna'a
The Hanafi says: 'We do not accept that emancipation is like sale because sale can be rescinded and emancipation cannot.' This is not just pointing out a difference; it is denying that the 'illa (nullification) applies equally.
The response is a mumāna'a, not a mufāraqa.
5
Apply the rule
When rebutting any qiyas, if you notice a difference, frame it as 'We do not accept the 'illa in the far' because [reason].' This makes the objection valid.
Always convert mufāraqa into mumāna'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
صحة كل الكلام في أصل وضعه وكل كلام صحيح في الأصل، أي في أصل وضعه وجوهره ولكن يذكر سبيل المفارقة التي هي باطلة عند أهل الأصول، فأذكره على سبيل الممانعة ليخرج عن حيّز الفساد إلى حيّز الصحة، ويكون مقبولاً بأصله ووصفه معًا، وإنما تذكر هذه القاعدة ههنا؛ لأن المعارضة في علة الأصل هي المسماة بالمفارقة عندهم؛ لأنه أتى السائل بعلة يقع بها الفرق بين الأصل والفرع، وهو فاسد عند الأكثر، فإذا أتى السائل بكلام لطيف مقبول في ضمن هذه المفارقة الفاسدة، فلا بد أن يذكر ذلك الكلام بعينه في ضمن الممانعة ليكون ذلك الكلام مقبولاً بمادته وهيئته معا، مثاله ما قال الشافعي في إعتاق الراهن العبد المرهون: إنه لا ينفذ إعتاقه؛ لأن الإعتاق تصرف من الراهن يلاقي حق المرتمن بالإبطال، فكان باطلاً كالبيع، فمن جوّز منا المفارقة قال في جوابه: إن الإعتاق ليس كالبيع؛ لأن البيع يحتمل الفسخ والعتق لا يحتمله، وكل كلام إلخ لما كان المعارضة في علة المستدل فاسدًا عند الأكثر بين قاعدة بعد بيان تلك المعارضة مقبولة إذا أوردت بهذه القاعدة، فقال الماتن: وكل كلام إلخ، وحاصل معنى العبارة أن كل كلام يذكره أهل الطرد على سبيل المفارقة فأذكره على سبيل الممانعة ليخرج من حيّز الفساد إلى حيّز الصحة ويكون مقبولاً بأصله ووصفه معا. (السنبلي) أصل وضعه إلخ فإنه في الأصل والحقيقة منع للعلة المؤثرة. (القمر) ولكن يذكر إلخ أي يذكره أهل الطرد في مقام السؤال. (القمر) هي المسماة بالمفارقة إلخ فلا يرد عليه أن الكلام ههنا في المعارضة والمفارقة غيرها فلِمَ ذكرها المصنف ههنا؟ وتقرير الجواب غير خفي. (السنبلي) لأنه أتى إلخ: دليل لقوله: المسمّاة. (القمر) يقع بها الفرق إلخ فإنه يقول السائل: إن علة الحكم الأصل وصف كذا، وهذا الوصف موجود في الأصل ومعدوم في الفرع (القمر) وهو إلخ : أي إتيان السائل بعلة يقع بها الفرق.(السنبلي) في إعتاق الراهن أي بدون إذن المرتمن (القمر) إنه لا ينفذ إلخ وعندنا ينفذ إعتاقه.(القمر) كالبيع أي كما أن الراهن إذا باع المرهون بدون إذن المرتمن يردّ هذا البيع، فيكون باطلاً.(القمر) يحتمل الفسخ فيظهر أثر حق المرتمن بأن يمنع النفاذ فينفسخ البيع. (القمر) لا يحتمله إلخ فلا يظهر أثر حق المرتمن في المنع من النفاذ فينعقد العتق لازما.(القمر)
بيان دفع المعارضة
فلا يصح القياس، وهذا الفرق هو المعارضة في علة الأصل؛ لأن قائله يقول: إن علة عدم جواز البيع هي كونه محتملاً للفسخ بعد وقوعه فهذا السؤال وإن كان مقبولاً في نفسه لكنه لما جاء به السائل على سبيل المفارقة لا يُقبل منه، فكان حقه أن نورده نحن على سبيل الممانعة فنقول: لا نسلّم أن الإعتاق كالبيع، فإن حكم البيع التوقف على إجازة المرتمن فيما يجوز فسخه لا الإبطال، وأنت في الإعتاق تبطل أصلاً ما لا يجوز فسخه بعد ثبوته حتى لو أجاز المرتهن لا ينفذ إعتاقه عندك. ولما فرغ عن بيان المعارضة شرع في بيان دفعها، فقال: وإذا قامت المعارضة كان السبيل فيها الترجيح، أي ترجيح أحد المعارضين على الآخر. دفعها القياس: أي قياس الإعتاق على البيع (القمر) هي كونه محتملاً إلخ وهذه العلة لا توجد في الفرع أي الإعتاق. (القمر) الإعتاق كالبيع إلخ تقريره أن الأصل ههنا البيع، فإن أريد أن حكم الأصل ههنا البطلان فهو ممنوع؛ لأن الحكم عندنا في بيع الراهن الرهن التوقف، وإن كان حكم الأصل التوقف على إجازة المرتهن، فحكم الفرع إن ادّعيتم أنه البطلان فلا يكون الحكمان متماثلين، فكيف يصح القياس؟ وإن ادعيتم أنه التوقف على إجازة المرتمن فلا يمكن فإن العتق غير محتمل للفسخ فإن العبد أو المولى لو أراد فسخه بعد وقوعه لا ينفسخ . (القمر) حكم البيع أي بيع الراهن المرهون.(القمر) فيما يجوز فسخه إلخ وهو الإعتاق يعني إذا باع الراهن المرهون ينفذ موقوفا على إجازة المرتهن، وإذا أعتق الراهن المرهون أنت تبطل أصلاً، فقد غيّرت حكم الأصل، والحاصل أنا لا نسلّم أن قياسكم صحيح؛ لأن الأصل وهو البيع، والفرع هو العتق، وحكم الأصل هو التوقف وهو لا يوجد في الفرع، فإن العتق لا يتوقف، فعلى قياسكم كان أن يثبت التوقف فيه ولكنكم أثبتم حكمًا آخر في الفرع، وهو البطلان الذي هو حكم جديد لم يتعد من الأصل؛ لأن ذلك لم يكن موجودًا فيه، فكيف التعدي منه؟ (السنبلي) يجوز كالبيع والإجازة وغيرهما. (المحشي لا الإبطال الخ: فانعدم شرط القياس، وهو أن يتعدى الحكم الأصلي بعينه في الفرع وههنا لم يوجد؛ لأن الحكم في البيع التوقف وفي الإعتاق الإبطال (السنبلي) ما لا يجوز كالإعتاق والتدبير وغيره. (المحشي وإذا قامت المعارضة: أي لم تندفع بالممانعة والقلب وغيرهما. (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas: Every speech is correct in its original meaning, i.e., in its original and essence, but if it is mentioned as a mufāraqa (difference) which is invalid according to the scholars of usul, then I should mention it as a mumāna'a (objection) to take it out from the realm of invalidity to the realm of validity, and it becomes acceptable in its essence and description. This rule is mentioned here because the mu'āraḍa (counter-argument) in the 'illa of the asl is called mufāraqa by them; because the opponent brings an 'illa that makes a difference between the asl and the far', and it is invalid according to most. So if the opponent brings a subtle and acceptable statement within this invalid mufāraqa, he must mention that exact statement within the mumāna'a for it to be accepted in its content and form. Example: What al-Shafi'i said about the mortgagor emancipating the mortgaged slave: that his emancipation is not effective because emancipation is an act of the mortgagor that meets the right of the mortgagee by nullification, so it is invalid like sale. So one who allows mufāraqa from us says in response: Emancipation is not like sale because sale can be rescinded and emancipation cannot. [Explanation continues...] Statement of Daf' al-Mu'āraḍa (repelling the counter-argument): So the qiyas is not valid, and this difference is the mu'āraḍa in the 'illa of the asl because its proponent says that the 'illa of the impermissibility of sale is its possibility of rescission after occurrence. This question, though acceptable in itself, when brought by the opponent as a mufāraqa is not accepted. So it is our right to present it as a mumāna'a by saying: We do not accept that emancipation is like sale, for the ruling of sale is suspension pending the mortgagee's permission in what can be rescinded, not nullification, and in emancipation you nullify absolutely what cannot be rescinded after its establishment, so even if the mortgagee permits, the emancipation is not effective according to you. [Then it discusses that when mu'āraḍa stands, the way is tarjīh (preponderance).]
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is an usul al-fiqh rule regarding how to handle a counter-argument (mu'āraḍa) in qiyas. The text distinguishes between presenting a difference (mufāraqa) and presenting it as an objection (mumāna'a). According to the Hanafi usul scholars, a difference that is pointed out by the opponent between the original case (asl) and the new case (far') is considered invalid (fāsid) if presented as a mufāraqa. However, if the same point is presented as a mumāna'a (i.e., denying the effectiveness of the 'illa in the far'), it becomes valid and must be addressed. The author illustrates this with the classic debate between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the emancipation of a mortgaged slave. The Shafi'i argues that the emancipation is invalid because it is like selling the mortgaged slave without the mortgagee's permission. The Hanafi responds by noting that sale can be rescinded, whereas emancipation cannot, thus the 'illa (possibility of rescission) does not apply. The key point is that this response should be structured as a mumāna'a (objection to the 'illa) rather than simply pointing out a difference. The passage then transitions to discussing the repelling of mu'āraḍa, stating that if the mu'āraḍa stands (i.e., is not repelled by mumāna'a or other means), then the way to resolve it is tarjīh (preponderance). The Hanafi position is that in the case of a mortgagor emancipating a mortgaged slave, the emancipation is effective and binding, unlike the sale which is suspended pending the mortgagee's permission.

Key Terms
المفارقة (al-mufāraqa): A counter-argument that points out a difference between the asl and far' in the 'illa, considered invalid when presented by the opponent.
الممانعة (al-mumāna'a): An objection denying the effectiveness of the 'illa in the far', which is considered a valid way to rebut a qiyas.
المعارضة (al-mu'āraḍa): A counter-argument challenging the 'illa or the qiyas, which can be repelled by mumāna'a or heart (qalb) or ultimately by tarjīh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul rule explained in this passage, how should one present a difference between the original case (asl) and the new case (far') when rebutting a qiyas?
A) As a mufāraqa (difference) to show the 'illa does not apply.
B) As a mumāna'a (objection) denying the effectiveness of the 'illa in the far'.
C) As a simple comparison (tashbīh) between the two cases.
D) As a direct refutation (radd) of the 'illa without any specific format.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a mufāraqa is invalid; convert it into a mumāna'a to make a valid objection in qiyas.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Repelling Mu'āraḍah and Defining Tarjīḥ
Explanation of how to counter opposition in analogical reasoning and define preponderance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school repels opposition in qiyas through tarjīḥ and define tarjīḥ as the act of preferring one evidence over another by a descriptive quality.

Core Idea
Opposition in qiyas is repelled by tarjīḥ: preferring one evidence over another by a descriptive quality.

This passage from the chapter on Qiyas addresses a fundamental challenge in analogical reasoning: when an opponent presents a counter-analogy (muʿāraḍah), how does the responder respond? The answer is through tarjīḥ (preponderance), which requires showing that one evidence has a descriptive quality that makes it stronger. The text uses the example of a mortgagor's emancipation of a slave versus its sale to illustrate how the lack of revocability in emancipation breaks the analogy. It then defines tarjīḥ precisely, distinguishing the act of the mujtahid from the intrinsic quality of being preponderant (rajḥān). Understanding this distinction is crucial for engaging in scholarly debate and ijtihad within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem of muʿāraḍah in qiyas
Identify that muʿāraḍah occurs when an opponent offers a counter-analogy that conflicts with the original qiyas. The responder cannot simply ignore it; they must address it.
Muʿāraḍah is distinct from simple denial; it presents an alternative reasoning that must be weighed.
2
Analyze the emancipation vs. sale example
Follow the argument: the original qiyas claims emancipation is like sale. The Hanafi response shows that sale is revocable, so it can be suspended (tawaqquf), but emancipation is irrevocable, so the ʿillah fails. This demonstrates how tarjīḥ works by identifying a missing descriptive quality (waṣf) in the branch.
The key point is that the 'illah of revocability present in the original is absent in the branch, so the analogy is invalid.
3
Define tarjīḥ and distinguish from rajḥān
The text defines tarjīḥ as 'superiority of one of two similars over the other in description' (faḍl aḥad al-mithlayn ʿalā al-ākhar waṣfan). This is an act of the mujtahid, not the intrinsic superiority (rajḥān) of the evidence.
Tarjīḥ is transitive (the mujtahid does it), while rajḥān is intransitive (the evidence is preponderant).
4
Apply the definition to examples
Consider the examples: the testimony of an upright person is preferred over that of a sinful person because of the waṣf of ʿadālah. But four witnesses are not preferred over two because number is not a descriptive quality; it is quantity. Similarly, a qiyas is not preferred over another by having a supporting qiyas, because multiplicity does not add a descriptive quality.
Preponderance is based on the strength of the ʿillah (the cause), not the number of evidences.

أي يوافقه في الحكم
تندفع المعارضة فإن حكم العقل ترجيح الراجح (القمر) صار: أي المجيب منقطعا، فإن الانقطاع عبارة عن حالة تعتري المناظر بالعجز عما رام بالمناظرة. (القمر) وإن يَتَأت أي الترجيح له، أي للمجيب. (القمر) فقد مضى أي فصل التعارض بين الحجج (المحشي) أي بيان إلخ فيحصل بهذا البيان ظن في النتيجة بالنسبة إلى نتيجة الدليل الآخر، فيعمل بها، وهذا دفع دخل، وهو: أن فضل أحد المثلين على الآخر وصفا رجحان، فكيف فسرتم به الترجيح؟ وحاصل الدفع أن المضاف في الكلام محذوف (القمر) أي بيان إلخ: جواب سؤال مقدر، تقديره: أن تفسير الترجيح بالفضل غير صحيح؛ لأن الترجيح هو تفضيل المجتهد أحد الدليلين على الآخر، والفضل بعينه الرجحان، وهو ليس بفعل المجتهد، فكأنه فسر المتعدي باللازم. (السنبلي) ولهذا أي لكون الفضل والرجحان بحسب الوصف لا بحسب الذات يترجّح شهادة العادل إلخ لثبوت الفضل بحسب وصف العدالة. (القمر) ولهذا يترجّح إلخ وهذا مبني على أصل مشهور، وهو أن الترجيح يقع بقوة في العلة لا بكثرة العلل (السنبلي ولا يترجّح إلخ: لأن الفضل لا يثبت بحسب الذات.(القمر) أربعة إلخ لأن ههنا لا اعتبار للتعدّد. (السنبلي) لا يترجّح القياس إلخ فإن القياسين أو الحديثين أو الآيتين مساويان في إفادة الحكم لقياس أو حديث أو آية وقيل: إن الحديثين إذا تأكد أحدهما بالآخر بأن ينسد باب تأويله يرجّحان على حديث يعارضهما، فإنه بدون التأكيد يحتمل التأويل، وهذا الترجيح في الحقيقة إنما هو بنظر قوة الدليل لا بالنظر إلى أن ههنا دليلين (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of Repelling Opposition. So qiyas is not valid, and this difference is the opposition in the cause of the original case; because its proponent says: the cause of the permissibility of sale is that it is susceptible to revocation after occurrence. So this question, although acceptable in itself, when the questioner brings it in the manner of differentiation, it is not accepted from him. It would be proper for us to present it as a prevention and say: We do not accept that emancipation is like sale, because the ruling of sale is suspension pending the mortgagee's permission concerning what can be revoked, not annulment. While you, in emancipation, annul fundamentally that which cannot be revoked after its establishment, so that even if the mortgagee permits, the emancipation does not take effect according to you. (i.e., emancipation by the mortgagor). When he finished explaining opposition, he began explaining its repelling. He said: Explanation of Repelling Opposition. And when opposition occurs, the course of action is preponderance, i.e., preferring one of the two opposing evidences over the other. The repelling of opposition: Qiyas: i.e., analogizing emancipation to sale. (al-Qamar) It is being susceptible etc. And this cause is not found in the branch, i.e., emancipation. (al-Qamar) Emancipation is like sale etc. Its explanation: The original here is sale. If it is intended that the ruling of the original here is nullity, it is denied, because the ruling according to us regarding the mortgagor's sale is suspension. If the ruling of the original is suspension pending the mortgagee's permission, then the ruling of the branch, if you claim it is nullity, then the two rulings are not similar, so how can qiyas be valid? And if you claim it is suspension pending the mortgagee's permission, that is impossible, because emancipation is not susceptible to revocation; for if the slave or the master wanted to revoke it after its occurrence, it would not be revoked. (al-Qamar) The ruling of the sale: i.e., sale of the mortgaged property by the mortgagor. (al-Qamar) 'Concerning what can be revoked' etc.: it is emancipation, meaning when the mortgagor sells the mortgaged property, it is executed suspended on the mortgagee's permission; and when the mortgagor emancipates the mortgaged property, you annul it fundamentally. So you have changed the ruling of the original. The conclusion is: we do not accept that your qiyas is correct, because the original is sale, and the branch is emancipation. The ruling of the original is suspension, and that does not exist in the branch, because emancipation is not suspended. So according to your qiyas, suspension should be established in it, but you have established another ruling in the branch, i.e., nullity, which is a new ruling that has not been transferred from the original, because that [nullity] did not exist in it. So how can the transfer be made? (al-Sanbali) It is permitted like sale and permission and others. (al-Muhashi) 'Not annulment' etc.: So the condition of qiyas is absent, which is that the original ruling itself be transferred to the branch. Here it is not found, because the ruling in sale is suspension and in emancipation is annulment. (al-Sanbali) 'What cannot be revoked' etc.: like emancipation, tadbir, and others. (al-Muhashi) 'And when opposition occurs': i.e., it is not repelled by prevention, reversal, etc. (al-Qamar) Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of Repelling Opposition. Such that the opposition is repelled. If the responder cannot achieve preponderance, he becomes cut off. And if he can achieve it (i.e., the first proponent), then the questioner may oppose him with another preponderance. This is the ruling of opposition in qiyas. As for opposition in transmitted texts, its explanation has already passed. (i.e., the texts). And it (tarjīḥ) is the superiority of one of two similars over the other in terms of description, i.e., an explanation of the superiority of one of the two opposing things. It is not a definition of being preponderant (rajḥān) but of preponderating (tarjīḥ). The meaning of his statement 'in terms of description' is that the thing by which preponderance occurs is not an independent proof by itself, but is a description of the essence, not subsisting by itself. For this reason, the testimony of an upright person is preferred over the testimony of a sinful person, but the testimony of four is not preferred over the testimony of two. And qiyas is not preferred over a qiyas that opposes it by another third qiyas that supports the latter, because it becomes as if on one side there is one qiyas and on the other side two qiyas. (i.e., that thing) (i.e., agrees with it in ruling) Opposition is repelled, for reason dictates preferring the preponderant. (al-Qamar) 'He becomes cut off': i.e., the responder, for being cut off is a state that befalls the debater due to inability regarding what he aimed for in the debate. (al-Qamar) 'And if he can achieve it': i.e., preponderance for him, i.e., for the responder. (al-Qamar) 'Has already passed': i.e., the chapter on conflict between proofs. (al-Muhashi) i.e., explanation, etc. So by this explanation, a supposition is obtained regarding the result in relation to the result of the other proof, and action is taken accordingly. This is a repelling of an objection: that the superiority of one of two similars over the other in description is 'rajḥān' (being preponderant), so how have you interpreted tarjīḥ with it? The summary of the repelling is that the genitive construction in the statement is omitted. (al-Qamar) i.e., explanation, etc.: answer to an estimated objection, its estimation: that the interpretation of tarjīḥ as superiority is incorrect, because tarjīḥ is the muftahid's act of preferring one of the two proofs over the other, and superiority itself is rajḥān, which is not an act of the muftahid, so it is as if he interpreted the transitive as intransitive. (al-Sanbali) 'For this reason': i.e., because superiority and being preponderant are by virtue of description, not by virtue of essence, the testimony of the upright is preferred, etc., due to the establishment of superiority by virtue of the description of uprightness. (al-Qamar) 'For this reason it is preferred, etc.': This is based on a well-known principle: that preponderance occurs by strength in the cause, not by multiplicity of causes. (al-Sanbali) 'And it is not preferred, etc.': because superiority is not established by virtue of essence. (al-Qamar) 'Four, etc.': because here multiplicity is not considered. (al-Sanbali) 'And qiyas is not preferred, etc.': for two analogies or two hadiths or two verses are equal in conveying the ruling to one analogy, hadith, or verse. And it is said that if two hadiths are strengthened one by the other such that the door of interpretation is closed, they are preferred over a hadith that opposes them, because without strengthening it is open to interpretation. And this preponderance in reality is by considering the strength of the proof, not by considering that there are two proofs. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Qiyas (analogical reasoning) and deals with the topic of repelling mu'āraḍah (opposition) in qiyas. Mu'āraḍah occurs when the opponent presents a counter-analogy that challenges the original analogy. The author explains that the proper response is to seek tarjīḥ (preponderance) by showing that one of the two analogies is stronger. The discussion includes an example: the analogy of a mortgagor's emancipation of a mortgaged slave to a mortgagor's sale of mortgaged property. The opponent argues that both should be suspended pending the mortgagee's permission, but the Hanafi response is that emancipation is not revocable, so it cannot be suspended; thus the analogy fails. This leads to the definition of tarjīḥ as 'the superiority of one of two similars over the other in terms of description' (faḍl aḥad al-mithlayn ʿalā al-ākhar waṣfan). The author clarifies that tarjīḥ is an act of the mujtahid, while rajḥān (being preponderant) is a quality intrinsic to the evidence. He gives examples: the testimony of an upright person is preferred over that of a sinful person due to the quality of ʿadālah (uprightness), but the testimony of four people is not necessarily preferred over two because the quality of number is not considered in testimony. Similarly, a qiyas is not preferred merely because it is supported by another qiyas; preponderance depends on the strength of the ʿillah (cause), not on multiplicity. The passage also distinguishes between opposition in qiyas and opposition in naqliyyāt (textual evidences). The principle is that when opposition arises, the debating partner must attempt tarjīḥ; if he cannot, he is considered 'munqaṭiʿ' (cut off).

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-muʿāraḍah): The situation where an opponent presents a counter-evidence or counter-analogy that challenges the original proof
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): The act of preferring one evidence over another based on a descriptive quality

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, why is the emancipation of a mortgaged slave not analogous to its sale?
A) Because emancipation requires the slave's consent, while sale does not.
B) Because sale is revocable and thus can be suspended, while emancipation is not revocable, so suspension is impossible.
C) Because the mortgagee's permission is required for both, but emancipation is final.
D) Because the analogy is between two different types of property.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method to resolve opposition in qiyas is tarjīḥ: preferring one evidence over another by a descriptive quality (waṣf), not by mere quantity or intrinsic strength.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Tarjīḥ in Qiyās: Definition and Conditions
Explains tarjīḥ as quality-based preference and its applications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of tarjīḥ, distinguish it from rajḥān, and apply the condition that tarjīḥ is by an inherent attribute (sifa), not by multiplicity.

Core Idea
Tarjīḥ prefers by quality, not quantity — one just witness outweighs many sinful ones.

This lesson unpacks the concept of tarjīḥ (preponderance) as used in Hanafi usul al-fiqh to resolve apparent conflicts between qiyās evidences. The text emphasizes that tarjīḥ is not about counting proofs but about the strength of an attribute within the evidence itself. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a mujtahid when weighing opposing analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Find the sentence that defines tarjīḥ as 'superiority of one of the two similars over the other by a description'. Note that the text clarifies this is not a definition of rajḥān (state of superiority) but of tarjīḥ (act of preponderating).
The definition uses 'فضل أحد المثلين على الآخر وصفاً'.
2
Distinguish tarjīḥ from rajḥān
Understand that tarjīḥ is the action of the mujtahid, while rajḥān is the inherent superiority of the evidence. The text states that the definition given is for tarjīḥ, not rajḥān.
The commentary emphasizes this difference to avoid confusion.
3
Understand the condition 'by a description'
The 'description' (sifa) is an attribute that inheres in the evidence itself, not an independent proof. For example, justice (ʿadāla) is a description of the witness, not a separate dalīl.
This condition excludes multiplicity as a basis for tarjīḥ.
4
Apply to the examples
Examine the examples: testimony of a just person preferred over a sinful person (attribute of justice), but four witnesses not preferred over two (no attribute). Similarly, a single qiyās is not strengthened by a supporting qiyās because the attribute is not multiplied.
The text also gives examples of wounds and shufʿa to reinforce the principle.

بحيث تندفع المعارضة، فإن لم يتأت للمجيب الترجيح صار منقطعًا، وإن يتأت له أي المعلل الأول فللسائل أن يعارضه بترجيح آخر، وهذا هو حكم المعارضة في القياس، وأما المعارضة في النقليات فقد مضى بيانها. أي النصوص وهو عبارة عن فضل أحد المثلين على الآخر وصفًا، أي بيان فضل أحد المثلين، ولا يكون أي المتعارضين تعريفا للرجحان لا للترجيح، ومعنى قوله: "وصفاً" أن لا يكون ذلك الشيء الذي يقع به الترجيح دليلاً مستقلاً بنفسه، بل يكون وصفاً للذات غير قائم بنفسه، ولهذا يترجّح شهادة العادل على شهادة الفاسق، ولا يترجّح شهادة أربعة على شهادة شاهدين. لا يترجّح القياس على قياس يعارضه بقياس آخر ثالث يؤيده؛ لأنه يصير كأن في جانب قياسًا وفي جانب قياسين. أي ذلك الشيء أي يوافقه في الحكم. تندفع المعارضة فإن حكم العقل ترجيح الراجح (القمر) صار: أي المجيب منقطعا، فإن الانقطاع عبارة عن حالة تعتري المناظر بالعجز عما رام بالمناظرة. (القمر) وإن يَتَأت أي الترجيح له، أي للمجيب. (القمر) فقد مضى أي فصل التعارض بين الحجج (المحشي) أي بيان إلخ فيحصل بهذا البيان ظن في النتيجة بالنسبة إلى نتيجة الدليل الآخر، فيعمل بها، وهذا دفع دخل، وهو: أن فضل أحد المثلين على الآخر وصفا رجحان، فكيف فسرتم به الترجيح؟ وحاصل الدفع أن المضاف في الكلام محذوف (القمر) أي بيان إلخ: جواب سؤال مقدر، تقديره: أن تفسير الترجيح بالفضل غير صحيح؛ لأن الترجيح هو تفضيل المجتهد أحد الدليلين على الآخر، والفضل بعينه الرجحان، وهو ليس بفعل المجتهد، فكأنه فسر المتعدي باللازم. (السنبلي) ولهذا أي لكون الفضل والرجحان بحسب الوصف لا بحسب الذات يترجّح شهادة العادل إلخ لثبوت الفضل بحسب وصف العدالة. (القمر) ولهذا يترجّح إلخ وهذا مبني على أصل مشهور، وهو أن الترجيح يقع بقوة في العلة لا بكثرة العلل (السنبلي ولا يترجّح إلخ: لأن الفضل لا يثبت بحسب الذات.(القمر) أربعة إلخ لأن ههنا لا اعتبار للتعدّد. (السنبلي) لا يترجّح القياس إلخ فإن القياسين أو الحديثين أو الآيتين مساويان في إفادة الحكم لقياس أو حديث أو آية وقيل: إن الحديثين إذا تأكد أحدهما بالآخر بأن ينسد باب تأويله يرجّحان على حديث يعارضهما، فإنه بدون التأكيد يحتمل التأويل، وهذا الترجيح في الحقيقة إنما هو بنظر قوة الدليل لا بالنظر إلى أن ههنا دليلين (القمر)

وكذا الحديث لا يترجّح على حديث يعارضه بحديث ثالث يؤيده، والكتاب لا يترجّح على آية تعارضه بآية ثالثة تؤيده وإنما يترجّح كل واحد من القياس والحديث والكتاب بقوة فيه، فيكون الاستحسان الصحيح الأثر مقدّمًا على القياس الجلي الفاسد الأثر، والحديث الذي هو مشهور مقدّمًا على خبر الواحد، والكتاب الذي هو محكم قطعى مقدّمًا على ما هو ظني. وكذا صاحب الجراحات لا يترجّح على صاحب جراحة واحدة حتى تكون الدية نصفين، فإن جرح راحةً واحدةً وجرحه آخر جراحات متعددة، ومات المجروح بها، كانت الدية بين الجارحين سواء بخلاف ما إذا كان جراحة أحدهما أقوى أي بجميع الجراحات أي صالحة للقتل من الآخر؛ إذ ينسب الموت إليه بأن قطع واحد يد رجل، والآخر جز رقبته كان القاتل الأقوى هو الجاز؛ إذ لا يتصوّر الإنسان بدون الرقبة، ويتصور بدون اليد. وكذا قلنا الشفيعان في الشقص الشائع المبيع بسهمين متفاوتين سواء في استحقاق الشفعة، ولا يترجّح أحدهما على الآخر بكثرة نصيبه صورتها دار مشتركة بين ثلاثة نفر: بقوة فيه: الباء للسببية أي بسبب قوة في الدليل؛ فإن الشيء إنما يتقوّى بصفة توجد في ذاته لا بانضمام مثله إليه كما في المحسوسات. (القمر) مقدمًا إلخ كما في طهارة سؤر سباع الطير من أنهم عملوا بالاستحسان لا بالقياس الجلي. (القمر) الذي هو محكم إلخ وكذا الكتاب الذي هو مفسر مقدّمًا على المجمل، واعلم أن ما في شرح "الحسامي" يعارض ما في "التلويح" ههنا، فإن عبارة أول الذكر يدل على أن المصير من كتاب الله إلى السنة ليس بجائز، وعبارة ثاني الذكر يدل على أنه جائز، وليس هذا موقع إيراد العبارتين، ههنا، فتبصر وتدبّر. (السنبلي) وكذا إلخ: أي مثل عدم ترجّح الدليلين على دليل واحد لا يترجّح إلخ؛ لاستواء الجراحة الواحدة والجراحات في الإفضاء إلى الموت فإن الإنسان قد يموت من جراحة واحدة وقد لا يموت من جراحات متعدّدة، فلا يعتبر العدد في الجراحة، بل يعتبر عدد الجارحين (القمر) وجرحه أي جرح ذلك الرجل آخر جراحات كل واحدة منها صالحة للقتل. (القمر) الجارحين سواء أي على عاقلتهما، وهذا في جراحة الخطأ، وأما في جراحة العمد فيقتص منهما إذا مات المجروح؛ فإن القصاص لا يقبل التجزي. (القمر) إذ لا يتصوّر الإنسان إلخ فالترجيح لزيادة قوة فيما هو علة للقتل. (القمر) بسهمين إلخ متعلق بالشفيعين أي بسبب ملك سهمين. (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyās. Explanation of pushing back objection. Such that the objection is repelled. If the responder cannot perform tarjīḥ, he becomes cut off. And if he can (i.e., the first reasoner), then the questioner may oppose him with another tarjīḥ, and this is the ruling of objection in qiyās. As for objection in transmitted texts, its explanation has already passed. It (tarjīḥ) is the superiority of one of the two similars over the other by a description, i.e., showing the superiority of one of the two similars, and it is not a definition of rajḥān (superiority) but of tarjīḥ (preponderance). The meaning of 'by a description' is that the thing by which tarjīḥ occurs is not an independent proof by itself, but rather a description of the essence not subsisting by itself. For this reason, the testimony of a just person is preferred over the testimony of a sinful person, and the testimony of four is not preferred over the testimony of two. A qiyās is not preferred over a qiyās that opposes it by a third qiyās that supports it, because it becomes as if on one side there is one qiyās and on the other side two qiyās. (Commentary continues...)
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of tarjīḥ (preponderance) in the context of qiyās (analogy). The text defines tarjīḥ as the superiority of one of two similar things over the other by an attribute (sifa), not by the number of proofs. It distinguishes between tarjīḥ (the act of the mujtahid) and rajḥān (the state of being superior). The commentary clarifies that the attribute is not an independent proof but a quality inherent in the thing. Examples are given: a just witness's testimony is preferred over a sinful one's because of the attribute of justice; four witnesses are not preferred over two because preference is based on quality, not quantity. Similarly, a qiyās is not strengthened by a supporting qiyās because then it becomes two proofs against one. The same applies to hadith and Quranic verses. The text then gives further examples: multiple wounds vs. one wound in liability for blood money, and two partners with unequal shares in a property. In both cases, preference is based on strength of the cause (illa), not multiplicity. A marginal note warns about a contradiction between two commentaries on whether one may move from Quran to Sunnah, but the author leaves it unresolved.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): Preponderating one evidence over another by an attribute present in it, not by external proofs.
الرجحان (al-rajḥān): The state of being superior, not the act of preponderating.
المعارضة (al-mu‘āraḍa): Opposition between two evidences that are apparently equal.
الصفة (al-ṣifa): The attribute inherent in the evidence that forms the basis of tarjīḥ, e.g., justice in a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage on tarjīḥ, why is the testimony of a just person preferred over that of a sinful person?
A) Because a just person is more numerous in court.
B) Because justice is an attribute of the witness that makes his testimony stronger.
C) Because the sinful person's testimony is always rejected.
D) Because two just witnesses are required in all cases.

Key Takeaway
Tarjīḥ in Hanafi usul is based on inherent quality (sifa), not on quantity; it is the act of preferring, not the state of being preferred.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Principles of Rebutting Opposition in Qiyas
Explains the rule for resolving contradiction between evidences by intrinsic preponderance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tarjih based on intrinsic strength and distinguish it from accumulation-based preponderance in resolving conflicting evidences.

Core Idea
Preponderance (tarjih) is based on intrinsic strength, not external accumulation.

How does a Hanafi jurist resolve an apparent contradiction between two legal proofs? This passage from Noor al-Anwar lays down a foundational rule: preponderance is determined by the inherent strength of each evidence, not by gathering supporting evidences. We will unpack this rule, apply it to real examples, and see how it shapes the Hanafi approach to istihsan, hadith, and even disputes in preemption law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule of tarjih
Find the sentence that states how preponderance is achieved. The text says: 'Rather, each of analogy, hadith, and Book is given preponderance by its own strength.' This is the key principle: intrinsic strength, not external support.
The phrase 'بقوة فيه' indicates that strength is in the evidence itself.
2
Understand the three exceptions/precedence rules
The text gives three specific applications: 1) valid athar-based istihsan over clear analogy with weak athar, 2) widely transmitted hadith (mashhur) over solitary report (khabar wahid), 3) definitive Quranic verse (muhkam qat'i) over speculative (zanni). Each is a case of intrinsic strength prevailing.
These are not exhaustive but illustrate the principle.
3
Analyze the wounding example
The example of one person with multiple wounds vs. one with a single wound shows that number of wounds does not create preponderance; only the strength of the causal link matters. Death is attributed to the stronger cause (e.g., beheading over hand-cutting).
This reinforces the idea that quality, not quantity, determines preponderance.
4
Examine the preemption dispute
The passage presents a disagreement with al-Shafi'i on division of preempted property. Hanafi: equal division regardless of shares; Shafi'i: proportional to shares. The Hanafi argument is that ownership as a whole is the cause ('illa), not proportional parts.
This is a concrete illustration of how the principle of intrinsic strength applies in furu'.
