Chapter of Analogy
94
Explanation of Rebutting Opposition
Likewise, a hadith is not given preponderance over a hadith that contradicts it by a third hadith that supports it, and the Book is not given preponderance over a verse that contradicts it by a third verse that supports it. Rather, each of analogy, hadith, and Book is given preponderance by its own strength. So the valid athar-based istihsan is given precedence over clear analogy with weak athar, and the well-known hadith is given precedence over a solitary report, and the Book that is definitive and unambiguous is given precedence over what is speculative.
And
A man
Similarly, the one with multiple injuries does not take precedence over one with a single injury until the blood money is half each. For if one wounded with a single stab and another wounded him with multiple wounds, and the wounded died from them, the blood money is shared equally between the two wounders, unlike if one's wound was stronger
i.e., with all the wounds
i.e., lethal
than the other; for then death is attributed to the stronger, e.g., if one cut off a hand and the other beheaded, the killer is the beheader; for a person cannot be imagined without the neck, but can be imagined without the hand.
Similarly, we say: two preemptors in a common undivided share sold for two unequal shares are equal in entitlement to preemption, and one is not given preponderance over the other by the size of his share. Its form: a house shared among three persons:
... (glosses)...
One owns a sixth, another a half, and a third a third. If the owner of half sells, and the other two claim preemption, the sold property is divided between them equally in preemption. According to al-Shafi'i, it is divided into thirds; because preemption is a benefit of ownership, so it is divided according to its proportion. The issue is placed in the share even though the rule of adjacency with us is such to allow the disagreement with al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar, under 'Explanation of Rebutting Opposition,' lays down fundamental rules for preferring one legal evidence over another. The author establishes that preponderance (tarjih) is based on the intrinsic strength of the evidence itself, not on external support from additional similar evidences. Thus, a hadith is not strengthened by a third hadith supporting it against a contradicting hadith; similarly for Quranic verses. Instead, each evidence type (analogy, hadith, Quran) is weighed by its own quality: sound athar-based istihsan over clear analogy with weak athar, widely transmitted hadith (mashhur) over solitary reports (khabar wahid), and definitive unambiguous Quranic verses (muhkam qat'i) over speculative ones. The passage then illustrates with a legal example: a person with multiple wounds is not automatically considered more liable for death than one with a single wound; liability is based on the strength of the cause, not the number. If one wounds a single stab and another inflicts multiple wounds, and the victim dies, blood money is divided equally unless one wound is clearly stronger (e.g., beheading vs. cutting a hand). The same principle applies in preemption (shuf'a): co-owners with different shares (one-sixth, one-half, one-third) are equal in the right of preemption when one sells his share, and the preemptors divide the sold property equally, not according to their shares. This contradicts al-Shafi'i, who divides the preempted property in proportion to ownership stakes. The Hanafi position is that preemption is a right attached to ownership as a whole, not proportional, analogous to adjacency rights where neighbors are equal regardless of proximity. The glosses by al-Qamar and al-Sanbali clarify that the strength of evidence is inherent, not from accumulation, and they caution against conflicting statements from al-Hasami and al-Talwih regarding resorting from Quran to Sunnah.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A legal method that gives precedence to a stronger effect (athar) over a clear analogy, based on a sound transmission or rational preference.
القياس الجلي (al-qiyas al-jali): Clear analogy where the 'illa (cause) is evident and undisputed.
دفع المعارضة (daf' al-mu'arada): Rebutting or resolving apparent contradiction between legal evidences by applying principles of preponderance (tarjih).
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of giving preponderance to one evidence over another when they conflict, based on intrinsic strength.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two pieces of evidence are compared in the example of istihsan over clear analogy?
A) Valid athar-based istihsan and clear analogy with weak athar
B) Widely transmitted hadith and solitary report
C) Definitive Quranic verse and speculative verse
D) Multiple wounds and single wound

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when evidences conflict, the preponderant one is determined by its intrinsic strength, not by external supports or accumulation.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Preponderance by Strength of Effect (Quwwat al-Athar) in Hanafi Usul
Defines criteria for preponderance in conflicting qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four criteria for tarjih in conflicting qiyas and apply the principle of quwwat al-athar using the example of istihsan.

Core Idea
Preponderance between conflicting qiyas is determined by the strength of effect, not by quantity or personal preference.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar introduces the four ways to prefer one qiyas over another when they conflict. The key principle is 'strength of effect' (quwwat al-athar), which is why istihsan prevails over clear qiyas. A subtle point clarifies that justice ('adala) is not gradable, so a 'more just' witness does not have a stronger effect. Understanding these criteria is essential for navigating conflicting analogies in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall topic
The passage is titled 'Explanation of Aspects of Preponderance' (Wujuh al-Tarjih). It lists the ways to preponderate one qiyas over another when they conflict.
The passage mentions 'four' ways but elaborates only one: quwwat al-athar.
2
Locate the first criterion: quwwat al-athar
Find the phrase 'بقوة الأثر' (by strength of effect). This is the primary criterion discussed. The passage explains that istihsan is given preponderance over qiyas because its effect is stronger.
The gloss clarifies that both qiyas must be effective; only then does preponderance arise.
3
Analyze the objection and response
A hypothetical objection: if strength of effect determines preponderance, a more just witness (ashhad) should be preferred over a just one. The Hanafi response: justice does not admit of degrees; it is defined as refraining from prohibitions, so there is no 'more just' that would increase effect.
This shows that quwwat al-athar refers to the intrinsic soundness of the cause, not the personal quality of the narrator or witness.
4
Compare with the analogy to hadith transmission
The gloss (al-Sanbali) analogizes to hadith: a hadith becomes proof by its chain, and its strength is increased by fame, the narrator's fiqh, precision, etc. Similarly, a qiyas is strengthened by the soundness of its illa.
This analogy helps understand that 'strength' comes from verifiable factors, not subjective opinion.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position on tarjih
The Hanafi school holds that preponderance is based on the quality of the cause (illa), not on the quantity of proponents or the number of textual proofs. The effective cause must be sound, free from obstruction, and truly impactful.
This principle distinguishes Hanafi usul from some other schools that may prioritize other factors.

Source Text

بيان وجوه الترجيح
نصيبه،

كالثمر للفجر
الملك
المسألة في الشقص وإن كان حكم الجوار عندنا كذلك ليتأتى فيه خلاف الشافعي ليه.
بيان وجوه الترجيح] وما يقع به الترجيح، أي ترجيح أحد القياسين على الآخر أربعة بقوة الأثر كالاستحسان في معارضة القياس والأثر في الاستحسان أقوى، فيترجّح عليه، فإن قيل: فعلى هذا يلزم القياس الجلي
أن يكون الشاهد الأعدل راجحا على العادل؛ لأن أثره أقوى؟ أجيب بأنا لا نسلّم أن
العدالة تختلف بالزيادة والنقصان فإنها عبارة عن الانزجار عن محظورات الدين بالاحتراز
يكون المبيع إلخ: لأن استحقاق الشفعة على الكمال لكل واحد من الشفيعين فلما تعارضا حكم لهما على السوية . (القمر) وعند الشافعي له إلخ والجواب أن الدار المشفوعة علة فاعلية يثبت بها الشفعة، لا علة مادية يتولّد منها المعلول بمنزلة الشجر والحيوان، فقد ثبت في علم الكلام أن تأثير العلة الفاعلية في المعلول ليس بطريق التوليد بإيجاد الله تعالى إياه عقيبه، فلا يكون ترتب استحقاق الشفعة على الملك كترتب الثمر على الشجر والولد على الحيوان ثم الشارع قد جعل مجموع الملك علة للحكم، فينقسم الحكم على أجزاء العلة، وجعل كل جزء من العلة علة الجنسه من المعلول نصب للشرع بالرأي، وهو فاسد. "تلويح". (السنبلي) :أثلاثا فالثلثان لصاحب الثلث والثلث لصاحب السدس. (القمر) مرافق الملك: أي منافع ملك الشفيع فيما يشفع به. (القمر) كذلك فإن شفيعي الجوار مساويان وإن كانا مختلفين في الجوار قلة وكثرة. (القمر) ليتأتى فيه إلخ : فإنه ليس عند الشافعي بالله شفعة الجوار. (القمر) بقوة الأثر : أي سلامة الوصف المؤثر عن المنع والنقض وكونه مؤثرًا في الواقع. (القمر) بقوة الأثر إلخ أي التأثير بأن كان أحد القياسين المؤثرين المتعارضين
أقوى تأثيراً من الآخر، وأما إذا لم يكن أحدهما مؤثراً فلا يكون حجة، فلا تعارض، فلا يترجح. (السنبلي) في الاستحسان أقوى إلخ فإن الاستحسان يقدّم على القياس لقوة فيه وإن كان القياس مؤثرا، ونظيره الخبر، فإنه لما صار حجة بالاتصال برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وجب رجحانه بما يزيد معنى الاتصال من الاشتهار وفقه الراوي
وحسن ضبطه وإتقانه وصلاحه (السنبلي فعلى هذا أي على أن الترجيح يكون بقوة الأثر. (القمر)
Chapter of Analogy
95
Explanation of Aspects of Preponderance
His share: one owns a sixth, another a half, and a third a third. If the owner of half sells, and the other two claim preemption, the sold property is divided between them equally in preemption. According to al-Shafi'i, it is divided into thirds; because preemption is [divided] into thirds; because preemption is a benefit of ownership, so it is divided according to its proportion. The issue is placed in the share even though the rule of adjacency with us is such to allow the disagreement with al-Shafi'i.
[Explanation of Aspects of Preponderance] And what preponderance occurs by, i.e., preponderance of one qiyas over the other, is four: by strength of effect (athar), like istihsan in opposition to qiyas, and the effect in istihsan is stronger, so it is given preponderance over it. If it is said: According to this, it would follow that the more just witness (ashhad) is superior to the just one because his effect is stronger? The answer: We do not concede that justice differs by increase and decrease, for it is expression of restraint from religious prohibitions by cautiousness." etc. (glosses: The sold property etc.: because the entitlement to preemption is complete for each preemptor, when they conflict, judgment is given equally. According to al-Shafi'i, the answer is that the preempted house is an efficient cause by which preemption is established, not a material cause from which the effect is generated like tree and animal. It is established in theology that the effect of an efficient cause on the effect is not by way of generation by Allah creating it after it, so the connection of preemption to ownership is not like the connection of fruit to tree and offspring to animal. The Lawgiver made the totality of ownership the cause for the ruling, so dividing the ruling into parts of the cause, and making each part of the cause a cause for its part of the effect, is setting up a law by opinion, and it is invalid. (Talwih) (al-Sanbali) into thirds: so two-thirds for owner of third and one-third for owner of sixth. (al-Qamar) benefits of ownership: i.e., benefits of the preemptor's ownership in what is preempted. (al-Qamar) similarly, preemptors by adjacency are equal even if they differ in nearness and farness. (al-Qamar) to allow etc.: for according to al-Shafi'i, there is no preemption by adjacency. (al-Qamar) by strength of effect: i.e., soundness of the effective attribute from obstruction and refutation and its being effective in reality. (al-Qamar) by strength of effect etc., i.e., effect that one of the two conflicting effective qiyas is stronger in effect than the other. If neither is effective, it is not a proof, so no conflict, so no preponderance. (al-Sanbali) in istihsan stronger etc., for istihsan is preferred over qiyas due to strength in it even if qiyas is effective. Its analogy is the report, for when it becomes a proof by connection to the Messenger of Allah, it must be given preponderance by what increases the meaning of connection: fame, fiqh of the narrator, good memory, precision, and righteousness. (al-Sanbali) thus according to this, i.e., that preponderance is by strength of effect. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This section, 'Explanation of Aspects of Preponderance' (Wujuh al-Tarjih), outlines the four ways to prefer one qiyas over another when they conflict. The passage continues from the previous discussion on shuf'a, emphasizing the Hanafi stance against al-Shafi'i's proportional division. The main principle stated is that preponderance is achieved by 'strength of effect' (quwwat al-athar), meaning the attribute of the cause is more sound and effective. Istihsan is given as an example: it is preferred over clear qiyas because its effect is stronger, even if the qiyas itself is effective. A potential objection is raised: if strength of effect is the criterion, then a more just witness (ashhad) should be preferred over a just one. The answer refutes this: justice ('adala) does not admit of degrees; it is defined as refraining from prohibited acts. Therefore, one cannot have 'more justice' that would increase the effect. The glosses clarify that preponderance applies only when both qiyas are effective; if one is ineffective, there is no conflict. The analogy to hadith transmission is noted: a hadith becomes proof by its chain, and its strength is increased by fame, the narrator's fiqh, precision, etc. The passage underscores the Hanafi usul principle that tarjih is based on intrinsic quality, not mere quantity.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Preferring one legal evidence over another when they conflict, based on specified criteria.
قوة الأثر (quwwat al-athar): Strength of effect: the attribute that makes a cause more effective, free from defects or counter-evidence.
العدالة (al-'adala): Justice: a quality of a witness or narrator, defined as refraining from religious prohibitions, not differing in degree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary criterion for preponderance between two conflicting qiyas?
A) Number of jurists following each qiyas
B) Strength of effect (quwwat al-athar)
C) Personal preference of the mujtahid
D) The later date of the evidence

Key Takeaway
Preponderance by strength of effect (quwwat al-athar) is the core Hanafi criterion for resolving conflicts between qiyas, requiring that the cause be sound and unaffected by non-gradable personal attributes like justice.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
12 min
Tarjih between Conflicting Analogies: Strength of Effect and Stability
Explains two bases for preferring one qiyas over another: strength of effect (quwwat al-athar) and stability of attribute (quwwat al-thabat).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the two Hanafi criteria for tarjih (strength of effect and stability of attribute) to prefer one qiyas over another, and evaluate the objections raised.

Core Idea
Tarjih between analogies is based on which cause has stronger effect or more stable attachment to the ruling.

When two analogies conflict, how does the Hanafi jurist decide? This passage from Noor al-Anwar presents two key principles: preferring the qiyas whose cause (illa) has a stronger effect, and preferring the qiyas whose attribute (wasf) is more stably attached to the ruling. The lesson illustrates these principles with concrete examples from shuf'a (preemption) and the intention in fasting, and addresses objections.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the problem of conflicting qiyas
Identify that two analogies produce opposite rulings for the same case, requiring a method of preference.
The preemption example shows a concrete conflict between Hanafi and Shafi'i analogies.
2
Understand tarjih by strength of effect
Examine the first criterion: a qiyas whose illa produces a stronger effect is preferred. The example of istihsan over qiyas illustrates this.
The objection regarding justice ('adala) tests this principle.
3
Analyze the 'adala objection and response
The objection claims tarjih by effect would demand preferring a more just witness. The Hanafi response is that 'adala is a single quality, not graded.
This clarifies that strength of effect does not apply to fixed legal qualities.
4
Understand tarjih by stability of attribute
Examine the second criterion: an attribute that is more stable (thabat) – i.e., recurs with the ruling across multiple cases – is preferred. The fasting intention example is analyzed.
Stability is demonstrated by comparing the scope of 'determination' vs 'obligation'.
5
Consolidate the two criteria
Both criteria are methods of tarjih. The passage illustrates that a correct application may lead to no preference if both analogies are equally stable.
The final part notes that if the opponent's analysis is refined, tarjih may not be possible.

بيان وجوه الترجيح
نصيبه، لأحدهم سدسها، وللآخر نصفها، وللثالث ثلثها، فباع صاحب النصف مثلاً وطلب الآخران الشفعة، يكون المبيع بينهما نصفين بالشفعة، وعند الشافعي له يُقضى بالشقص المبيع أثلاثا؛ لأن الشفعة أثلاثا؛ لأن الشفعة من مرافق الملك، فيكون مقسوما على قدره، وإنما وضع كالثمر للفجر الملك المسألة في الشقص وإن كان حكم الجوار عندنا كذلك ليتأتى فيه خلاف الشافعي ليه.
بيان وجوه الترجيح
وما يقع به الترجيح، أي ترجيح أحد القياسين على الآخر أربعة بقوة الأثر كالاستحسان في معارضة القياس والأثر في الاستحسان أقوى، فيترجّح عليه، فإن قيل: فعلى هذا يلزم القياس الجلي أن يكون الشاهد الأعدل راجحا على العادل؛ لأن أثره أقوى؟ أجيب بأنا لا نسلّم أن العدالة تختلف بالزيادة والنقصان فإنها عبارة عن الانزجار عن محظورات الدين بالاحتراز عن الكبائر وعدم الإصرار على الصغائر ، وهو أمر مضبوط لا يتعدّد، وإنما الاختلاف في التقوى.
وبقوة ثباته، أي ثبات الوصف على الحكم المشهود به يكون وصفه ألزم للحكم المتعلّق المتنازع فيه به من وصف القياس الآخر كقولنا في صوم رمضان إنه متعيّن من جانب الله تعالى، فلا يجب التعيين على العبد في النية أولى من قولهم صوم فرض فيجب تعيين النية فيه كصوم القضاء؛ لأن هذا أي وصف الفرضية الذي أورده الشافعي طلبه مخصوص في الصوم، بخلاف التعيين الذي أوردناه فقد تعدّى إلى الودائع والغصوب، وردّ المبيع في البيع الفاسد، أي إذا ردّ الوديعة إلى المالك، والمغصوب إليه، أو ردّ المبيع الفاسد إلى البائع بأيّ جهة كانت يخرج عن العهدة، ولا يشترط تعيين الدفع من حيث كونه وديعة أو غصبًا أو بيعًا فاسدًا؛ لأنه متعيّن لا يحتمل الردّ بجهة أخرى، فيكون ثبات التعيين على حكمه أقوى من ثبات الفرضية على حكمها، وقيل عليه إن هذا إنما يرد لو كان تعليل الخصم لا يتعدد فليس له أنواع متفاوتة بعضها فوق بعض.
وقيل عليه إن هذا يعني لو كان تعليل الشافعي على وجوب تعيين النية بمجرد وصف الفرضية يلزم عليه النقض بالحج وبالزكاة، فإنه يصح بمطلق النية بدون التعيين مع أنهما فرض، وإنما يوجد تعليله في الصوم والصلاة دون غيرهما، وأما إذا كان التعليل بالصوم الفرض فلا يرد النقض؛ لأنه يوجد في جميع أفراده كما في صوم القضاء والنذر والكفارة وفي جميعها يشترط التعيين، فحينئذٍ يكون دليل الخصم أيضًا ألزم في المواد، وأثبت في القوة، فلا يقع الترجيح لقياسنا بمقابلة قياسه.
(القمر) بقوة الأثر : أي سلامة الوصف المؤثر عن المنع والنقض وكونه مؤثرًا في الواقع.

(القمر) من حيث كونه إلخ : أي من حيث إنه دفع وديعة أو دفع مغصوب أو دفع المبيع بالبيع الفاسد.

Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of the aspects of tarjih. His share: for one of them a sixth, for another a half, for the third a third. So if the owner of the half sells, for example, and the other two demand preemption, the sold property is divided between them half and half by preemption. According to al-Shafi'i, it is adjudicated that the sold share is divided into thirds, because preemption is in thirds; because preemption is a conjoined right of ownership, so it is divided according to its measure. And it was posed like fruit for the tree. The issue is about the share even though the ruling of neighborly right according to us is likewise, so that the disagreement with al-Shafi'i becomes possible for him. Explanation of the aspects of tarjih: and that by which tarjih occurs, i.e., preferring one of the two qiyas over the other, is four: by strength of effect, like istihsan in opposing qiyas, and the effect in istihsan is stronger, so it is preferred over it. If it is said: then this would entail that the more just witness should be preferred over the just one, because his effect is stronger? It is answered: we do not concede that justice varies by increase and decrease, for it is an expression of refraining from prohibited matters of religion by avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins, and this is a fixed matter that does not multiply; rather the difference is in taqwa. And by strength of its stability, i.e., the stability of the attribute on the ruling attested to: its attribute becomes more binding to the disputed ruling than the attribute of the other qiyas, like our saying concerning the fast of Ramadan that it is determined from Allah's side, so determination is not obligatory upon the slave in the intention, is more appropriate than their saying: fasting is an obligation, so determination of the intention is obligatory in it like the make-up fast; because this, i.e., the attribute of obligation which al-Shafi'i brought, is specific to fasting, unlike determination which we brought, for it extends to deposits, usurpations, and return of defective sales, i.e., if one returns the deposit to its owner, and the usurped item to its owner, or returns the defective sale to its seller in any manner, he becomes free of liability, and determination of the payment as being a deposit or usurpation or defective sale is not required; because it is determined and does not admit of return by another means. So the stability of determination on its ruling is stronger than the stability of obligation on its ruling. And it was objected: this only applies if the opponent's analysis were not multiple; it has no varying types some above others. And it was objected: this means if al-Shafi'i's analysis for the obligation of determining intention were solely by the attribute of obligation, it would be refuted by the Hajj and the Zakat, for they are valid with absolute intention without determination even though they are obligations; his analysis only occurs in fasting and prayer without others. But if the analysis is by obligatory fasting, then the refutation does not apply because it exists in all its instances like in make-up, vow, and expiation fasting, in all of which determination is required. In that case, the opponent's evidence is also more binding in materials and more stable in strength, so no preference occurs for our qiyas in opposition to his qiyas.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar deals with the principles of tarjih (preference) between conflicting analogies (qiyas) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first clarifies that tarjih can be based on two main factors: (1) the strength of the effect (quwwat al-athar) and (2) the stability of the attribute (quwwat al-thabat) on the ruling. The explanation begins with a concrete example from fiqh: a property co-owned by three partners with different shares (one-sixth, one-half, one-third). When the half-owner sells his share and the other two demand preemption (shuf'a), the Hanafi position holds that the sold share is divided equally between them, whereas al-Shafi'i divides it proportionally to their ownership shares (thirds). The Hanafi view is based on the principle that preemption is attached to the ownership itself—thus after the sale, the remaining partners become equal co-owners of the acquired share. The author then generalizes: tarjih by strength of effect means that one qiyas has a more potent legal cause (illa) that produces a stronger effect, as in the case of istihsan over qiyas. An objection is raised: if effect strength were the measure, then a more just witness would be preferred over a just one. The Hanafi response is that justice ('adala) is a single quality—refraining from major sins and not persisting in minor ones—and does not admit degrees except in taqwa (piety), which is not part of the legal probity required for testimony. The second type of tarjih is by strength of stability: an attribute that is more strongly attached to and recurring with a ruling is preferred. The author illustrates with a Hanafi argument about the fast of Ramadan: since the month is determined by Allah, the slave need not specify the intention—unlike make-up fasts which require specification. The Hanafi attribute here is 'determination' (ta'ayyun), which applies broadly (deposits, usurpations, defective sales) and thus has stronger stability than the opponent's attribute 'obligation' (fardiyya), which is specific only to fasting. The passage ends with a refinement: if the opponent's analysis is properly formulated, it may also have wide applicability, and then no tarjih occurs. The marginal notes by al-Qamar and al-Sunbuli clarify definitions, adding that strength of effect means the description is free from objections and actually effective, and that istihsan's strength comes from its connection to the authoritative texts, similar to the reliability of a hadith transmitter.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjīḥ): Preference of one legal evidence (like qiyas) over another when they conflict
أثر (athar): The effect or impact of a legal cause (illa) in producing a ruling
ثبات (thabāt): The firmness and recurrence of an attribute (wasf) in relation to a ruling
استحسان (istiḥsān): Preferring a stronger evidence (like a text or public interest) over a qiyas
عدالة (ʿadāla): Legal probity of a witness; refraining from major sins and not persisting in minor ones

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, why is the preempted property divided equally between the two preemptors even though their original shares were different?
A) Because preemption is a right attached to ownership, so co-ownership after sale makes them equal
B) Because the larger shareholder should get more
C) Because the seller's share is divided according to the number of preemptors
D) Because the Quran commands equal division

Key Takeaway
Tarjih between conflicting analogies is achieved by preferring the cause with a stronger effect or a more stable attachment to the ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Tarjih by Strength of Attribute's Connection (Thabat al-Wasf) – The Fast of Ramadan Example
Explaining preponderance when one attribute is more inherent to its ruling, using the intention specification debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of thabat al-wasf to compare two analogies and evaluate a Hanafi tarjih argument in a disputed case.

Core Idea
The more stable and comprehensive an attribute's connection to its ruling, the stronger its analogy becomes for preponderance.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar introduces a key Hanafi method for resolving conflicts between analogies: the strength of the attribute's stability (thabat al-wasf) upon its ruling. The debate over whether intention must specify the type of fast in Ramadan provides a vivid illustration. The Hanafi school argues that the attribute of 'determination' (ta'ayyun) is more firmly attached to the ruling than the attribute of 'obligatoriness' (fardiyya) because it applies broadly across many legal contexts. This lesson walks you through the argument and a later scholarly objection, sharpening your skills in usul al-fiqh analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two analogies
Locate the Hanafi and Shafi'i analogies regarding the requirement of specifying intention in the Ramadan fast.
The Hanafi analogy uses deposits, usurpations, and invalid sales as the asl. The Shafi'i analogy uses qada' fasts as the asl.
2
Extract the attribute (wasf) from each analogy
Determine the effective cause (illa) in each analogy. The Hanafi attribute is 'determination' (ta'ayyun); the Shafi'i attribute is 'obligatoriness' (fardiyya).
The text describes the Hanafi attribute as 'muta'ayyin' (specified by Allah) and the Shafi'i attribute as 'fardiyya' (being an obligation).
3
Assess the stability (thabat) of each attribute
Evaluate how broadly the attribute applies across other legal rulings. The Hanafi attribute extends to deposits, usurpations, and invalid sales; the Shafi'i attribute is restricted to fasting.
Broader application indicates stronger thabat because the attribute is more inherent to the ruling.
4
Apply the tarjih rule
The attribute with stronger thabat gives preponderance. Conclude that 'determination' is stronger, so no specification is required in Ramadan fast.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
5
Examine the counter-objection
Read the objection: if the Shafi'i 'illa is narrowed to 'obligatory fast' (sawm al-fard) rather than generic obligatoriness, the Hanafi counterexample may not apply.
This shows that tarjih is not absolute; the opponent can refine the illa to create a stronger analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقوة ثباته، أي ثبات الوصف على الحكم المشهود به يكون وصفه ألزم للحكم المتعلّق المتنازع فيه به من وصف القياس الآخر كقولنا في صوم رمضان إنه متعيّن من جانب الله تعالى، فلا يجب التعيين على العبد في النية أولى من قولهم صوم فرض فيجب تعيين النية فيه كصوم القضاء؛ لأن هذا أي وصف الفرضية الذي أورده الشافعي طلبه مخصوص في الصوم، بخلاف التعيين الذي أوردناه فقد تعدّى إلى الودائع والغصوب، وردّ المبيع في البيع الفاسد، أي إذا ردّ الوديعة إلى المالك، والمغصوب إليه، أو ردّ المبيع الفاسد إلى البائع بأيّ جهة كانت يخرج عن العهدة، ولا يشترط تعيين الدفع من حيث كونه وديعة أو غصبًا أو بيعًا فاسدًا؛ لأنه متعيّن لا يحتمل الردّ بجهة أخرى، فيكون ثبات التعيين على حكمه أقوى من ثبات الفرضية على حكمها، وقيل عليه إن هذا إنما يرد لو كان تعليل الخصم لا يتعدد فليس له أنواع متفاوتة بعضها فوق بعض. (القمر) في التقوى: فإن المتقي من يتقي عن المنهيات، والأتقى من يتقي عن الشبهات والمباحات حذرًا عن الوقوع في المنهيات. (القمر) يكون وصفه: أي وصف أحد القياسين ألزم للحكم إلخ : فإذا كان الوصف زائد لثبات على الحكم وألزم له ازداد قوة. (القمر) مخصوص أي لا يتعدّى إلى الفروض المتعينة الأخرى، فإن التعيين فيها لا يجب بوصف الفرضية.(القمر) بخلاف التعيين إلخ فإن للتعيين تأثيرًا في جميع الفرائض المتعينة حيث لا يشترط التعيين فيها، فإنه قد تعدّى إلخ، والمراد بالتعيين: التعين بطريق إطلاق اسم السبب على المسبب. (القمر) بأي جهة كانت أي سواء علم صاحب الحق به أو لا. (القمر) من حيث كونه إلخ : أي من حيث إنه دفع وديعة أو دفع مغصوب أو دفع المبيع بالبيع الفاسد. (القمر) لأنه : أي لأن المودع والمغصوب والمبيع بالبيع الفاسد. (القمر) :وقيل عليه إلخ يعني لو كان تعليل الشافعي لله على وجوب تعيين النية بمجرد وصف الفرضية يلزم عليه النقض بالحج ،وبالزكاة، فإنه يصح بمطلق النية بدون التعيين مع أنهما فرض، وإنما يوجد تعليله في الصوم والصلاة دون غيرهما، وأما إذا كان التعليل بالصوم الفرض فلا يرد النقض؛ لأنه يوجد في جميع أفراده كما في صوم القضاء والنذر والكفارة وفي جميعها يشترط التعيين، فحينئذٍ يكون دليل الخصم أيضًا ألزم في المواد، وأثبت في القوة، فلا يقع الترجيح لقياسنا بمقابلة قياسه. (السنبلي) إن هذا أي إيرادنا على الشافعية بأولوية قياسنا. (القمر) فلا يناسب مقابلته إيراد مسألة ردّ الوديعة والمغصوب والبيع الفاسد.
And by the strength of its stability, i.e., the stability of the attribute upon the testified ruling, its attribute becomes more binding to the disputed ruling than the attribute of the other analogy, as in our statement regarding the fast of Ramadan: it is specified (muta'ayyin) by Allah, so specification (ta'yin) is not obligatory upon the servant in intention, which is more appropriate than their statement: 'Fasting is an obligation (fard), so specification of intention is obligatory in it, as in the fast of qada'. Because this attribute of obligatoriness (fardiyyah) which al-Shafi'i advanced is specific to fasting, unlike the attribute of specification which we advanced, for it extends to deposits, usurped goods, and the return of a defective sale in an invalid sale. That is, when one returns a deposit to its owner, a usurped item to its owner, or returns an invalid sale item to the seller by any means, one is discharged of responsibility, and specification of the payment is not required in terms of being a deposit, a usurpation, or an invalid sale, because it is specified (muta'ayyin) and does not admit return by another means. Thus, the stability of specification upon its ruling is stronger than the stability of obligatoriness upon its ruling. And it was objected that this only applies if the opponent's 'illa is not varied, having no types some above others. (al-Qamar) Regarding taqwa: the muttaqi is one who avoids prohibitions, and the atqa is one who avoids ambiguities and permissible things out of caution against falling into prohibitions. (al-Qamar) 'Its attribute becomes more binding': i.e., the attribute of one of the two analogies is more binding to the ruling, so when the attribute is more stable upon the ruling and more binding, it increases in strength. (al-Qamar) 'Specific': i.e., it does not extend to other specified obligations (furuḍ muta'ayyina), for specification is not obligatory in them by virtue of obligatoriness. (al-Qamar) 'Unlike specification': specification has effect in all specified obligations where specification is required, and it has extended, etc. The meaning of specification is the specification by way of applying the name of the cause to the effect. (al-Qamar) 'By any means': whether the owner knows of it or not. (al-Qamar) 'In terms of being': i.e., whether it is a deposit, a usurpation, or an invalid sale. (al-Qamar) 'Because': because the depositor, the usurped owner, and the seller in an invalid sale. (al-Qamar) 'And it was objected': meaning that if al-Shafi'i's 'illa for the obligation of specifying intention is purely the attribute of obligatoriness, then the objection (naqḍ) would apply from Hajj and Zakat, for they are valid with absolute intention without specification despite being obligations, while his 'illa is only found in fasting and prayer. But if the 'illa is 'obligatory fast', then the objection does not apply because it exists in all its instances, as in qada' fast, vow fast, and expiation fast, which all require specification. Then the opponent's proof is also more binding in the matters and more firmly established, so no preponderance occurs for our analogy over his. (al-Sunbuli) This (our objection against the Shafi'is regarding the superiority of our analogy) is not appropriate to be countered with the issue of returning deposits, usurped goods, and invalid sales.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage explains a mode of tarjih (preponderance) between two analogies (qiyas) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the strength of the attribute's connection to its ruling. The author uses the example of intention (niyya) in fasting. The Hanafi position is that for the month of Ramadan, the intention does not need to specify the type of fast because the fast is already determined (muta'ayyin) by Allah's command. The Shafi'i counter argues that since fasting is a fard (obligation), it requires specification of intention, like in qada' fasts. The Hanafi response shows that the attribute of 'being determined' (ta'ayyun) is more strongly attached to the ruling (discharge from responsibility) than the attribute of 'obligatoriness' (fardiyya). This is because the attribute of determination applies beyond fasting to deposits, usurpations, and invalid sales—where no specification is needed to be discharged from liability. The Shafi'i's attribute (obligatoriness) is specific to fasting and does not extend to other obligations like Hajj or Zakat where specification is not required. A later gloss (al-Sunbuli) notes a potential objection: if the Shafi'i's 'illa is narrowed to 'obligatory fast' (sawm al-fard), then the Hanafi counterexample would not apply, and the preponderance might not hold, but the text leaves this as a point of debate.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification in intention; specifying the type of act (e.g., which fast) in one's intention.
ثبات الوصف (thabat al-wasf): The stability or firmness of an attribute's connection to its legal ruling.
فرضية (fardiyya): The quality of being an obligation (fard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, why is the intention for the Ramadan fast not required to specify the type of fast?
A) Because Ramadan is a supererogatory fast.
B) Because the attribute of determination (ta'ayyun) is stronger and extends to other cases.
C) Because the fast is not obligatory.
D) Because the Shafi'i school does not require specification.

Key Takeaway
Thabat al-wasf is a Hanafi method for preferring one analogy over another; a more stable and encompassing attribute wins, but the opponent's 'illa can be narrowed to reduce that stability.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Tarjih by Multiplicity of Principles and Inverse Relationship
Explaining two tarjih methods: multiplicity of principles and inverse relationship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of tarjih by multiplicity of principles and inverse relationship to compare analogies and identify the preponderant one.

Core Idea
More analogous cases strengthen a qiyas; an 'illa must be both coextensive and inversely coextensive.

In Hanafi usul, when two analogies conflict, we need a method to give preponderance (tarjih). This passage introduces two such methods: one based on the number of supporting original cases (usul), and another based on the logical property of the effective cause ('illa) being absent when the ruling is absent. We will unpack each with the classic example of wiping the head during wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two tarjih methods
Read the passage and extract the two modes of tarjih: (1) multiplicity of principles (kathrat al-usul), (2) inverse relationship (al-'adam 'ind al-'adam / al-'aks).
The phrase 'بكثرة أصوله' introduces the first; 'وبالعدم عند العدم' introduces the second.
2
Understand multiplicity of principles
Digest that kathrat al-usul means one analogy is supported by more original cases (usul) than another. It is NOT about multiplying analogical proofs or similarities, which are invalid. The strength comes from the number of analogues.
The passage explicitly says 'ولا يكون هذا من قبيل كثرة الأدلة القياسية، أو كثرة أوجه الشبه لشيء، فإن هذه كلها فاسدة'.
3
Apply to the wiping example
Hanafis argue wiping the head (mash) should not be repeated thrice because it is like wiping the khuff, jabira, and tayammum – all are mash actions not requiring repetition. These multiple usul support the Hanafi analogy. The Shafi'i analogy (like ghusl, a rukn) has only one principle, making the Hanafi analogy stronger by kathrat al-usul.
Note the contrast: Hanafi has three usul, Shafi'i one.
4
Understand inverse relationship
The second method: an attribute ('illa) that exists when the ruling exists and is absent when the ruling is absent (coextensive and inversely coextensive) is superior to one that lacks inverse coextensiveness. This is al-'aks.
The passage states: 'إذا كان وصف يطرد وينعكس كان أولى من وصف لا ينعكس'.
5
Address the objection
The gloss notes that this does not increase the standard categories of tarjih beyond four, meaning these methods are already subsumed under established categories.
'فلا يرد أنه يلزم أن يكون أقسام الترجيح زائدا على الأربعة' – the objection is answered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبكثرة أصوله أي إذا شهد لقياس واحد أصل واحد ولقياس أخر أصلان، أو أصول أحد القياسين يترجح هذا على الأول، والمراد بالأصل المقيس عليه، ولا يكون هذا من قبيل كثرة الأدلة القياسية، أو كثرة أوجه الشبه لشيء، فإن هذه كلها فاسدة، وكثرة الأصول صحيحة كقولنا في مسح الرأس: إنه مسح فلا يُسنّ تثليثه، فإن أصله مسح الخف والجبيرة والتيمم، بخلاف قول الشافعي له: إنه ركن فيسن تثليثه فإنه لا أصل له إلا الغسل وبالعدم عند العدم، وهو العكس أي إذا كان وصف يطرد وينعكس كان أولى من وصف لا ينعكس. فلا يرد أنه يلزم أن يكون أقسام الترجيح زائدا على الأربعة. (المحشي)
And by the multiplicity of its principles: i.e., if one analogy is supported by one principle (asl) and another analogy is supported by two (or more) principles, the one with more principles is given preponderance. The 'principle' here means the analogue (maqis 'alayh). This is not a case of multiplicity of analogical proofs (adilla qiyasiyya) or multiplicity of points of similarity, for these are invalid. Rather, multiplicity of principles is valid, as in our statement about wiping the head: it is wiping (mash), so it is not sunna to repeat it thrice; its principle is the wiping of the khuff, the splint (jabira), and tayammum. In contrast, the Shafi'i statement that it is a pillar (rukn) so it is sunna to repeat it thrice has no principle except washing (ghusl). And by [the attribute's] absence at [the ruling's] absence: i.e., the inverse (al-'aks), meaning if an attribute exists when the ruling exists and is absent when the ruling is absent (i.e., it is coextensive and inversely coextensive), it is superior to an attribute that is not inversely coextensive. Then it cannot be objected that this would make the categories of tarjih exceed four. (al-Mahshi)
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents two further modes of tarjih in Hanafi usul. First, tarjih by multiplicity of principles (kathrat al-usul): when one analogy is supported by multiple analogous cases (usul), it is stronger than another analogy with fewer. This is distinct from multiplying the number of analogical proofs or points of similarity, which are invalid. An example: Hanafis say that wiping the head (mash) during wudu should not be repeated thrice because the basic ruling for wiping actions (like wiping the khuff, the splint, and tayammum) does not require repetition. The Shafi'i say it is a rukn, so it should be repeated like washing (ghusl). But the Shafi'i have only one principle (washing), whereas Hanafis have multiple (khuff, jabira, tayammum), so Hanafi analogy is stronger. Second, tarjih by inverse relationship (al-'adam 'ind al-'adam): if the attribute is present when the ruling is present (integration) and absent when the ruling is absent (inverse), it is superior to an attribute that does not exhibit this inverse property. This is about the coextensiveness of the 'illa. The gloss (al-Mahshi) notes that this does not increase the standard categories of tarjih beyond four.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): The original case (maqis 'alayh) used as the basis for analogy; a primary or analogous case.
العكس (al-'aks): The inverse condition: when the ruling is absent in the absence of the attribute.
كثرة الأصول (kathrat al-usul): Multiplicity of the analogues supporting a single analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the Hanafi analogy regarding the number of times to wipe the head during wudu considered stronger than the Shafi'i analogy?
A) Because Hanafis use more analogical proofs.
B) Because the Hanafi analogy is supported by multiple analogous cases (wiping khuff, jabira, tayammum).
C) Because the Shafi'i do not have any analogy.
D) Because wiping the head is not a rukn.

Key Takeaway
The strength of an analogy is increased by having more original cases (usul) supporting it, and a valid 'illa must exhibit both coextensiveness and inverse coextensiveness.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Tarjīḥ by Kathrat al-Uṣūl (Multiplicity of Origins) in Qiyas
Explains preponderance by multiplicity of origins in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of tarjīḥ by kathrat al-uṣūl to identify which qiyas argument is preponderant and evaluate its difference from invalid types of tarjīḥ.

Core Idea
A qiyas supported by multiple origins is stronger than one with a single origin—but only if the ʿilla is unified.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not all qiyas arguments are equal. When two analogies conflict, one may be given preponderance (tarjīḥ) over the other. Among the valid bases for tarjīḥ is kathrat al-uṣūl—multiplicity of original cases (aṣl) on which the analogy rests. This lesson unpacks this principle, distinguishes it from invalid forms like multiplicity of evidences, and applies it to the classical dispute on repeating the wiping of the head in wuḍūʾ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting qiyas arguments
Clearly state the Hanafi and Shafiʿi positions on whether wiping the head (masḥ al-ra's) should be repeated thrice. The Hanafi say once suffices; Shafiʿi say thrice is sunnah.
The ʿilla (effective cause) for each is different: 'masḥ' vs 'rukn'.
2
Determine the ʿilla for each argument
The Hanafi ʿilla is 'masḥ' (wiping) – an act that, by its nature, is not repeated. The Shafiʿi ʿilla is 'rukn' (pillar) – like washing the face, which is repeated thrice.
The choice of ʿilla determines the number of origins.
3
Count the origins supporting each ʿilla
Hanafi: three origins (wiping the khuff, the splint, and tayammum) all confirm that wiping is not repeated. Shafiʿi: only one origin (washing the face).
Origins are the analogous bases (maqīs ʿalayhi) that share the same ʿilla.
4
Apply the tarjīḥ rule
According to Hanafi usul, multiplicity of origins strengthens the ʿilla, making the Hanafi argument preponderant over the Shafiʿi.
This is valid only when the ʿilla is one; multiple origins confirm the same ʿilla.
5
Distinguish from invalid forms
This is not multiplicity of evidences (each origin is not a separate dalīl) nor multiplicity of aspects of similarity (which would involve multiple descriptions on a single origin).
The commentator explicitly rejects those forms as invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبكثرة أصوله أي إذا شهد لقياس واحد أصل واحد ولقياس أخر أصلان، أو أصول أحد القياسين يترجح هذا على الأول، والمراد بالأصل المقيس عليه، ولا يكون هذا من قبيل كثرة الأدلة القياسية، أو كثرة أوجه الشبه لشيء، فإن هذه كلها فاسدة، وكثرة الأصول صحيحة كقولنا في مسح الرأس: إنه مسح فلا يُسنّ تثليثه، فإن أصله مسح الخف والجبيرة والتيمم، بخلاف قول الشافعي له: إنه ركن فيسن تثليثه فإنه لا أصل له إلا الغسل فلا يناسب إلخ لأن المقصود بيان أن علتنا أثبت وألزم من علة الخصم ومتى كان علة الخصم الصوم الفرض لا يحصل هذا المقصود ببيان أن علتنا وهو التعيين أثبت وألزم من مطلق الفرضية كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) لأنه أيضا يتعدى إلى صوم القضاء وصوم النذر وصوم وصوم الكفارة. (المحشي) بالأصل: لا الدليل ليلزم الترجيح بكثرة الأدلة. (المحشي) صحيح؛ ولا يكون إلخ لما زعم بعض أصحابنا وبعض أصحاب الشافعي له أن الترجيح بكثرة الأصول غير لأن هذا الترجيح بمنزلة الترجيح بكثرة العلة، فإن شهادة كل أصل بمنزلة علة على حدة، وهو لا يعتبر، دَفَعَ الشارح به زعمهم بقوله : ولا يكون هذا من قبيل كثرة الأدلة القياسية، فإنه إنما يكون كذلك إذا كان لكل قياس علة على حدة، وفيما نحن فيه القياس واحد والمعنى المؤثر أي العلة واحد، إلا أن الأصول كثيرة، فيحصل بكثرتها زيادة قوة في نفس الوصف فإن في كثرة الأصول زيادة لزوم الحكم معه. (القمر) كثرة الأدلة إلخ فإن الدليل في عدم التثليث هو المسح، وهو يوجد في مواضع كثيرة، ولا يُسنّ تثليثه، وتلك المواضع ليست أدلة لعدم التثليث، بل أصول له بمعنى أنها نظائر له حتى يلزم علينا الترجيح بكثرة الأدلة فافهم فلا يرد على هذا أن الترجيح بكثرة المقيس عليه دالة على الحكم، فيكون الترجيح بكثرة الأدلة، وهو باطل.(السنبلي) أو كثرة أوجه إلخ أي لا يكون هذا من قبيل كثرة أوجه الشبه، فإنه ترجيح بأوصاف كثيرة مع كون المقيس عليه واحدا، وههنا قد تعدّد المقيس عليه. (القمر) فإن هذه كلها أي كثرة الأدلة القياسية وكثرة أوجه الشبهة. (القمر) صحيحة فإن كثرة الأصول تفيد قوة التأثير. (القمر) إلا الغسل وهذا أصل واحد، ولكثير ترجيح على الواحد (القمر)
And by multiplicity of its origins: i.e., if one analogy has one origin and another analogy has two origins or more, the one with more origins is preponderant over the first. What is meant by 'origin' is the analogous basis. And this is not from the category of multiplicity of analogical evidences or multiplicity of aspects of similarity for something, for all of these are invalid. Multiplicity of origins is valid, like our saying regarding wiping the head: it is wiping so its triple repetition is not sunnah, for its origins are wiping the khuff, the splint, and tayammum, unlike the statement of al-Shafi'i: it is a pillar so its triple repetition is sunnah, for it has no origin except washing. So it is not appropriate etc., because the purpose is to show that our cause is more established and binding than the opponent's cause, and whenever the opponent's cause is the fast of Ramadan, this purpose is not achieved by showing that our cause—specification—is more established and binding than absolute obligation. Thus said Ibn al-Malak. (al-Qamar) because it also extends to make-up fasts, vowed fasts, and expiatory fasts. (al-Muhashshi) By 'origin' is meant not evidence, lest preponderance by multiplicity of evidences be required. (al-Muhashshi) Correct. And it is not, etc., because some of our companions and some of al-Shafi'i's companions claimed that preponderance by multiplicity of origins is not valid because this preponderance is like preponderance by multiplicity of causes, for the testimony of each origin is like a separate cause, and that is not considered. The commentator refuted their claim by saying: This is not from the category of multiplicity of analogical evidences, for it is only so if each analogy has a separate cause, whereas here the analogy is one and the effective meaning—the cause—is one, except that the origins are many, so by their multiplicity an increased strength in the very description occurs, for in multiplicity of origins there is an increased binding of the ruling with it. (al-Qamar) Multiplicity of evidences etc.: the evidence for non-tripling is wiping, which exists in many places, and its tripling is not sunnah, and those places are not evidences for non-tripling, but origins in the sense that they are its analogues, so that preponderance by multiplicity of evidences does not necessarily apply to us—understand. So it is not refuted that preponderance by multiplicity of the analogous basis indicates the ruling, thus it would be preponderance by multiplicity of evidences, which is invalid. (al-Sanbali) Or multiplicity of aspects, etc.: i.e., this is not from the category of multiplicity of aspects of similarity, for it is preponderance by many descriptions while the analogous basis is one, whereas here the analogous basis is multiple. (al-Qamar) These all—i.e., multiplicity of analogical evidences and multiplicity of aspects of similarity—(al-Qamar) are valid, for multiplicity of origins yields strength of effect. (al-Qamar) Except washing, and this is one origin, and multiple things have preponderance over one (al-Qamar).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage discusses one of the valid types of tarjīḥ (preponderance) in qiyas: tarjīḥ by kathrat al-uṣūl (multiplicity of origins). The author clarifies that when one analogy has more than one original case (aṣl) on which it is based, it is preponderant over another analogy with only one origin. This is not to be confused with multiplicity of analogical evidences (adilla qiyāsiyya) or multiplicity of aspects of similarity (wujūh al-shabah), which are invalid forms of tarjīḥ. The example given is wiping the head (masḥ al-raʾs) in wuḍūʾ. The Hanafi position is that wiping the head is 'masḥ' (wiping), which is a category of action that does not require repetition (tathlīth) as sunnah. This is supported by multiple origins: wiping the khuff, wiping the splint (jabīra), and tayammun—all of which are likewise wiping and not repeated. In contrast, al-Shafiʿī argues it is a rukn (pillar) like washing the face, so it should be thrice. The Hanafīs respond that the opponent has only one origin (ghusl) for his claim, while we have multiple origins, thus our position is stronger. The passage also rebuts objections that this would constitute preponderance by multiplicity of evidences. The key is that the ʿilla (effective cause) is one—'masḥ'—but multiple origins confirm the same ʿilla, strengthening its effect. This is a valid form of tarjīḥ.

Key Terms
كثرة الأصول (kathrat al-uṣūl): Multiplicity of original cases (aṣl) on which an analogy is based.
أصل (aṣl): The original case upon which an analogy is built (maqīs ʿalayhi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi argument for not repeating wiping the head, how many origins support the ʿilla of 'masḥ'?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Multiplicity of origins (kathrat al-uṣūl) strengthens the ʿilla in qiyas and is a valid basis for tarjīḥ in Hanafi usul, provided the ʿilla remains one.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Tarjīḥ by al-ʿAdam ʿinda al-ʿAdam: The Condition of Ṭard and ʿAks
Explains preponderance by absence of ruling when description is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that an ʿilla with both ṭard and ʿaks is preponderant over one with only ṭard, using the example of wiping the head.

Core Idea
A valid ʿilla must both coincide with the ruling (ṭard) and vanish with it (ʿaks).

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the strength of an effective cause (ʿilla) is measured not only by its coextensiveness with the ruling (ṭard) but also by its converse (ʿaks): when the description is absent, the ruling must also be absent. This lesson unpacks the rule of tarjīḥ by absence at absence (al-ʿadam ʿinda al-ʿadam) through the classic Hanafi-Shafiʿi debate on wiping the head (masḥ). You will see why the Hanafi description of 'masḥ' is considered more deserving than the Shafiʿi description of 'rukn'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule of tarjīḥ
Spot the statement: 'And by absence at absence, which is the converse: i.e., if a description is coextensive and converse, it is more deserving than a description that is coextensive but not converse.' Understand that this is a rule for preferring one ʿilla over another.
This is a principle of tarjīḥ, not a definition of ʿilla itself.
2
Define ṭard and ʿaks
Ṭard (coextensiveness) means the ruling exists whenever the description exists. ʿAks (converse) means the ruling is absent whenever the description is absent. Note that the text uses 'al-ʿadam ʿinda al-ʿadam' to express ʿaks.
Think of logical contrapositive: if description → ruling, then no ruling → no description.
3
Apply to the Hanafi ʿilla for masḥ
The Hanafi ʿilla for wiping the head is 'it is wiping (masḥ)'. Since it is wiping, repetition is not sunnah (ṭard: when masḥ exists, no repetition). Conversely, when it is not wiping (e.g., washing the face), repetition is sunnah (ʿaks: when masḥ absent, repetition present).
This shows the ʿilla of 'masḥ' satisfies both conditions.
4
Compare with the Shafiʿi ʿilla of rukn
The Shafiʿi ʿilla is 'it is a pillar (rukn)'. When it is a pillar, repetition is sunnah (ṭard holds). But when it is not a pillar (e.g., rinsing the mouth), repetition is still sunnah – so the ʿaks fails because absence of the description does not lead to absence of the ruling.
The Shafiʿi ʿilla lacks ʿaks, making it weaker.
5
Recognize the logical necessity
The marginal notes clarify that the converse (ʿaks) is actually the contrapositive of the original statement. For the Hanafi example, 'whatever is not wiping, its repetition is sunnah' is the contrapositive of 'wiping’s repetition is not sunnah'. This logical equivalence ensures the ʿilla is sound.
The text uses 'lāzim al-ʿaks' (necessary concomitant of the converse).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالعدم عند العدم، وهو العكس أي إذا كان وصف يطرد وينعكس كان أولى من وصف يطرد ولا ينعكس فالاطراد حينئذٍ هو الوجود عند الوجود فقط، والانعكاس هو العدم عند العدم، مثل قولنا في مسح الرأس : إنه مسح فلا يُسَنّ تكراره، فإنه ينعكس إلى قولنا: ما لا يكون مسحا، فيُسنّ تكراره كغسل الوجه ونحوه بخلاف قول الشافعي له: إنه ركن، فيُسنّ تكراره فإنه لا ينعكس إلى قوله ما ليس بركن لا يُسنّ تكراره، فإن المضمضة والاستنشاق ليس بركن ومع ذلك يُسنّ تكراره. هو الوجود أي وجود الحكم عند وجود الوصف. (القمر) هو العدم أي عدم الحكم عند عدم الوصف. (القمر) فإنه ينعكس: أي بعكس النقيض إلى قولنا: ما لا يكون مسحا إلخ، ثم اعلم أن هذا لازم للعكس، والعكس ما يُسنّ تكراره لا يكون مسحًا. (القمر) فإنه لا ينعكس إلخ : فلم يوجد العدم عند العدم. (القمر) ما ليس بركن إلى هذا لازم العكس والعكس ما لا يُسنّ تكراره ليس بركن (القمر)
And by absence at absence, which is the converse: i.e., if a description is coextensive and converse, it is more deserving than a description that is coextensive but not converse. Coextensiveness then is the existence (of the ruling) only at existence of the description, and converse is the absence at absence. For example, our saying regarding wiping the head: it is wiping so its repetition is not sunnah, for it converts to our saying: whatever is not wiping, its repetition is sunnah, like washing the face and similar. Unlike the statement of al-Shafi'i: it is a pillar so its repetition is sunnah, for it does not convert to his saying: whatever is not a pillar, its repetition is not sunnah, for rinsing the mouth and snuffing water are not pillars yet their repetition is sunnah. It is existence: i.e., existence of the ruling at existence of the description. (al-Qamar) It is absence: i.e., absence of the ruling at absence of the description. (al-Qamar) For it converts: i.e., by contrapositive to our saying: whatever is not wiping, etc. Then know that this is a necessary concomitant of the converse, and the converse is: whatever is repeated in sunnah is not wiping. (al-Qamar) For it does not convert, etc.: so absence at absence is not found. (al-Qamar) Whatever is not a pillar: this is a necessary concomitant of the converse, and the converse is: whatever repetition is not sunnah is not a pillar (al-Qamar).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage introduces another valid type of tarjīḥ: when a description is both coextensive (ṭard) and converse (ʿaks) with the ruling, it is stronger than a description that is only coextensive. Coextensiveness means that whenever the description is present, the ruling is present. Converse means that whenever the description is absent, the ruling is absent. This is the ideal condition for an effective cause (ʿilla). The example again uses wiping the head. The Hanafi ʿilla of 'masḥ' is both coextensive (wherever there is masḥ, there is no repetition) and converse (wherever there is no masḥ—like washing the face—there is repetition). In contrast, the Shafiʿi ʿilla of 'rukn' is only coextensive: if it is a rukn, repetition is sunnah, but the absence of rukn does not necessarily mean no repetition (e.g., rinsing the mouth is not rukn but repetition is sunnah). Thus the Hanafi description is more deserving of being the cause. The marginal notes clarify that 'converse' here refers to the contrapositive logic: 'not masḥ implies repetition' is logically equivalent to the original statement's converse in this context.

Key Terms
طرد (ṭard): Coextensiveness: the ruling is present whenever the description is present.
عكس (ʿaks): Converse: the ruling is absent whenever the description is absent.
ترجيح (tarjīḥ): Preponderance: the process of preferring one evidence or cause over another when both seem applicable.
علة (ʿilla): Effective cause: the attribute that is taken as the basis for extending a ruling via qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi ʿilla of 'masḥ' for wiping the head have tarjīḥ over the Shafiʿi ʿilla of 'rukn'?
A) It is coextensive only
B) It is both coextensive and converse
C) It has more origins
D) It is based on the Quran

Key Takeaway
A description that is both coextensive (ṭard) and converse (ʿaks) with the ruling is preponderant over one that is only coextensive, as demonstrated by the Hanafi ʿilla of masḥ compared to the Shafiʿi ʿilla of rukn.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

8 min
Conflict of Two Preponderances: Essence Over State
States a usul rule of tarjīḥ hierarchy with a furūʿ application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of taʿāruḍ al-tarjīḥayn by prioritizing preponderance in essence over preponderance in state in a furūʿ case.

Core Idea
When two tarjīḥs conflict, the preponderance in the essence prevails over that in a state.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar explains a critical usul principle: when two forms of preponderance (tarjīḥ) conflict, which one takes priority? The author clarifies that preponderance in the essence (dhāt) outweighs preponderance in a state (ḥāl). This principle is then applied to a concrete fiqh issue: a usurped sheep that is cooked. Through this example, you will see how usul rules directly shape substantive rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
Recognize that the passage establishes a hierarchy between two types of tarjīḥ: preponderance in essence (dhāt) and preponderance in state (ḥāl).
2
Understand the Rationale
Because the state (ḥāl) is subordinate to the essence (dhāt), the derivative cannot overcome the original. The state is qāʾima bi-dhāt (established by the essence).
This is a key Hanafi usul maxim.
3
Examine the Furūʿ
Apply the rule to the case of a usurped sheep: cooking transforms the property, so the owner's right is cut off from the specific object (ʿayn) and transferred to value (qīma).
The cooking is a state that overrides the original essence? Wait, the ruling is that the owner cannot take back the cooked meat.
4
Contrast with Slaughter Only
If the usurper only slaughters without cooking, the owner retains a choice to take the carcass with compensation or claim value. This shows that without full transformation, the essence (the original right) still has some effect.
The distinction hinges on whether the act fundamentally changes the property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أراد أن يبين حكم تعارض الترجيحين، فقال: بيان حكم تعارض الترجيحين] وإذا تعارض ضربا ترجيح كما تعارض أصل القياسين كان الرجحان في الذات أحق منه في الحال أي من الرجحان الحاصل في الحال؛ لأن الحال قائمة بالذات تابعة له في الوجود، ولا ظهور للتابع في مقابلة المتبوع في الوصف أي الوصف فينقطع حق المالك بالطبخ والشي، تفريع على القاعدة المذكورة، وذلك بأنه إذا غصب رجل شاة رجل، ثم ذبحها وطبخها وشوّاها، فإنه ينقطع عندنا حق المالك عن الشاة المطبوخة والمشوية هو الوجود أي وجود الحكم عند وجود الوصف. (القمر) هو العدم أي عدم الحكم عند عدم الوصف. (القمر) فإنه ينعكس: أي بعكس النقيض إلى قولنا: ما لا يكون مسحا إلخ، ثم اعلم أن هذا لازم للعكس، والعكس ما يُسنّ تكراره لا يكون مسحًا. (القمر) فإنه لا ينعكس إلخ : فلم يوجد العدم عند العدم. (القمر) ما ليس بركن إلى هذا لازم العكس والعكس ما لا يُسنّ تكراره ليس بركن (القمر) ولا ظهور إلخ فلو اعتبرنا للحال التابعة الذات فيلزم نسخ الأصل أي الذات بالتبع أي الحال، وهو غير معقول. (القمر) فينقطع إلى أي من العين إلى القيمة. (القمر) وذلك تسمى هذه المسألة مسألة انقطاع حق المالك من العين إلى القيمة. (المحشي) وطبخها إنما قيد بهذا؛ لأنه لو ذبح الغاصب الشاة ولم يطبخ ولم يشوها فقد استهلكها من وجه لكنه لم يعارضه فعل الغاصب؛ لأن فعله ليس بمتقوم، فحينئذٍ لم يبطل حتى المالك، لكن المالك مخير إن شاء نظر إلى جهة الهلاك فيضمن الغاصب القيمة، وإن شاء لاحظ إلى جهة قيام المال، فيأخذ الشاة ويضمن الغاصب النقصان كذا قيل. (القمر)
Then he intended to explain the ruling on conflict of two preponderances, so he said: [Explanation of the ruling on conflict of two preponderances] And if two types of preponderance conflict, just as the original two analogies conflict, then preponderance in essence is more deserving than preponderance in state—i.e., than the preponderance that occurs in the state—because the state is established by the essence, subservient to it in existence, and there is no manifestation for the subservient in the presence of the dominant. In the description—i.e., the description—so the right of the owner is cut off by cooking and roasting, as a branch from the mentioned rule. That is, if a man usurps another man's sheep, then slaughters it, cooks it, and roasts it, then the right of the owner is cut off, according to us, from the cooked and roasted sheep. It is existence: i.e., existence of the ruling at existence of the description. (al-Qamar) It is absence: i.e., absence of the ruling at absence of the description. (al-Qamar) For it converts: i.e., by contrapositive to our saying: whatever is not wiping, etc. Then know that this is a necessary concomitant of the converse, and the converse is: whatever repetition is sunnah is not wiping. (al-Qamar) For it does not convert, etc.: so absence at absence is not found. (al-Qamar) Whatever is not a pillar: this is a necessary concomitant of the converse, and the converse is: whatever repetition is not sunnah is not a pillar (al-Qamar) And there is no manifestation, etc.: for if we consider the subservient state alongside the essence, then abrogation of the original—i.e., the essence by the subservient—would be required, i.e., the state, and that is unfathomable. (al-Qamar) So it is cut off to: i.e., from the specific object to the value. (al-Qamar) And that: this issue is called the issue of cutting off the right of the owner from the specific object to the value. (al-Muhashshi) And cooking it: he specified this only because if the usurper slaughtered the sheep but did not cook or roast it, then he has consumed it in one sense, but the usurper's act does not counter it, because his act is not financially valuable. Therefore, the right of the owner is not voided until the owner, but the owner has the choice: if he wishes, he looks at the aspect of destruction and the usurper guarantees the value; and if he wishes, he looks at the aspect of the property's existence, and he takes the sheep and the usurper guarantees the diminution. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage first establishes a general rule: when two types of tarjīḥ conflict, preponderance in the essence (dhāt) is given priority over preponderance in a state (ḥāl). This is because the state is derivative and subordinate to the essence; the derivative cannot overcome the original. Then a practical branch (furūʿ) is given from the Hanafi fiqh: if a usurper (ghāṣib) takes someone's sheep, slaughters it, cooks it, and roasts it, the owner's right is cut off from the specific object (ʿayn) and changes to a right to the value (qīma). This is based on the rule that the description (cooking) changes the essence of the property. If the usurper only slaughters without cooking, the owner still has a choice to take the carcass with compensation for the loss or to claim the value. The marginal notes clarify the logic of tarjīḥ and the fiqh details, emphasizing that the owner's right is not voided by the usurper's act alone; the transformation of the property by cooking is the key. This illustrates the broader usul principle that the essence (the property) is more fundamental than the state (the act of cooking), and the preponderance in essence (the original right) is more deserving than the state (the transformed object).

Key Terms
تعارض الترجيحين (taʿāruḍ al-tarjīḥayn): Conflict between two types of preponderance in analogical reasoning.
انقطاع حق المالك (inqiṭāʿ ḥaqq al-mālik): Cutting off the owner's right from the specific object to the value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of the usurped sheep, why does the owner's right transfer from the specific object to the value?
A) Because slaughter is always destructive
B) Because cooking transforms the item, making restoration impossible
C) Because the usurper owns the item after cooking
D) Because the owner abandoned his right

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that preponderance in essence outweighs preponderance in state directly determines that an owner's right transfers to value when a usurped property is fundamentally transformed.
